O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	O you, very dear sons, I have finished this book which is the end of the science of medicine, assembled from its teachings and pronouncements.
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	And it came to pass that I realized I must accompany this treatise, which is a part of the work of hands, namely surgery.</start_of_turn>
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	And because the work of hands is fraught in our region and is strange to all, if the science is lost and forgotten, and nothing remains of it except for the small descriptions in the books of the ancients which the hands have performed.</start_of_turn
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	And from this arises the error and the emptiness, and are closed the understandings and is displaced the science.</start_of_turn
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation; et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation; et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	Or it seems to me that I shall make it live altogether the order of this physician according to the way of exposure and declaration and of the abbreviation; and I shall join together the forms of the instruments of cautery, and of other instruments of the work with the arrangement of the declaration and preparation of it, as it is necessary.</start_of_turn>
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	And it is necessary that he who enters this field should be skilled in the science of anatomy, as Galen says, until he has grasped the judgment of limbs, and the forms and the joints and the separations of things, and has knowledge of bones and nerves and muscles and their number, and the structure and the veins moving and resting, and their issue.</start_of_turn>
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc; et meismement en l’art de main.	And thus Hippocrates teaches us that with the hand one must not touch, but must work with the work; and in the art of healing.
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes; ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	We are told in the beginning of this book that he who is not skilled in the things that are before him, if he dares to handle them without caution and respect, will often cause more harm than good; as I have often seen happen in this science, when people abandon both science and sense.
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa .i. apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col; por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	For I have seen a madman who, when he has incised a scrophule or the neck of a woman, has also cut the arteries of the neck; and so much blood has flowed out that the woman has died between his hands.
Et vis .i. autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans; si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens .iij. jors.	And thus another marvel which treats a stone of a bladder stone, and the stone was large; if it took away with it a piece of the bladder, and remained in the body for two days.
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	And thus I have already been called to treat it, and I saw the disposition of the patient and the greatness of the stone, and if it were cut out it would surely die.</start_of_turn>
Et vis .i. autre mire qui prist en cure .i. duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie; et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi .i. termine; et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie; et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	And thus another marvel which treats a limb broken in our land which had a wound; and with the fracture it had a wound; and the physicians of this land were unable to rejoin the fracture above the wound as these things are often done by strong bands, and did not leave the wound open, and left it until it was finished; and they commanded that it should not be moved; and when the limb was whole again and the bone and the flesh were lost, it was finished.</start_of_turn>
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe; et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	I beseech thee to come hither, and I hasten to come and loosen the limb; and when I see it dislocated, there is peace and no pain is felt.
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner; et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	But every way the corruption is already confirmed or the limb is unsound, and it will not be healed; and the corruption will persist as long as the limb is completely lost
Et vis .i. autre mire qui effondra .i. apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	And thus another mire which undermines the bone marrow swells, and then inflames from the malice of its lordship.
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	For cancer, when it is pure of melancholy humor, does not yield except when iron is touched upon it unless all the corrupted parts can be removed.
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en .ij. divisions: c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions; et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	And thus, know this well, that the work of hands has become divided into twelve divisions: that is to say, where there is peril in many things; and I shall show in every chapter of this book where there is doubt and peril.
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez; et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit; et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	If you keep your arms firmly in place, they will not speak badly of you. If you take up your weapons in custody and undertake your patients with lightness and composure, and use the best way possible, God will grant you success; and let the frivolous diseases of this life pass by. Stay close to your weapons, for from this world to the next you will receive glory.
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens: «Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.	The glory of God is in the renunciation of all earthly things: "Do not take my cure for sickness, for you are not remembered for your follies.
» J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc III chapitres.	I have devised this treatise in three chapters.
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez; et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	The first chapter concerns fire cautery and aqueous medicine, and the chapter orders from the head down; and about the forms of instruments, and instruments of cautery, and everything that is necessary for the work
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses; et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	The second chapter deals with cutting and piercing, and the dressing of wounds, and the extraction of arrows, and similar things; and the chapter orders and the forms of instruments.
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses; et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	The third chapter deals with restoring dislocations and twists, and similar things; and it is ordered from the shoulder chief down to the feet, and from the forms of the instruments.
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	As we have remembered from the work, it is necessary to say the quality of the aid and the great discomfort of great complexion.
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus; et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu; et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	I say that the quality of the aid, and the discomfort, is the longest word and the most subtle science and the greatest secret; and about this many have spoken, and they agree on this; and I am suffocated by their words, because I reduce the length.
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que .ij. complexions: c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	I say that the fire cautery helps universally for all complexion or there is matter, for it is to say complexion hot sense matter, and complexion dry sense matter.
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide; et li autre dirent le contraire: que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	In complexion chaude et seche, matters assemblement, they declare that the cautery is of great aid; and others declare the contrary: that the cautery is of no avail in disease but comes from heat and drought.
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour; et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	For the nature of fire is hot, and should not be the cure for hot diseases by heat, but by drought; and thus those who say the opposite that the cautery does great aid in hot and dry diseases that arise in the bodies of men.</start_of_turn>
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	For when you compare the body of a man and his moisture to the complexion of fire, you find the body dry.</start_of_turn
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	And I consent to this word.
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	For I have never seen it happen before in practice.</start_of_turn>
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens; des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	And thus, in no way do I know of anyone who has ever experienced such a thing except for those who have seen it, who know by long experience the chapter of cautery, the variety of complexion of men, and the causes and dispositions of their diseases, and the results and the causes of their pains; for other complexions we have no experience, even in cold and moist diseases.</start_of_turn
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	And all the more must they agree to the cautery.
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	And know this, sir, that cautery with fire is more effective for secret cures than burning cautery.
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	For fire is simple, and brings no further heat than to the member that is being cauterized, and harms no other member save its name.</start_of_turn>
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation; et par aventure ocit lou malaide Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	Burning medicines come from one member to another, causing ailments of grief to depart from the member; and by chance the patient feels the fire due to its height and the goodness of its substance does not make me do this, if there is no superabundance.
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses; et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant; or le recevez en vos pensees.	And this I have learned through experience and by the length of my service and study in this art, and it is confirmed by the truth of things; and for this reason I apologize for the length of my words, for it does not please me to keep silent the secret which is returned or the fire, and the quality of this work, as it unravels the diseases of the body, as the philosopher demonstrates; or you may follow this in your thoughts.
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	Know, son, that it is necessary to determine at what tension the cautery should be made, and when they are pricked.</start_of_turn>
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere; et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	I say that the cautery is useful in all tensions, for the harmful effects resulting from it are overcome by the aid of the cautery; and indeed if the cautery is for necessary pains that are urgent and cannot wait until the greater harm is removed from the limb.</start_of_turn
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire; car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue; et il le dient ensi; mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	And think not, dear son, if the madman makes fools of himself; for the disease which is cured by cautery has no return; and he says so; but it is not thus if they are cured, for cauteries are but medicine which moves the complexion, and dries the humors which are the cause of the pain, and is worth more than medicine for its promptness of value, and for the excellence of its work and its sovereignty.
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut; et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie; mais ce avient poc.	Indeed, it is known that disease does not arise at any time according to the complexion of the patient and the nature of the disease and its virtue; and there are assembled in him the superfluities by the acquisition of foods and similar things, except when cauteries are administered in place or if there is little superfluity and moisture, for as with cauteries of the dense kind for pain, and the similar things, and part of the pain does not return again; but this often happens.</start_of_turn>
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir; mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	And many people do not understand that cauteries are not called medicine, and that is true; but they do not believe that cauteries are worth more than medicine, but their understanding is false, for cauteries are the last of medicine for in no disease have we administered remedies that have not been useful, so we administer the cautery, and it is worth more.</start_of_turn>
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	Therefore, even though cautery is behind medicine, it does not please the minds of fools.
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance; et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes; et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	The ancients say that golden cautery is more stupid than iron, and they say that fire only comes from the quality of gold and the height of its substance; and they say that the lead of the cautery does not cause harm, but this is not seen because I have proved it, and I have found that it is like in certain men; and golden cautery is worth as much as iron, as they say.</start_of_turn>
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez; et s’on le chaufe trop; si font au feu; et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	And indeed, whenever you burn an instrument of gold, you do not know how much it is scorched by the color of gold, and when it has cooled down; and if you burn it too much, there is fire; and there is enough hindrance.
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	And for this reason we use our fire cautery, as we have learned from experience.
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	Or you have commanded this chapter from beginning to end, so that the patient may see that the matter is more manageable.</start_of_turn>
dou cautere olivaire	olive cautery
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	These olive cauteries are useful for moisture and for cold on the brain, and there are two reasons for their use: one is a disease called "soda," and the other is the accumulation of many humors that descend from the head as sweat, and from the ears, and from a multitude of dreams and pain in the teeth and throat, and even from many diseases that come from cold, such as paralysis, soda, and apoplexy, and similar diseases.
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief .iij. nuis ou .iiij., selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir; et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	The form of this cautery is that the patient should be purged by a medicinal solution modifying the head, either twice or thrice, according to what is useful and agreeable to the patient's custom; and then make the patient recover the head.
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis; aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses .ij. eulz; et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	And then make him sit comfortably between your hands, and put his hands under his belly; after that put the root of your thumb on the root of his nail between his two eyes; and there is where his two means will come, if he bleeds from the nail then withdraw the cautery which is called "olive," for this is the form:
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant; puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os .i. sol petit; et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit; aprés pren .i. poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse .iij. jors; aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre; et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	And put out the sign of ink, and make descending and extracting your hand back and forth; then keep your hand still, and rejoin the bone if you see the marrow; and if you do not see it, if you repeat the cautery until you see the bone as I told you; then take out one-eighth of an inch of the wound, and put in cotton wool and soak for two days; then put on a moist bandage. Leave on it until the swelling has gone down; then cure the wound of the bleeding which is called "tetrafarmaçon," until it is healed.
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge; et por ce si aide mues.	And the old men say, the more time passes over a wound, the more it purges; and for this reason they help with mustard.
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	And they say that the fire cautery should be left on for as long as part of the bone is not burnt, and then remove what is superfluous from the bone, and be cured.</start_of_turn>
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme .i. vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors; et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte; aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	And others say that the fire cautery should be left on for as long as there is a vein left whole, and press so hard that the bone is split as wide as a woman’s hair; and it should be left open for a long time; then it should be cured and dressed.</start_of_turn
Et ces .ij. manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor; et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier; car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres; et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	And these three methods of cautery do not seem to me to be of any use in bones in general, unless in some cases where there is pain; and mustard seems to me to be more useful; for the head of the shoulder is easily loosened by the continuous solutions of nature, as we have seen in other members; and even when the disease is slight by nature, the first semblance of cautery is more helpful and muedres for me, and I will give up on this method in these cases.</start_of_turn>
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	From ancient times, pain in the head.
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres; et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	When there is chronic pain in the head that lasts a long time, the patient should use poultices called "cochie", and purgatives of head and oil and patches; and if we do the cautery as we have said before, it is of no avail.</start_of_turn>
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit; adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	Beware if the patient's condition is serious and not too painful; then cauterize only as much as we have said previously.</start_of_turn
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai .i. cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»; et est .i. leus en coi on met ventouses; et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os: li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors; et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	After you have cauterized up to the bone of the head as we have said, and you have cauterized the vein which is called "vasselz"; and you must put on a bandage. Keep your hand still so that you do not see blood until the bone is reached: the patient feels much more pain in this cautery than in others, and I will speak of that later; and it is better to cauterize the corners than the middle of the head, for the form is like this:
dou cautere dou chief	Dou cautere dou chief.
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie: adonques li fai cauteres selonc .ij. manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	When in a part of the shoulder there comes sudden pain, and the disease extends until the root, and the head of the shoulder is expelled by medicines that modify it, and other cures have been made as I have said in the division of diseases, and all this has not helped: then make cauteries according to two methods, namely medicine of age and medicine of fire.
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope .i. poc as .ij. chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir; et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi .xij. houres; et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi .ij. jors ou .iij.; puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	The cauteries of age medicine are as follows: if you take a strong dose of alum, and oil the bone and scrape it out. If there are two heads, do the temple where the pain is located as much as you can until you can replace the dose of alum under the skin; and when it is replaced, bind it firmly and leave it in place for .xij. hours; then remove it and treat the wound with vinegar, and leave the wound open for .ij. or .iij. days; then put on a bandage soaked in butter until it covers the wound.

Instruct the patient to put his head in order; and keep his head between your hands in such a manner that he does not move, do not lower his head; after that put a wet cloth or juice of persicaria on the oil; after that burn the cautery which is partly: and let it touch the head as if it were a pine cone of wool, gather together that which is above so that the cautery is firm; if you see that the head is pointed from one side to the other, or if you see that it is as if there is a tent; however, this that is touching is worth more than your work.
Aprés presse la fistule s’ele est overte, et en trai la porriture, et la seche; et s’ele est close, si la oevre, et trai fuers la bowe; aprés met sus le cautere chaut forment, et tien ta main au cautere a la partie dou neif ensus de l’oil, que ta mains ne faice folie; et met le cautere en la graisse de l’oil, et la corromp.	After pressing the fistula, it swells out over the bone and the marrow; and if it closes, if the bone is soft, draw out the arrow. Then put on the hot cautery and hold your hand over the cautery at the part of the thumb next to the oil, so that your hand does not tremble; and place the cautery in the fat of the oil and corrupt it.
Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien.	If you come to the beginning of the cautery up to the bone, that would be well.
Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse III jors; aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se XL jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers; et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	If this is not the case, if you repeat the cautery once more, and if you are in doubt, let it remain for three days; after that put on a moist bandage and keep the cure of desiccation until it is healed; and if forty days pass and it is not healed, put on an aggressive corrosive medicine until the bone is uncovered; and proceed according to what comes to light in your chapter.
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent.	And there is a manner of cautery for fistula of which none of the ancients have spoken
Entens a fistule, et fens le leu; aprés met en la fendure I camahan subtil de coi ci est li forme:	When there is a fistula, and open the limb; after that put in the wound one barleycorn-sized piece of charcoal of this sort:
et i font a la quantiteit d’une .З. de plonc; et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil; et covient c’on mette sus l’oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d’uefz ou en awe: li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit.	And I do it in the quantity of a third of a pound; and hold your hand or arm firmly, and do not move the patient at all, only let the molten plumbe fall to its own level; and I advise you to put upon the patient a soft cloth moistened in vinegar or wine: for the plumbe will otherwise cause great harm to the limb from the great heat.
Et se li fistule est sanee per le cautere que nos avons dit, c’est boin.	And if the fistula is cured by the cautery as we have said, then it is well.
Se ce non, si covient aministrer pertus au neif, et ramener la fistule au cors dou neif selonc ceu qu’il covient en som propre leu.	And if not, if you must administer an opening to the fistula, and bring it back to its original place as it should be in its proper place.
des crevaices en levres	in limb bones
Mout de fois avienent crevaices en levres que sont apelees «poil», et meismement en levres des enfans.	Many times crevasses occur in limbs which are called "hair", and even in limbs of children.
Quant tu cures ces crevaices de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et li cure ne profite, adonques eschaufe .i. petit cautere cultellaire selonc ceste forme:	When you treat these fractures in the way we have mentioned in the sections, and the cure does not help, then you must make a small cautery burn according to this form:
Et le met hastanment en celles crevaices tant qu’il viegne jusc’a font; aprés cure le leu de cerote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And hold the burn on these fractures until it is dead; after the cure the limb until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
de l’aposteme de la goule	of the opening of the vein.
Quant apostume vient en la racine de la goule ou en l’uve, ou ou palais, ou as racines des dens, aprés fait porriture et ront et est enveillis et devient fistule; et tu le cures si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie: adonques covient il que tu aies .i. cautere selonc la quantiteit de la fistule; aprés le bote ou pertus de la fistule, et tien ta main tant que li fer chaus viegne au font de li, et ou derrien leu; et fai ensi une fois ou .ij., aprés le cure de ce que nos avons dit en cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est curez ensi, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si covient descovrir le leu et oster l’os corrumput, selonc ceu que vos le troverez en son chapistre.	When the root of the gullet, or in the eye, or in the palate, or in the root of the teeth, after making an incision and drilling, becomes swollen and forms a fistula; you shall cure it as we have said in the preceding divisions, and it will not be of use: therefore you must cauterize according to the quantity of the fistula; after draining or perforating the fistula, and holding your hand until life returns to its former state at the front or behind; and do this once or twice, after the cure of what we have said in the cures, until it is healed; and if it is cured thus, it is well; but if not, you must uncover the bone and remove the corrupted bone, as you would in its chapter.
dou movement des dens	When the root of the gullet, or in the eye, or in the palate, or in the root of the teeth, after making an incision and drilling, becomes swollen and forms a fistula; you shall cure it as we have said in the preceding divisions, and it will not be of use: therefore you must cauterize according to the quantity of the fistula; after draining or perforating the fistula, and holding your hand until life returns to its former state at the front or behind; and do this once or twice, after the cure of what we have said in the cures, until it is healed; and if it is cured thus, it is well; but if not, you must uncover the bone and remove the corrupted bone, as you would in its chapter.
Quant les gencives sont mollifies par moistor et les dens muevent, et tu le cures per medicines et ceu ne vaut, adonc met le chief dou malaide en ton sain; aprés eschaufe le cautere dont li forme venra ci aprés en teil maniere que tu mettes une cainne sor le dent; et met dedens le cautere chaut hastanment, et tien tant ta main que li malaides sente la chalor venant a la racine dou dent; aprés lieve ta main et rencomence le cautere selonc ta volenteit; aprés emplisse li malaides sa bouche d’awe salee, et la teigne une houre et raiche fuers.	When the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth move, and you cure it with medicines; this is of no use: therefore you must put the patient’s head in your hand; after flushing out the cautery which will come afterwards in part as much as you put a bandage over the tooth; and put charcoal inside the cautery immediately, and hold your hand until the patient feels the heat coming from the root of the tooth; after that let go of your hand and repeat the cautery as you wish; after that fill the patient’s mouth with coarse salt and hold it for an hour and a quarter.
Et en teil maniere li dens qui estoit movans si est confermez, et li gencive mollifie restrainte, et li moistors corrumpue sechie.	And in part, when it moves thus, if confirmed, and the joint softens, restrains, and the moisture corrupts dries.
de la dolor des dens	And in part, when it moves thus, if confirmed, and the joint softens, restrains, and the moisture corrupts dries.
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc .ij. manieres: et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	When pain of the teeth comes from cold, or there is cold or heat, and medical cures are of no avail, then it is necessary to cauterize according to two methods: cautery of the carpus and cautery of fire.
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain; aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez; et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus .i. fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.	If cautery of burn is like taking barley straw, and you take the end in a spatula of iron or of lead; after taking cotton and wrapping over the tip of a needle, and the soft tissue in barley, and put on the aching tooth immediately and hold until it is cold; and do it often until the virtue comes to the root of the tooth, and if you see that the soft tissue is slipping and cotton in barley is rough, and put on the aching tooth, and put on the iron hot until the fire comes to the root of the tooth.
Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide; aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez; fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain.	The cautery is applied with such force that if you take a cauldron of iron or lead, or something of great size, if the fire does not reach the patient's mouth; after heating the cautery, when it has formed like this, put it on the tooth and hold your hand until the cautery is cold; do this often, for the pain will be great or even greater tomorrow.
Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l’empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And you must make the patient fill his mouth with good burr in the haste of this cautery, and then hold it tight; this is the shape of the cautery:
Et fai cautere dou queil chief que tu voudras, et selonc ceu que tu as pooir; et c’est li forme de la caine:	And do the cautery as you please, and according to what you have desired; and this is the form of the needle:
des scrophules	And the size on the pierced wound and the moisture, if it is less severe, because they are of little blood. And if there are some of these wounds or chieftains or it has no moisture, and of those wounds which I cauterize or chieftain from an old woman; and find the wound just like a hard stone, rough and white, and cannot break it; and if no blood comes out, it is just as well to make a wound like a stone. In other wounds that come from chieftains and have roots of ears, it overturns if it is kept too long, for it makes the wound worse. And it cures as it should.
Quant les scrophules sont de fleume et de moistors froides, et ne sont obeissans a digestion par medicines, adonques eschaufe le cautere cheveit de coi ci aprés vient li forme, et ait II aovertures por les fumees a issir au cautere de l’autre partie; et met le cautere chaut sus l’apostume une fois, ou II se mestier est, tant qu’il viegne au font de l’apostume; et se li apostume est petis si met cautere selonc la quantiteit de l’apostume, et le laisse ensi III jors; et met sus coton moilliet em burre tant que li arsure soit ostee; aprés cure le leu d’oignemens et de tentes tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the scrofula is of phlegm and cold moisture, and is not subject to digestion by medicines, then evacuate the cautery quickly; for two openings will form from the fumes to irritate the cautery on the other side; place the cautery hot upon the abscess once, or if it sticks, until it comes to the front of the abscess; and if the abscess is small, put the cautery in proportion to the quantity of the abscess and leave it in place for three days; place upon it a wet compress until the swelling has subsided.
Li forme de la cainne:	The formation of the abscess:
Quant les moistors vainquent sus les chenals dou pormon, et meismement quant ce vient de froide complexion, adonc covient que li malaides soit voidiez premiers par medicines solutives; aprés li fai cautere a la racine de la gorge, et te garde que tu ne venir mie jusc’a la gorge, et n’ardre dou keur mais c’un poc.	When moisture prevails over the channels of the pores, and in the same way as when it comes from a cold complexion, then it is necessary that the patient be first emptied by means of resolving medicines; then apply the cautery to the root of the throat, and keep it so that you do not go too far up, and do not burn anything except the pus.
Aprés li fai I autre cautere a la jointure dou col au chief de l’espinee, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» de coi nos avons la forme devant; et cure le leu si com nos avons devant dit tant qu’il soit sanez.	After that, do another cautery at the joint of the collarbone at the base of the scapula; and let the cautery be named "clamp" because of its shape; and cure the limb as we have said above until it is healed.
de la toust	of the vomitting
Quant tous et maladie de pormon sont de moistors froides, et li malaides nen ait fievre ne sechor, et est li maladie anciaine, se li fai ij cauteres sus la forcele en leus vuis; et .i. autre cautere emmi le pis entre .ij. mameles; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» selonc la forme qui est devant dite.	When all diseases of the pores are caused by cold moisture, and the patient has neither fever nor sweating, and is an ancient ailment, then make three cauteries on the forcele of the veins; and another cautery between two mammelons; or let the cautery which is called "claw" according to the shape which is before said.
Et se tu vues, fai cautere en poignant a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins» de coi li forme est ci devant en la maladie des oreilles; et soient li poins jusc’a XXX, ou enqui entor.	And if you see, do a cautery by pricking with all the cautery that is called "staples" because of their shape in the ear disease; and let the staples be up to XXX, or as much as needed.</start_of_turn>

Et por ceu sont li cautere plus legier, por ceu que tu en fais .iij. a cop.	And for these two are the lighter cauteries, because you make two at a time.
de la dislocation de l’ajutoire	De la dislocation de l’ajutoire.
Quant li chiés de l’ajutoire est desaloiez par cause de moistor, et on le remet a leu, et il n’i puet demorer ains revient adés et desalue par petit movement qui avient, si com nos avons esproveit, adonques covient il que tu ramoinnes la dislocation premierement.	When the head of the shoulder is dislocated due to moisture, and it is reset but cannot stay in place, repeatedly dislocating with slight movement as we have experienced, then you must first reset the dislocation.
Aprés soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos et sus son costeit; aprés lieve le keur qui est dedens le titillite as dois de ta main senestre; et se li jointure est desaluee dedens, si eschaufe le cautere qui a .ij. ners douqueil ci est li forme:	Afterwards, support the patient on his back and on his ribs; then hold the thumb that is inside the armpit with your left hand; and if the joint is dislocated, if necessary, grasp the cautery which has about the size of a needle.
et cauterize lou keur tant qu’il le perce jusc’a costeit, et venrait li fugure dou cautere ensamble .iiij. cauteres; et por ceu est faite cautere avec le cautere qui a .iij. ners, por coi li figure de cauterization sunt sis cauteres; et sont li nerf selonc la subtiliteit d’une tente et c’est li forme dou cautere qui a .iij. ners:	and cauterize the thumb until it reaches the ribs, and the escape of the cautery would be around three cauteries; and for this reason the cautery is done with the cautery that has two needles, because the shape of the cautery is that of two needles:
Et aucune fois est ajostez sus ce .i. nerf por coi il i a .viij. cauteres.	And never is it adjusted upon this vein because there are six cautery marks upon it.
Aprés met sus le cautere porrelz broiez avec seil; aprés fai reposer le malaide, et ne soit meus li membres par lonc tens tant qu’il soit bien confortez.	And afterwards put on the cautery pliers bruised with silk; afterwards rest the patient, and do not move the limb long after it is well comforted
Et s’il est desaloiez desus, liquelz chose avient poc, adonques fait cautere sus l’epaisse dou cautere clavile, ou mout de cauteres en poignant.	And if it is dislocated below, whatever the cause, do a cautery on the thickness of the clamp cautery, or do several pricks.</start_of_turn
Car li jointure est refermee, et est ostee li moistor et est sanez li malaides.	For the joint is closed, and the moisture is bony, and the patient is healed.
Quant en l’estomac vienent froidures et mout de moistors tant qu’il l’estraient a sa complexion, et sont multipliet li catharre a lui, et es manieres de cures acostumees et il ne profite mie, adonc covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son dos, et estende ses jambes et ses mains.	When in the stomach come cold chills and moisture as much as they are expelled from their complexion, and are multiplied by customary treatments, it does no good; therefore it is recommended that the patient should lie on his back, extend his legs and arms.
De ceu en aprés li fai III cauteres I desoz la cuillier dou pis per la quantiteit d’un doi, a tout le cautere clavile, et II cauteres defuers les II costez tant que li figure des cauteres soit a III angles, et ait teil espaice entre l’une et l’autre qu’elles ne soient jointes ensamble quant elles giteront porriture; et soient li cautere si parfont qu’il porpreignent les II pars dou keur, et soit li figure des cauteres selonc ceste forme sens ajostement:	Afterwards, make three cauteries one on the navel and two below the ribs for the amount of an egg, at every cautery nail, and two cauteries further down the two ribs until the figure of the cauteries is at a right angle, and has a space between them that they are not joined together when they swell with pus; and let the cauteries be so firm that they protrude the two parts of the kidney, and let the figure of the cauteries be as described above.</start_of_turn>
Et se tu vues cauterize d’un grant cautere enmi l’estomac selonc ceste forme; et celui qui avra paour de cest cautere, cauterize en poignant et seigne sus l’estomac i. point selonc la quantiteit que tu vues d’enche; puis le cauterize a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins».	And if thou seest cauterized with a great cautery in the stomach according to this form; and he who hath fear of this cautery, cauterize by pricking and marking on the stomach at a single point according to the quantity that thou seest of the incision; then cauterize at all the cautery that is called `poins`.
Aprés le cure de la cure que nos avons eut devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After the treatment of the ailment that we have seen before, while it is still sane.
Quant au foie vient dolor de froit et de moistor et de grosse ventositeit, tant qu’il est fuer mis de sa complexion natureil per les superfluitez; et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne li profite mie, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son haitereil; et signe d’enche III cauteres selonc ceste forme et ceste figure et ceste quantiteit sus lou foie, defuer les ypocondres, lai ou li coutes de l’ome vient; et ait d’espaice entre chaicun cautere la groissece d’un doi; et soient li cautere dou lonc dou cors, et ne presser mie mout ta main a tot le cautere; et soit arse tant soulement li moitiez dou keur, et soit li malaides drois sus ses piez; et s’il ne peut, si soit gisans, et estende ses jambes, et lieve ses brais; et c’est li forme:	When the liver comes with pain of fruit and moisture and great distension, since it is forced out of its natural complexion by the excesses; and the patient is cured of what we have said in divisions, and he does not benefit from it, if he is not treated with gentleness on his belly; and to sign of the incision, three cauteries according to this form and figure and quantity on the liver, driving away the spleen, the liver or the ribs of the man; and let there be between each cautery the thickness of an egg; and let the cautery be long as the nail of the thumb, and do not press too hard with your hand over all the cautery; and let the burn only half as much as necessary, and let the patient lie on his side; and if he cannot, let him lie without moving, and extend his legs, and hold his arms; and this is the form.
Et se ta volentez est, si cauterize ces cauteres dou cutellaire, se tu es subtilz et saiges en l’art, et te warde que tu n’ardes mie tout le keur, car tu feroies sechier tout le cors; et qu’il ne viegne jusc’a boueil, car li keurs est mout subtilz lai endroit, et lou saiches por voir.	If your will be so bold, if you cauterize these tender carbuncles, if you are subtle and prudent in the art, and guard that you do not burn all the hair, because you must fiercely dry all the body; and that it does not reach boiling, for the hair is subtle in that place, and the nails for seeing.
Quant il a apostume au foie, et tu vues savoir s’il est en la char dou foie ou en la toile: s’il est en la char, se sent li malaides dolor ne mie trop fort; et s’il est en la toile, si sent dolor forsenee.	When there is swelling in the liver, and you see that it is in the liver itself or in the spleen: if it is in the liver, the patient feels little pain; but if it is in the spleen, the pain is violent.</start_of_turn>
Et lors quant ceste cure desoit les mires, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus sa teste; et puis seigne d’enche le leu ou li apostumes est, et puis chaufe le cautere qui est semblans au rais, de coi ci est li forme:	And when this cure is finished, if you command that the patient be calm on his head; and then mark on the skin where the vein or abscess is, and then burn the cautery that is similar in shape to a thorn, because this is the form.</start_of_turn
Et cauterize I cautere tant que li keurs soit ars, et viegne jusc’a syphac, tant que li porreture soit toute fuers; aprés la cure selonc la cure des essues tant qu’il soit sanez; et ne covient mie que de cest cautere use nuls fuers que cil qui ait estudieit longement en l’art de medicine, et par cui mains cestes maladies ont corrut aucune fois.	And cauterize I cauterize while the hair is coarse, and come until the root is strong; while the wound is open; after the cure according to the cure for the ailments until it is healed; and do not dare to use this cautery except for those who have studied for a long time in the art of medicine, and by whom these diseases have never occurred.
Adonques puet il hardiement ovrer, et toutevoies il me semble que mues vaut li laissier.	Therefore, he dares not work, and in truth it seems to me that it is better to leave it alone
dou cautere de pleuresin	of chest pain
Li ancien dirent que on doit faire a pleuresin cauteres de racines d’aristologe, et en teil maniere: pren une racine d’aristologe longe, la plus grant que tu poras troveir, et soit seche, et soit ausi grosse et ausi longe comme tes dois; et la moille en oile, et l’emprens au feu, et cauterize .i. cautere entre la forcele et lou col, et .ij. petis cauteres un poc en dessendant en la partie qui est desoz la barbe; et .ij. cauteres entre la quinte coste et la sisime, en declinant derrier un poc; et .i. cautere emmi le pis, et .i. autre sus l’estomac, et .i. entre .ij. espaules, et .ij. as .ij. costez dou pis defuers le cautere qui est entre .ij. espaules; et ne presser mie ta main, ains fai apertement ausi com en odorant.	The ancient said that we must make at pleasure incisions of the roots of Aristotle, and in this manner: take a root of Aristotle long, the greatest that you will find, and let it be dry, and let it be as thick and as long as your thumbs; and moisten it in oil, and impress it on fire, and cauterize. Namely, cauterize between the shoulder and the elbow, and twice cauterize a little bit in descending on the part which is below the beard; and once cauterize between the fifth rib and the hip, declining behind a little bit; and once cauterize the spleen, and once on the stomach, and once between the two ribs, and twice as many costae as there are ribs defending the cautery which is between the two ribs. And do not press your hand, but make it open as much as if you were smelling.
Et dirent aucun ancien que aucun home usent de cautere de feir semblant a I raseur, et l’eschaufent et le mettent entre les costes, tant qu’il vient a cel aposteme; et saut fuers li dolor, si com nos avons dit en l’aposteme dou foie.	And they say no old man has ever used a fire cautery similar to this, and the ash and charcoal are placed between the ribs, until it comes to this abscess; and sudden pain follows, as we have said in the abscess of the liver.
Mais en cestui ovraige est paour ou li malaides muert maintenant, ou fistule i vient qui ne puet estre sanee.	But in this work there is fear or the patient dies immediately, or an abscess forms which cannot be healed.
de la mice	of mice.
Quant tu cures la maladie de la mice de ceu que nos avons dit as divisions des cures, et il ne profite mie, adonques i afierent .iij. manieres de cautere que tuit sont boin.
