Et puis le fai entrer ou bain tant que li cors li soit un poc arousez, et lou fai entrer ou lit, et li dolor s’en ira toute et sera sanez.	Then let him enter the bath or wash as long as his body is relaxed, and let him enter the water or lie down, and the pain will vanish and be healed.
Et saiches que nuls ne doit user de cautere de telz medicines, se ceu n’est aprés l’evacuation de cors.	And let no one use the fire cautery of such medicines, except after the evacuation of blood.
Et Dyascorides dist que quant li voine sciatique est cauterizee de fiens de chievre, si i aide mout; et doit estre fais li cauteres en teil maniere.	And Dioscorides says that when the sciatic vein is cauterized with vinegar, if it helps with moisture; and it must be done cautiously.</start_of_turn>
Prenez lainne et la beurez d’oile vielz, et metez sus la fossete qui est entre le pouce dou piez et l’autre qui est apelez foscile.	Take lint and soak it in oil, and put it on the pit between the thumb and the great toe and the one that is called fossicle.</start_of_turn
Aprés pren fiens de chievre sec, et l’empren a feu tant qu’il soit charbons, et lou met sus la laine, et le laisse tant qu’il soit estains; et refai encor ensi, et ne cesser de faire ensi tant que tu penses par sens qu’il viegne jusc’a la hainche, et que li dolor soit cessee; et cist manieres de cautere est apelez «cautere de chievre».	Then take vinegar and soak it in oil until it is dry, and burn it until it is charcoal, and put it on the lint, and leave it until it is stained; and do it again, and do not stop doing it until you think that the pain has gone away; and this method of cautery is called "vinegar cautery".</start_of_turn>
de la dolor dou dos	of backache.</start_of_turn>
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	When pain comes from the back, or from sitting or percussion or from too great an evacuation, or from similar things of cold expanding matter, none of these signs are worth cautery, except for that which comes from the infusion of cold matter.
Il covient c’aprés ceu que li malaides est voidiez de pilules fetides ou d’autres semblans, que on li faice sus lou dos, lai ou li dolor tient, trois lignes signies d’enche, et en chescune ligne .v. cauteres ou plus selonc la vertut et la quantiteit que li malaides puet soffrir; et soit fait li cauteres selonc le cautere qui est apelez «poins»; et se tu vues, fai .iij. cauteres ou .iiij. au cautere clavile moien selonc ceste forme:	When the patient is free from foul pills or other things of that kind, that we make on the back where the pain persists, three lines signed with a hook, and in the middle line three cautery marks or more, as much as the patient can bear; and let the cautery be done according to the cautery called "pointed"; and if you see it, do two or three cautery marks at the middle cautery according to this fashion:
Maintes fois vient ceste maladie as petis enfans, et li signes de l’encomencement si est qu’il ont estroite alainne quant il se lievent, et paor; et tu trueves en la derriene espinee dou dos et en nous l’apparance qui vient sus les autres espinees.	Many times this disease comes as a small swelling, and the signs of its beginning are that it has burst the skin when it swells, and there is pain; and you find it at the lower spine of the back and in us the appearance that comes after the others.
Quant tu vois ceu et tu le vues curer, si le cauterize au cautere de celcle selonc ceste forme.	When you see this and you see it healed, if you cauterize at the cautery of this circle in this fashion.
Si que li cautere porpreigne chescune partie de l’espinee egaument.	If the fire cautery burns some part of the spine, it increases.
Et se tu vues, si cauterize entor l’espinee au cautere poignant II lignes ou III, et soient li poins pres l’uns de l’autre.	And if you see that the burn penetrates the spine as much as two or three lines, and that the points are close to each other.
Aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez selonc ceu que nos avons dit, et warde que tu n’amenistrer cautere en gilbositeit qui soit en spame de nerf.	After treating the wound as much as necessary, and when it is healed as we have said, keep the cautery away from the bone which is close to a nerve
de la dolor des jointes	of the pain of the joints
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere: fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	When joint pain arises from moisture that has spread throughout the limb, and when pain originates from a wound, the sufferer cries out "podagre!" properly; and when the cause is cold and treatment by medicine fails to cure it, if it is cured by cautery in part: make the mouth of the cautery around the joint of the limb and let the cautery be olive oil in this fashion.
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point».	And if it is necessary to prick on the face of the bone, do not make the burn with the whole cautery; rather mark it with the word "point".
Et se les dolors viegnent jusc’a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil III cauteres ou IIII de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire; et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n’i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.	And if there is pain that extends up to the joints of the limbs and such things occur repeatedly, if you make the burn on each elbow three times or on each limb twice, with the olive cautery; and if you must do more, do so, but do not hold your hand too tightly until the burn is cool.
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre.	And if the pains descend down to the groin and the back, administer the cautery as we have said in this chapter.
Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile II lignes; et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main; et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines.	And if the pains are as far as the hands, if you make points at the elbow two lines; and if there is no more pain there, if you make points at the wrist and at the root of the hand; and if the pains come down to the buttocks or as far as the shoulder, if you cauterize some part, and make the patient drink and give medicine.
Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	For if you make him drink and purge phlegm, he will be healed by the help of God.
de la routure dou syfac	from the root to the surface
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor; et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre; aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors; puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When the scapula is fractured, and the bone fragments descend as nails, this is new; if you see that it must be cured, do not move him from his place; and if he uses things that leave his belly open, so that the bowels descend from his belly; after that, make him sit on his buttocks between your hands, and command him to hold his arm tight until the bone fragments are rejoined, and hold them at your sides, and sign an incision on the scapula over the shoulder blade, and do everything that seems like half of a circle below the ribs; then withdraw the cautery like this:
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles.	As long as he is limp and groans senselessly.
Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu; et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier; et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui I cussin et I serjant sus les cuisses, et I autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains; puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere; que tu ne le brulasses; et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	Then bind the belly to its place; and he holds his hand over so that it does not return backwards; and give the patient good compresses on the body, and put a cushion and a servant on the hips; then put the cautery on the sign at the whole hand, and hold it straight and hold it as long as you touch the bone, and if you do not touch the bone the first time, do it again until you reach the bone; and beware prudently that the belly does not swell when you make the cautery; that you do not burn it; and that by this the patient does not die or any other harm.
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien.	And soaks that when you do not reach the bone with the cautery, your work is in vain.
Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure; aprés III jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides XL jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee; et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	And it is recommended that the cautery be subtle in relation to the measure of the body, and for great people also great in relation to their measure; after three days cure the wound of the burn until the eschar is bony; after that cure other wounds until they are healed; and keep the patient lying down for forty days on his back until the wound is well closed; and it is recommended that his movements be relaxed so that the swelling does not go down when he sits up to go to bed.</start_of_turn>
Et aprés XL jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse XL autres jors; et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire; et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement.	And after forty days, when he wishes to rise, let him be supported by a good cushion and let him stay for forty days; and let him rest peacefully, that he works little and takes care of himself, and avoids too great indulgence in drink and eating, and too high a diet; and when he has followed this advice, if he is healed entirely.</start_of_turn
Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	And I shall speak of the cure of the tail in its chapter.
de la routure dou ventre	Of the evacuation of the belly.
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai I cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur; aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit; et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a III angles selonc ceste forme:	When they come out through other bellies and are known, and you see that they do not grow any more, if you make the burn with the burn cautery as much as is necessary, and a third of the way up; after the cure as we have said; and no one has said that it should be burned with the burn cautery at three angles according to this form.
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile.	but first sign the limb well and make a line along the width of the wound, and another at the bottom, and hold your hand firmly with all your might on the burn cautery clamp
Mais li premiers cauteres est plus legiers et muedres.	But the first burnings are lighter and milder.
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	than the old ones in any limb.
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor.	When pain comes to any limb, or to the hip or to the wound, and this pain lasts a long time, and the medical cure is not worth it, then it is advisable to burn it with the cautery which is called “points,” and to burn it according to the length of the limb and the width and its weakness and its toughness and its twists and its pain.
s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien; se ceu nom, recomence I autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	If he is sane after the first cautery, it is well; if not, repeat another cautery on that side, for it is customary that it must burn towards the neighboring limb, so that you make the cauteries until the patient is sane.
de meselerie	When pain arises in any limb, be it from sitting or injury, and this pain persists for a long time, and the medical cure proves useless, then it is appropriate to cauterize using the cautery called "poins," or to cauterize according to the length of the limb, its breadth and weakness, its toughness and flexibility, and its location of torsion and pain. If it is cured after the first cautery, that is well; if not, repeat the procedure. Indeed, it is customary to perform subsequent cauteries on the adjacent part of the limb so that you can make the cauteries until the patient is cured.
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie.	The disease never helps itself with a cautery, and even the sickness that comes from the corruption of phlegm and melancholy.
Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai V cauteres sus lou chief: I emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous; et II sus les II cornes, et I derrierre sus le haiterel; et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir; et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	Can you see the cautery being made? Take care if the sickness is at its beginning, and if it is cured as we have said in the division, and do not delay, and you doubt that the corruption does not reach the whole sickness, then do five cauteries on the head: one at the new head, and the other towards the front at the end of the beard; and two on the two horns, and one behind on the heel; and leave as much of your hand as the cauteries come up to the bone, and as long as the scabs come out forcefully so that the vapors of the thick humors can escape; and cauterize on the mouse according to what is before you
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse; et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et .i. cautere en som lou neis, et .ij. cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et .vj. cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et .i. grant sus la crupie et .i. autre delez, et .ij. sus les .ij. espaules; et .ij. sus les coutes, et .ij. sus les tendrons dou pis, et .i. sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains; et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler; et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et .i. autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et .i. autre sus lou foie.	And if the moisture is sparse throughout; and it persists openly, as you must know, that you must cauterize from these cauteries which we have mentioned or chief, namely: cauterize on the summit of the nose, and two on the eyebrow of the eye, three on the eyebrow of the shoulder, one large on the hip and one elsewhere, two on the two thumbs, two on the wrists, and two on the tendons of the elbows, and one on each joint of the hands and feet, and on the fossae of the hands; and beware of the nerves that are behind the calcaneus, that you do not burn them; and in no way perform cautery on the bone of the ankle or on the bone of the stomach or on the liver.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite; et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus.	And the boils that the more you burn, the more they help, and nourish them; and the boils that the patients do not feel pain from the burn, because the flesh is already corrupted.
Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers.	And you must know that the burn should be large and small according to the members and joints, as you will do in handling various objects.
Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	After treating the wound with flour from time to time with honey and other cures until it is healed
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre; et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	When swelling comes to any limb and is cured with medicines and oils and plasters, and is not healed, then you must burn the limb according to the greatness and smallness of the limb; and the burn must be done at the thick end of the bone; then you must cure the wound with ointment until it is healed
Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure; et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	And never is the fire cautery done on hand, foot, or back, at the issue of nerves that move the limb; and thus if it is ossified, it swells; and in no way should anyone interfere with it unless they are skilled in handling members and the issues of nerves that move like horses.
de albaras	When swelling occurs in any limb and is cured by medicines, oils, and plasters, and is not completely healed, then it is necessary to perform cautery on the limb according to the size and severity of the swelling; and let the burn penetrate deeply into the flesh. Then cure with unguents until the swelling is healed. And never perform cautery on the hand, foot, or back, at the opening of a nerve that causes the limb to move, or if it is bony swelling; and in no case should anything interfere with it except one who is skilled in limbs and the issues of the moving nerves and bones.
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color; puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie; et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the disease called "albaras" is present, and medicines are of no avail, then it is necessary to cauterize with a needle a little deep, according to the amount of flesh involved, until the burn is solid; and then cure with flour of times, lentils with rose oil and plantain leaves, with colon and alum, a part of each; mix them all together and bind them with a cloth, and keep it covered until healed.
li cure de chancre par cautere	The cure for fistula by cautery
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble I cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.	When a boil comes at the beginning, and you see it stop, if you burn it with the cautery that seems like a circle, all around the boil.</start_of_turn>
Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre; et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois; et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	And all these people say that the burn is done in the middle of the boil; and in no way does it seem good to me, because I fear that it will be ulcerated and corrupted, and I have already seen several times that it must not be done; and the right thing is to burn around it, with the cautery which is called the circle, as we have said previously.</start_of_turn>
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	of the swelling that cannot be measured
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens; et tu la vues haster de meurer: adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant; aprés le laisse ensi.	When anyone has a disease which is called "adubelati", and it delays in healing or because of its excessive growth or because of the patient's weakness when decrepit (that is to say when he is old), and there is a great amount of blood, or for some other reason; and you see it haste to heal: then you cauterize around the mouth of small cauteries by pricking; and afterwards you leave it alone.
Car elle se hastera de meureir.	For it will haste to heal.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you see it turning pale with all the cautery, if the burn is large:
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis.	And put your hand in the middle of this disease which is called "adubelati" until the cauteries have perceived the cold, and be such cauteries as the patient feels the pain depart in part as the process of putrefaction is accelerated.
Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	Afterwards, cure as long as he is perfectly healthy.
li cure dou feu par fer	The fire cautery. Instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches.	Another symptom of disease is called "corrodens," which is nothing other than the swelling of a limb, because it softens the bones like dry leather.
Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est; aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit.	If you see this disease in which one can suffer from the entire fire cautery, then you must burn the nails small and great according to what is appropriate for the limb or the disease; after you have cauterized all the parts until you have eradicated all the corruption, and nothing remains of it, only that which is corrupted remains osteomyelitis.</start_of_turn>
Et puis le laisse III jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption.	And then leave it for three days, and put on the cauterized limbs, and cover them with oil until the blisters from the fire are ossified, and all the corruption.</start_of_turn
Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.	After the cure of external medicines that cause carbuncles.</start_of_turn>
Et se tu vois aprés III jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus.	If after three days the hair does not grow back, it is good; and if this does not happen, repeat the cautery on that which remains corrupted.
Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu; mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division: pren la quant tu en as mestier.	This medicine is never enough to cure a wound; but indeed the fire cautery is of greater help, as I have already said in the previous section: take as much as you need.
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	from pores that come as pieces
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet.	Often there arises a disease from the swelling of the feet, which is called "clos" according to our understanding, and is a great burdensome thing that swells the feet
Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc II manieres.	And the cautery of this disease is done in two ways.
C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude.	That is to say, fire cautery and hot water cautery
Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe I cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi III jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines.	Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe. I cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges. Aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi III jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racine.
Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	If thou art scorched by fire, I order thee to cauterise as doth a needle of wool. Make it of good iron of the measure that it may penetrate the heel of all parts, and leave subtle margins. Then put all about the heel, and lay thy hand round the heel until it comes to the front of the heel; and leave it there for three days until it begins to yield. Then make an embolus of wild mallow bruised with gel, and leave the embolus upon all night, and bind it firmly and it shall be plucked from its root.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude; et est en teil maniere: pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues; et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine; et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre; puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines.	And if they are converted by boils of bad air, and happen often in the hands and in the feet, if you can bring forth a hot caustic; it is in part like this: take a splinter of thorn or iron, or a quill of gutta, and put it on the boil and the root, that is to say, blisters; and put the splinter on so that it covers everything around, then put a little of warm water, and hold your hand firmly, and press your hand backwards so that the margin of the splinter reaches the root of the boil, and can find the warm water going deep down to the root; and offer the patient a little of the warmth of the water for an hour; then leave it alone, and it will burst out all at its roots.
Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	So do another like that, until you have plucked out all that is at the source, and cure the sores that cause pain.
li cure dou trembler	you cure the tremor.
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices .iiij. cauteres ou .iv. sus l’espinee dou dos, .i. cautere entre chescune espinee; et .i. cautere ou pez, et .i. sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire; si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	When some tremble from cold, or from quartan fever or from any other cause, if you make for them three or four cauteries on the spine of the back, one cautery between the shoulder blades, and one cautery or pinch on the stomach at the olive cautery, if you leave them to tremble, they will haste the recovery from the cold sickness.
des pustules puans	When some tremble from cold, or from quartan fever or from any other cause, if you make for them three or four cauteries on the spine of the back, one cautery between the shoulder blades, and one cautery or pinch on the stomach at the olive cautery, if you leave them to tremble, they will haste the recovery from the cold sickness.
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues.	Never do wounds appear by chance, or boils filled with pus, which come from corrupted matters.
si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule: un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire.	If it is necessary at the outset when they appear, that we make cautery upon each head of the boils: a subtle cautery of fum of myrtle, or that the point be grasped by fire, or of long aristologe root, or of lenticular cautery.
Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez; mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	And never do we cauterize at the outset when they appear, according to this manner, for it does not prevent the pus from coming forward, but is broken by the excess from which it comes, and is healed; but it is necessary that this be done after the evacuation of blood
quant li artere est copee	When the artery is severed.
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	There have often been great discharges of blood from the artery that is severed at the wound that comes from the surgeon, or at the incision of the abscess, or at the cautery of the limb, and similar things; and it is a great grief thing to extend it.</start_of_turn>
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus; puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge; puis empren .i., ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	And whenever this happens to anyone, if you are in a hurry to put your thumb on the wound of the vein, and you strain too much without being appeased by the blood, and that no blood comes out any more; then put the olive cautery on the wound several small and large times until they are all red; and take hold, that is to say, big or small as the wound and the limb allow, since the artery is clear, and put the cautery on that vein or hold your thumb there, and hold the cautery as long as it is not fixed.</start_of_turn>
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement .i. autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if it spurts out when you take your thumb away from the vein, and the cautery is finished, take hold urgently of another cautery that is on the fire.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez; et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide; et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des .iiij. manieres que nos avons dit: ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc; et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	And cease not to do this one after the other until the limb is fully extended; and beware that thou dost not touch the nerve which is below, and that no other mischief arise upon the patient; and that when without drawing blood from an artery, one cannot well fill himself up again as when the artery is large, save by one of the three ways that we have said: or by cautery, or by extraction when it is not otherwise treated, or by tightly tying with thread or by medicines placed upon it which have power to fill up blood; and let it be bound and strained afterwards.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Who will bring about a lasting restoration of the limb except by the strict draping of cloths or the application of hot things upon it, or other similar things, if it does not profit thereby in some way.
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne; et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez; et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	And if this happens to anyone and there is no remedy or medicine present, if he must put his thumb on the wound of the vein as we have said, and keep it still until it is healed from under the wound and from under the vein; and do not move it, but moisten it often with cold water so that it be cold as long as the limb is frozen and swollen and healed; and make inquiries of him concerning the things which he must have to cauterize and medicate.
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille.
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres; et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	Now we have said or first chapter that every disease in which it is necessary to cauterize with fire, or with burning medicine, and the ointment and the causes and the instruments and the forms of cauterization; and I put this chapter from the head down to the toes, and I will speak of this chapter in the same way as we have found it more lightly in this way.
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	And thus, as I begin this chapter, it is necessary to say, my dear friend, that in this chapter there is more peril and fear than in all the previous cauteries, and for this reason it is necessary to take greater caution
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	For in the work of this chapter, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie.	And I advise you not to be rash
Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures.	For in various ways people come to cures.
si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice; et de ces doit on avoir paor.	For in various ways people come to cures. If they come from those who are so sick that they move easily from the disease through fear of the disease, and from the greatness of their malice; of these we must have fear.
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit: «atendez, je sui garis»; et li maladie est despitouse.	And of these there are some who make you understand, saying: "Wait, I am afraid"; and the disease is desperate
Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los; et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie; et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	I must only tell you that those who come to your aid in this way must be permitted; but put more great caution in your honor than in your covetousness, and do not fear me more foolishly than prudently from what you are certain, and what you have already taken and lost; and use prognostication and indication in the treatment of your patients so that salvation may be obtained, or converted; and this will help you to acquire good renown, glory, and memory for a long time.
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Very dear son, our Sirs, you must take good understanding and diligence, and if you yearn to be inspired by the holy inspiration of his hand, amen.
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	Or I have ordered this chapter in dividing by chapters, according to what is before or the chapter of cautery, that I have devised from the head to the toes, because you will find it more readily what you have to master.
dou chief plein d’aigue	Or I have commanded this chapter to be divided into chapters, according to what precedes or the chapter of cautery, that I have devised from the head to the toes, because you will more easily find what you have to learn.</start_of_turn>
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	The disease often comes out of the belly of a child, and when the bath is too hot the head of the child is strained; and never comes from a known cause except that one does not know it.</start_of_turn
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors; et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	And I never saw such a disease depart as quickly as in summer; and for all that I have seen, it is better to leave the work in parts rather than to risk it.
Et je vis .i. enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com .ij. nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	And I saw that in childhood, when the shoulder was dislocated, the head would swell up so much that it could not bear; and it was believed that the moisture was too great, and when it is gathered between the bone and the cartilage, between the shoulder and the bone; and when such moisture is between the shoulder and the bone, and the incision is small, that you must make a wide incision; and be as long as two fingers, until the moisture is gone.
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai .ij. fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	If the moisture is deeper and the incision is larger, if you make two incisions in the shape of a cross, according to this form:
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut: si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief .iij. fendures selonc ceste maniere:	If moisture is excessive on the bone, and you see the prominence of the chief over the lower part, and it is painful when you press it with your hand inwards, and it does not yield: if you suspect that the chief has fractured in two places, do as follows:
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers.	And after the incision, drain out all the moisture forcefully.
Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor; puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez. Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue; car aucune fois est elle devant; aucune fois derrier; aucune fois en destre; et aucune fois en senestre.	Another method of incision is to observe or open the prominence of the abscess, and the assembly of the pain; for it never faces forward; never backwards; never to the right; and never to the left.
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir; et warde que tu ne coper l’artere; et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor. de reume	When the shoulder or the armpit is open, and the filling of the water, and you do as you please with it; and beware that you do not cover the artery; and let the vein flow blood, so that the patient does not die from excessive bleeding and moisture discharge.
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les .ij. arteres.	When there is no known disease which is called "catarrh," and there is pus or a wound, and the disease is ancient, and the cure of medicine does not help, then the only cure is to cauterize with this that you cover the arteries.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief; aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout I drapel; puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues; puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de II pars, tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	It is necessary therefore, when you see the patient’s head displaced from its normal position, to massage the limb with a rough cloth until the arteries open; then extract the patient’s head from under the drape; then look to see if the vein is broken, and if the blood flows from both sides as far as the ears; and if so, restore them; then mark the place with a needle, and clip both ends with a pair of tweezers, until the size of the vein reaches the bone, which is about the width of the head.
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com .ij. dois au traver.	If you see, hold the sponge below the artery and grasp above, cutting as much as two fingers deep.</start_of_turn>
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	When the vein is cut, if blood spurts continuously, keep pressure on it without interruption.</start_of_turn>
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de III dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os; et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est VI c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins, selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere; puis regarde la plaie: s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	If the artery does not open on inspection, if you must, measure the amount of space of three fingers, then mark it and withdraw until you reach the bone; what is to be done is to put six fingers worth of pressure there, and sometimes more or less, according to what the patient can tolerate, and the refilling of the artery; then look at the wound: if it remains over the point of the spur, if the surrounding tissues are not pulsating, then strain the wound and bind it, and cure it with oil until it is healed.
de emigrainne	If the artery does not open on inspection, if you suspect it is obstructed by a foreign body, measure the distance of two finger-widths, then mark the spot and proceed until you reach bone.  If there is blood loss of more than a quarter, and sometimes less or more, according to what the patient can tolerate and the refilling of the artery, then look at the wound: if it remains over the point where the artery was opened, if the surrounding tissue does not swell, then strain the wound and bind it, and treat the wound with oil until it is healed.
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When ancient weeping comes, and acute catarrh, because of the moisture of tears and the phlegm in the temples and the ancient saliva weaken and similar things, it is cured by means of medical treatments and all that does not benefit it, if we extract the arteries of the temples and cauterize them, as we have said.</start_of_turn>
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit; et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement; puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	And thus is the method of extracting them [arrowheads] that if the patient causes the hair of his temples to recoil, and understands the artery which opens in the temple, for it opens well by its beating, and is not to be replaced more fiercely than in certain other men who are too cold; and if it is replaced, then the patient must hold his head back with some cloth, then wipe the area of any rough hair, and raise the area of water that is warm until the artery opens visibly; then take the sponge which is like this shape:
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie; et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des II chiés.	Then gently pull the skin away until you reach the artery, then pull it upwards as close as possible to the nails, and withdraw it well from the cloth that is below the armpit; if the artery is small, if the vein has a swelling at the shoulder, then close that part according to the quantity of two fingers.
Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	For if it is not securely held, if it does not leap without doubt in all things.
Et trai dou sanc des .vj. c/, jusc’a .iij.; et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en .ij. leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc; puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les .ij. liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez; et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	And thus is the method of extracting them that if the patient causes the hair of his temples to recoil, and understands the artery which opens in the temple, for it opens well by its beating, and is not to be replaced more fiercely than in certain other men who are too cold; and if it is replaced, then the patient must hold his head back with some cloth, then wipe the area of any rough hair, and raise the area of water that is warm until the artery opens visibly; then take the sponge which is like this shape: then gently pull the skin until you see the artery, then pull it upwards with pincers, and pull it out well of the cloth that is below the chest; and if the artery is fragile, if it has a blunt tip, then cut off that part according to the quantity of blood that is lost. For if it is not cut off, it will not jump out whole.
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors: por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	For the cautery is helpful to finish off moisture: because of this it is more useful against moisture.
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites; et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez; et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient; et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de .ij. pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	For the evacuation of arteries, one must fill the cavity with much cotton and put on well-made sponges; and when these are removed, if either dry medicines that cause the birth of hair, or sponges, are applied until they are healed; and if without a vein clip is done as you do with the work, if you hurry to cover with cautery, or if you use the hand of vitriol and strain it from your hand that it does not stain; and if you do not have this, if you must take away the hand, you must do so until it is frozen, and raise the hand of cold water until it stops, and strain as it should; and what is more tender and lighter in the evacuation of the vein is to cauterize the belly of this cautery trenching from a third part, but the trenching must be well spaced to prevent it from lasting longer.
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	For when the instrument is too tight, it holds less heat.
Et doit avoir entre les .ij. coutelz .i. doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les .ij. leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en .ij. leus; et soient esloigniet entre les .ij. chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	The fire must have between the joints of the handle a space of one inch; then when you have signed with the needle the bones, and you must let the loop of the burn be burning over until it comes up to the bone, and close the vein in one inch of bones; and let them be separated between the bones because it is not well soldered by this cautery in any way; and this is the form of the cautery:
des larmes	The fire must have between the joints of the handle a space of one inch; then when you have signed with the needle the bones, and you must let the loop of the burn be burning over until it comes up to the bone, and close the vein in one inch of bones; and let them be separated between the bones because it is not well soldered by this cautery in any way; and this is the form of the cautery: tears.
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis; et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	When the tears of the eyes are descending from the veins that are above the test of the chief of force, and it does no good any medical cure that is done to it, and you see the face of the patient to become swollen, and feel that the front of the body is limp as if with fear; and although they are tense and moist if the hair of paper is shed, and are scraped by the tears, and scorched by the heat of the tears, if there is any hope of this cure.
Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai III fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com II doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres II as II costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as II costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des II mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de III dois au traver joins; et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de II pars de coi ci est li forme:	For if it is not securely held, if it does not leap without doubt in all things. de l’estoupement des oreilles	From the swelling of the ears
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des .iiij. choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses. de l’estoupement des oreilles	From the swelling of the ears

de la gresle	De la gresle.

de la graisse des eulz	from the fat of the hairs
