Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then treat it as long as it is sane
Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it comes to opening an abscess, the cure of packing absorbs as much as it is possible while it is healthy.
des poilz des papieres	hair of papers</start_of_turn>
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc .iiij. manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When paper-like substances grow hair-like, other than their natural state, and are overgrown, if they prick at the eyes, they cause various diseases similar to tears and the softening of paper and gum, until it is the cause of the destruction of the eyes; and the cure is in three ways: either by complete fire cautery, or by medicine according to what is before or alongside the cautery, or by incision and stitching or by sutures, according to what I shall say.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout .i. fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai .i. fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai .i. fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	You must put the patient’s head in your left hand, and turn the paper of the oil to your right hand; if it is converted, that is good; but if not, if there is a needle at any one thread of the paper, either cut the margin of the paper or the hair will grow out from these hairs; and take one thread from below and pass it through the middle of the paper, and turn the paper with the needle; then make on the underside of the paper the paper of the hair, the hair that is overgrown, over the whole expanse, from the great tear to the little; then take out one thread, and put under the paper a little patch of cotton and bandage, and make on the paper a figure like a thrush’s beak, as much as you see the paper that is intended to be elevated.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor; et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	And if it comes to opening an abscess, the cure of packing absorbs as much as possible while it is healthy. If the skin has become softened due to a wound, then make a large incision two lines below the place of the wound, from the great toe to the heel; and if there is a fistula in the thickness of the flesh, insert the finger at the base of the hair, then draw up the surrounding tissue; then bring together the two layers with a suture of fine thread, and dry the wound, removing the excess thread from the two edges of the wound. If you see that it has healed, then leave the suture in place for three days or four; then cure the wound with dry and constricting things, for the wound will reunite itself at the base of the suture.
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	Then hold that which is above down with equal force according to the form which is mentioned above
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans; et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	And if you are unable to hold the teeth firmly, and the matter is not equal, take a needle or two, and pass one thread through the figure; and pass another thread loosely over the great limb, and the second thread loosely over the small one, and join the two threads together evenly; then steady your hand evenly, and steady all the skin over which you have marked, as we have said; and join the two layers of the wound together by stitching, and cure until it is healed; and if an abscess comes to your incision, if you apply cerate and other soothing poultices. Never has it happened that the hair of a wound has been converted: if you use what we have said concerning the incision; but the stitching in one and the other is more artificial.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai .ij. caines par art, et .ij. liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as .ij. chiés de .ij. pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les .ij. cainnes des .ij. parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	The cure for boils is as follows: convert the beard hair and leave it inside as I have said, then make three boils by art, and three threads as long as the beard and as wide as a palm; and put two threads of two parts or where you hold the hair; then assemble the one and the other securely over what rests on the beard oil, and strain the three boils of two parts forward; and leave it as it is for several days, and the skin that has been strained will rot and decay and will fester, until it heals by itself.
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If it is late, if the wound has great force, then cure until it is healed; and when the wound has healed and the arrow has been removed, the hair will no longer grow; and this is the form of two nails which you will make according to this figure and according to this quantity of length and width:
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute .i. fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse .i. autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a .i. ou .ij. ou .iij. ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	The work is such that you grasp a subtle needle, and there is in it a silken thread of silk and subtle; then gather the threads and know each one from the other subtly, and let the length of the threads be a palm of a long; then order in the chase another subtle thread of silk briefly, and do not tie the knots; then put the patient’s head in its place; and let there be a delay of the sun if the work is completed, for it is a subtle and small work, then withdraw the needle from all the chase at the root of the hair, and make it pierce in the papere hastingly as much as you can until you have treated as much of the hair as its natural position; then withdraw the hair until it comes back to the chase, and keep that hair which is there or two or three or more; then withdraw your hand until the vein has fled from all the chase in the papere with the natural position.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne .i. poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	If the chase is treated and the hair does not come out with it, if you draw out the chase to the end of the thread that you have ordered, until the chase vein comes out through the opening and you see it by the vision of the oil; then if you draw out the chase and the thread, close the oil and leave it closed for two or three days, until the hair has returned to its place and the burden has gone; and if the hair is small, if you accompany it with long nails of a natural kind, and be rid of it with that or leave it, until it is elongated and then leave it be.
de la porriture de l’oil	from the corruption of the oil
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	When this ailment called "aleacrati" or putrefaction arises from the oil, there are two ways: the natural one and the unnatural one.
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	And there may be from a wound, or a cut or burn, and from similar things.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	And the way of working in this is that you make the solder, dry the flesh, put in linen patches, and hold it until it is healed; and do not use anything but dry and restraining things in the treatment of this.</start_of_turn>
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	For if you do this, the disease will return worse than before; but there are things that soften, such as ruegerice; and alum or salt and linseed seeds boiled in any oil, and it surrounds a bandage, and treats this.</start_of_turn
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the treasure of your treatment is that you must take care that it does not heal differently from the way it was before; and this work that we have mentioned is not fierce except for addressing this disease, that it does not return differently from the way it was before.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	From the fire that comes in oil
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	This disease which is called "axacrati" in truth is natural and sudden.
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	The cause of this disease comes from wounds and cuts and burnings and similar things; and the way of the disease is that if you take an awl, because it has two files, and the file in the heel, and it makes split the sensitive marrow so that the vein bursts at two fingers of the heel; then the heel is elevated above the awl, and the pin is placed with one large spatula.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the limb returns to its proper position as it should be, that is good; but if not, if you take a saw and put it into the cut, and turn the limb, and make two incisions or break the bone inside the limb; and if two fingers of the two incisions are cut, or if you make an angle so that when they are put together, the limb is as well formed as a letter that has not a "G" at the top; then break that bone, according to the quantity of its cost and weight, of what is useful to the limb, and join the two broken ends together with a thread of silk; then heal from what we have said of the mollifying medicines and bandages, until it is healed
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les .ij. leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	And if the ailment comes from a fracture or sprain or burn, if you must make an incision, make it full through the hair of papers; then stretch between the two leaves of a tent, as I have said; and it must be done according to the form of the ailment, for it is diverse in form, and the wise masters perceive with great insight all sorts of things that must be done to return the limb to its natural shape; and the patient himself, according to what is to be done and the instruments in multiple positions.
dou soudement de la papiere	And if the ailment comes from a fracture or sprain or burn, if you must make an incision, make it full through the hair of papers; then stretch between the two leaves of a tent, as I have said; and it must be done according to the form of the ailment, for it is diverse in form, and the wise masters perceive with great insight all sorts of things that must be done to return the limb to its natural shape; and the patient himself, according to what is to be done and the instruments in multiple positions.
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	When this wound comes from a fracture at home in a part that is somewhat stiff as when the paper is sutured with white oil, and cannot move or do its natural works, if you must do so, then you must bite the point of a needle from the paper and keep it high; and hold as pinches, as long as you can bear the pain of the splinter, which is neither too great nor too deep, so that the patient does not suffer too much from the splinter and does not stain the oil; and make your incision, which you will stitch together, lightly, so that the paper returns to its natural shape; and all that is stitched together will be healed, and do not make use of strong water, but rather of sweet water and oil; and put between the paper and the oil a bandage of linen, and put on the oil wool in abundance; and after that put on a bandage and other things as much as necessary until it is healed.
de l’ungle de l’oil	De l’ungle de l’oil.
Saiches que li ungle est selonc .ij. manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a .i. dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	The pine oil has two qualities: it is nervous and somewhat soft like saffron, and another which is not very nervous but is like pale moisture congealed; when touched with iron and warmed, it does not burn; both of them resemble the greater part of the sperm, and they grow together so that they cover the whole cavity and the light and movement of the pine oil.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met .i. poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et .i. fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	And as for the incision, if the patient places his head in its proper position, then hold the eyes; then grasp the oil with your hand, and with a needle pierce the base of the hair; then take a needle, and put one hair of a horse, or of a mare, or of a bull, and one strong thread; and double the point of the needle a little and fix it with the oil, and pierce through the entire needle, and tie the oil with a thread and stretch it out, and drain from all around the oil the cost of the oil which nourishes the hair and the silk up to the root, and cut away all the remaining root with little forces, and leave the natural oil or the secretion, if there is no discharge of tears usually from the incision; and in no way should the oil be stretched only by the ointment and the thread, as we have said; then drain away all the surrounding fat so that this is the shape:
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	And keep that the sponge does not touch the fleshy part and breaks it, and that the needle does not pierce; and after the incision, pour in oil a spoonful of bruised salve, and sprinkle over it some laudanum, and leave it until the other side; then cure what is caused by that until it is healed.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	And if the nail is not nervous, and you cannot push out the needle, and the thread does not enter, many times this is cured by the semblance of a nail of medicine; and as I have said in the division, if you see it covered, if you see the oil of the patient, take the sponge lightly as much as necessary according to this form:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	And remove the nail silently, and if you see that it has diminished point and the bone is pressed, if you distill from your mouth into the oil laudanum made of laudanum and red ochre and bruised salve, and squeeze out the oil until the other side; then repeat the other work according to this same work, until it is completely healed.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If nothing hinders you, if like an abscess you have post-surgery, then milk should be withheld and first cure the abscess thoroughly until it has healed, and then resume the work as before, until it has healed.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne; puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	And if during the oil bath there appears soft tissue swelling at night, if you suspend it with an ointment and cut off a part and not all, that tears of marrow will not arise; then distill with the red colocynth oil which is made from litharge.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	from the hair that grows on the navel
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste; et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force; puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tu ne bleces l’oil a l’ovraige; et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre; et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut; et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut; puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	The hairs must grow long and even; if they prick at their root, keep the eyes steady until they grow.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil; et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer; et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	However, it is necessary that you feed the treatment with a weak oil from the natural way; and from an accident, in the work of iron; and do not touch your hand in any of these works until you see that this limb is suffering from that work.
des voines des eulz	From the veins of the eyes
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors.	The veins are red ones that are covered in oil, and they tolerate the gaze of the eye and disclose the oil throughout the days.
Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel; adonques le coil en teil maniere: comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	The master should first look at the oil, for if it is strong, then it is enough, and there is no other disease more fierce than melancholy; therefore the doctor must be skilled: instruct the patient to put his head in order, then suspend the veins all around as he is learned, and let the incisions be double as in this form:
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en .i. cors selonc ceste forme:	and be doubled superficially by degrees in a circle according to this form:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	and suspend them superficially twice by degrees in a circle according to this form; then withdraw the forces of those veins superficially, and wipe away the blood hour after hour until you see the veins freed from the fat; and keep that you do not burn the oil with the tips of your fingers, and do this work at noon before the sun, and be very thirsty during your work if you do not accomplish that the veins will not recover.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme des forces:	If you cannot firmly grasp all that in this hour, make a plaster on the oil of soothing things to calm the eye pain, and leave it until the pain is soothed and is secure from after-pain; then start again in the same manner as before until you are healed; and this is the form of strength.
de la fistule de l’oil	If you cannot firmly grasp all that is in this hour, make a plaster on the oil of soothing things to calm the eye pain, and leave it until the pain is soothed and is secure from after-pain; then start again in the same manner as before until you are healed; and this is the form of strength.
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	If you cannot firmly grasp all that is in this hour, make a plaster on the oil of soothing things to calm the eye pain, and leave it until the pain is soothed and is secure from after-pain; then start again in the same manner as before until you are healed; and this is the form of strength.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a .i. chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And when the bone is broken, and you see corruption and blackness, if the limb has all the signs, it is called "aspire chief," and should be made of ivory or a piece of bone resembling a lime in shape.
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	When the corrupted limb hangs down, then put your hand over it and press down until you feel the corruption is gone; do this only once, then restore the limb to the medicine.</start_of_turn>
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi XL jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent I foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a III angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	If the limb is swollen and a swelling has appeared, and the bone of the limb is swollen and remains for forty days, and does not heal and is not incisioned, and other evils do not come, except to bring the fistula to the surface as it should be done according to this form: uncover the bone a second time with iron, and with strong medicines, and when it has been uncovered take hold of the limb according to this form, and let the incision be triangular, and the wound should be narrowed until it reaches the head as you see here.
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil I poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et pues restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	Then put your thumb on the bone below the elbow, and wipe away the oil with your hand, then pull your hand back to the end until it breaks the bone and the patient feels it through what comes into the hole if he keeps his hand on his elbow; and when the bone is restored and hardened, if there is matter in the elbow, if it is less burdensome for the patient.
de l’issue de l’oil	Then place your thumb on the bone below the armpit, and wipe your hand with oil. Indeed, once you have grasped the whole forearm, pull it until it pierces the bone and the patient will feel it through what comes into being at that moment if he holds his hand on his elbow. Then restore the dry medicine, as I have taught you, and when the wound has healed and hardened, if there is anything that troubles the elbow; if it is less serious for the patient.
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil .i. liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en .iiij., et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the skin is open for a long time without causing any discomfort, no reduction, if you tie up the patient; then do the same, put on compresses or soak in oil, and then apply oil with acaice, aloe, incense, and sarcocoll, and then strain the oil, and put it on pads and cloths; and keep the cloths if you take cloths enough soft, and double gauze in threes, and then put one on top of the other according to the quantity of blood there is between them; then strain by means of a bandaging bandage forms, and restart the compresses soaking in the direction of the wound; then tighten the compresses and leave the oil strained for a day and night, and if the swelling subsides, if you strain it out of the mouth; then tighten the dressing after the swelling and the nut, and if you see the oil returning, that is good; if not, repeat the dressing and the cloths and the dressing and the compresses until it is healed.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	Dou derrompement de toile uvee.
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com .i. grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait .i. fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When the head of the shoulder is dislocated due to moisture, then open the joint, and bring forth pieces of paper like barley grains; it is expected to see; accordingly if you see that, bite the needle at the root of the bone up to this very point, then insert another needle or there is double thread of the limb; and make it pierce, and leave the first needle as it lies; then tighten the double thread and hold the limb firmly, then pull out the needle and put on absorbent oil cloth liberally; and leave it until the thread has bled out; then cure the oil with comforting things until the wound is healed; and no time is the wound restricted by the callous part of a circle of silk, until it is healed.

And if the wound shows great swelling, if you pierce the sensitive part which comes from the middle of the oil, and correct the moistness of the abscess and bring down the swelling, and enter in between to that extent; then pull it out when it is healed.
de la bowe de l’oil	De la bowe de l’oil.
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	This disease called "alcunnati" is not fierce but resembles a wound descending, which is not true; and the manner in which it appears is that you make the patient sit on a comfortable and straight chair, then take hold of his head with your hands two parts apart, and move it until you see the wound coming down towards your eyes; then either bind it tightly and do not loosen it, or break the light, and see the patient's condition as he alone knows; and if it does not drain out, consider it to be severe, for if the wound descends and is not apparent as we have said.
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If you make the patient sit between your hands, then take the sponge and put it on the horny patch I with the continuation of the conjunctiva with the horny patch and the crown, as long as the boil is there; and when it comes out, distill in hot water mixed with honey, or in vinegar or fenugreek boiled and honey, then let it be cured by another treatment until it is healed.
des aigues de l’oil	from the bowl of the oil
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit.	We have seen similar things in the division of the bowels, and this is what it is necessary to pierce; if in this case according to the sanctity.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	You must make the patient sit between your crossed hands, expose the light from the sun, and anoint with holy oil; then take the thumb of your left hand if the boil is on your left side, or your right thumb if the boil is on your right side; then take in your right hand, if the boil is on your left side, the instrument which is called the “almagda”, or in your left hand, if the boil is on your right side; then put the point of the instrument at the crown of the boil by the thickness of a barleycorn at the edge of the oily part of the larger tear, and hold the instrument called “almagda” effectively, and restore your hand until it pierces the oily blench, and feel that the “almagda” has come to the empty thing; and it is necessary that the measure of the “almagda” be equal to the measure of the space from the prunelet up to the black spot; and that is the crown of the oil; if you see the bone in that paper by the clarity of the horny patch, and then put the instrument until it is level or the liquid is, then press the oil from the wound afterwards.
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	If the pain increases now, if you see the patient before him and the instrument in his eye.
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	After a little rest, if the pain recurs through the second way, put the force with the instrument, and when it is firmly fixed and does not rise, if it is a wound, grasp gently around your hand and hand; and then remount the wound slightly, and release the oil from the eye.
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	Then put by force oil-soaked tampons or soaked cloth in rose oil and plenty of eggs, and tie with clean oil.
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	Yes, and those who are of our household, put on common broth with plenty of eggs.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if the almagda cannot enter the oil by its hardness, because there are parts of bones that have too many hairs, it is recommended that you take the instrument which is called the “alberit,” which is like this in shape:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	And pierce only the conjunctiva slightly, and do not go too deep, but make it firm, then put in the thumb, as we have said; and when the work is finished appears to the patient the dorming attendant, who sleeps on his back in the dark; and let him have light meals, and do not move his head to the right or to the left, and keep him still as much as possible; then take him out of this house, and let him spit out his tongue, and do not let him do anything, and then put him back in his place for seven days; and do not make him do anything in the meantime of the cure or after the incision now, but it is necessary that you feed him, because he has become painful.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	Leave the oil loose before the seventh hour, and hold the eye steady of that which soothes the abscess; and when it is calmed, withdraw the eye and put upon its face a little ointment to cover the eye, and keep it in that dark place.
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	Then go out of the house for a while, and in its place be converted in these matters; and towels that no disciple must interfere with in this case
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And one came to us from the Yrach who told us that in their land they often saw a wound that bled when it was at peace, but he never saw anyone in our land or read about it in the books of the ancients; and it is a new thing to us.

Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en .iij. angles ague.	And their heads are of this same subtlety, and their backs in two angles like an eagle.</start_of_turn>
de la char sor le neis	From the shoulder joint downwards to the hand.
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	Never do hair or nails of various sorts grow or swell like scorpions at the mouth of a beast; and if there are such things or if there is swelling of bone of a pale color, or if there is swelling of marrow of a reddish color
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	In those things of which there is swelling of marrow and it does not swell, then make the patient sit between your hands facing the sun; cover his nose, and vomit over those things, and drive away; for in that way you will support the subtle pain of the spleen until you know that that swelling is all bone.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout .i. des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	If there remains nothing more to do, if the opening has reached its utmost extent, and if nothing remains fixed; and if without being sutured, or with only slight sutures, if the wound persists; or if it is suspected that the wound is infected, or if the infection is malignant, then hasten and cauterize immediately until the surrounding tissue is no longer stained and all the pus has drained away. Then throw away or drain the wound with ease and without delay, with wine or vinegar.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	If he does not work, and moisture comes up to his throat, he swallows that which is sane; if moisture does not pierce as it should, that which is in the marrow above the bone becomes loose, because the instruments do not come through to break it: therefore it is necessary that you put in a large thread and grasp it with your hands, and leave between each knot no space more or less; and put the patient’s head on the thread at the front, and treat with odor until it comes out through the mouth; and many times they do this to children, and it is a light thing for one who has seen it done; then hold the chief which comes through the throat with one hand, and the other chief which comes through the mouth with the other hand, and pull the one after the other until they reach us who are holding.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait .i. mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And let it be of silver or gold, resembling a large lamp, if like a cord, and guide it thus; and if you see it, make a closed loop, and let the instrument be flat for evacuating the thumb; and hold the thumb of the thumb with one hand when warming the oil or no liquid.
de la char sor le neis	From the shoulder joint downwards to the hand.
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Many times there arises at the head of the arm a disease which is called "telul", and it increases and becomes great again, so that it is visible; and for this reason it is necessary that you immediately take hold of the beginning, and break the bone, then take out the cautery or the burning medicine; and if you wait too long to take hold of it when it is great, if you take hold of it with force, you will cause great harm to the patient; and if the abscess is of soft touch, not of color, and you see that you can take hold of it, you must evacuate the patient and take hold of it without fear, and cure the limb with dry things and restrictions.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	when the arm is cut and bound.
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	Do as much as you know until you sense that the hair has not been corrupted; then draw the thread, wipe the blood, and moisten the thread in Egyptian fashion, and reattach it as before; do this for three days or more, until the hair has consumed all that remains of the char; and then put on or remove a cauterizing bougie for a few days as long as it remains sound, and if there is a need for sedative medicines, if necessary; and this is the form of the instrument for extracting the head, from which we distill the oils and medicines or not.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	If there is no sign of infection in the wound, when it is fresh throughout, then join the two layers of skin with a suture, and cure until it is healed.  If the layers are already separated at one end and the other, if you can, support all the parts around the wound until they have healed, then reassemble the two layers of skin with a suture, and strain, and sprinkle with powdered dragon’s blood, and incense.  Put on a piece of strong or other absorbent dressing over the powder, and leave it until it stops bleeding by itself, then cure until it is healed.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The manner of the costure is that you assemble the solution: or by needles, as we have said in the costure of the belly; or by thread, as I have told you.</start_of_turn>
des apostemes des levres	of the separation of the layers of the skin.
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	At home in the hands, there are many veins that are like dense brushwood, somewhat like barley grains, smaller and larger; therefore, if you tear the veins, and make incisions on each nodule, and grasp them with tweezers and hold them in place; then after the incision of the vitriole broiet, until it is no longer stained; and then withdraw the needle easily, and cure the limb of dry things until it is healed.
de la char des gencives	From the roots of the gums.
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Many times blood appears on the gums of those who have bad breath; they call it "albulus"; if you support it with your teeth, and grasp it at its root, and let the blood drain away or evacuate; then withdraw the needle of the broiet, or other astringent and drying powders; and if the gum comes out again after the incision, and this happens many times, if you grasp it a second time and cauterize it: if it does not come out after the cautery; these are the forms of the instruments for covering.
des sordens	Des sordens.
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	Sometimes the teeth are gathered at the root of the jaw, between the gums, which are loose and jagged; and never are the teeth black and yellow and curved, until the corruption comes to the gum, and they are biting; if it is to be believed that you make the patient sit between your hands, and his neck be in your saint, and open the jaws or the gums open, until there remains nothing; and thus do black bile and green bile, and yellow bile and other humors, until they are dissolved; and if one has removed what is at the root at the first attempt, that is good; if that is not the case, if you must repeat the process a second and a third time, until you have done everything; and the teeth that have mixed with various forms of instruments to remove them, according to what the work shows, for those that remove the teeth have other forms than those that are between the teeth; and these forms and others appear with you.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	It is necessary when you cure the tooth from its pain that you wait a while before retracting too much, because this must not be done carelessly; for it is a viscous substance so that we have no excuse for neglecting to remove it.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	Therefore, when the patient is unable to bear pain, if you are certain that he can endure it.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Many times the patient complains of pain, but often this is either false or mild, and he forces the limb to move; and in no way does the pain depart until the malady is cured, for we have already had experience of this with many; and when you are quite certain that he can endure it, if you can, support the limb firmly to prevent all movement; then move the limb forward and backward a little at first, until it is well established, and then firmly bind it.  Let the patient’s pain be gentle between your thighs, and hold it firmly in place so that it does not move again
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	After that, if the tooth sticks directly forward, and if it does not jump up, take no one of these instruments and hold it loosely in the cheek; and move it as you did before.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	And if it is perceived that the tooth has penetrated and is gaping, if it is necessary, cover it with cloths, lace or pierce it; and if you grasp it too tightly, it will break when grasping; and it is necessary to move smoothly over the gum to extract the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	Take care that you do not break it, and leave some of it, and return to the patient with the greater pain of the first time
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	Be aware that you must not act carelessly like the ignorant layman, who often break bones without reason and without purpose; but you must not neglect the cause of this great disease caused by roots which remain embedded, or by the fracture itself, as we have often seen; and when the tooth is extracted, wash the wound with wine or vinegar and oil; and if there is bleeding, which often happens, apply pressure with a piece of vitriol sponge; and if that does not suffice, cauterize it
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The forms of instruments, that is to say without a sound, must first be long pointed and broad-handed; and they must not double when you draw the tooth.
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And be of large members if they do not bend when drawing, and be made of iron indeed well, and be toothless so that they may be held by hand
de la racine des dens	from the root of the tooth.
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	When the root remains stuck at the back, if you must bring out the moist cotton plug from the wound I or II,
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	as long as the limb is limp, since the teeth of the clamp which are left behind are called “algefri,” so that the head of the shoulder appears like a beak of a vulture; and be made in the same way as with a file, and that is the form:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	If the roots do not suffice to support all these tensions, then it is recommended that you uncover the bark entirely around the root, and place the instrument called «althali», which is to say a palainche, since this is its form:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	If it is strong and large so that it does not break me, and if the root jumps by this means, it is good; if not, support all the instruments, since their forms will come afterwards.
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait .ij. rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if one uses this instrument which has teeth, since this is its form:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	And other instruments that are before in the ratio of the teeth, and this instrument which appears like a great clamp, of which this is the form:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And other instruments which precede in the ratio of the teeth, and this instrument which appears like a great clamp, of which this is the form: if it is too strong to break, and the teeth that mouth instruments of teeth; and with other instruments which are not mentioned; and the chief surgeon will discover by himself the instrument which is suitable for each case, for there are many diseases where the former did not teach any instrument because of the variety of things. And if it breaks not by force of hand or of other bones, or if there is doubt, if it seeks other instruments which are worthy, as I have said, and which will aid by gestures, for this is the form:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And be great and firm to hold the bone, that it does not escape, but can hold and restrain; and then restore the limb of medicine suitable for this, and if there is decay in the bone, and it is small, if the limb has all these instruments:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a .i. petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When teeth emerge contrary to their natural course, and the form is awkward, even in women of gentle birth, if you suspect that their root is enclosed and cannot emerge naturally, and is not in its proper place, neither can it be relieved or comforted: then extract it. And if it is affected with the tooth, take hold of this instrument which has a similar shape, like a small beak, and which may be of iron without a cutting edge on top.
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And when the tooth persists in the gums and hands are clasped for a long time due to the duration of the tooth, and because you do not move the others, if it appears, it can be limed, if you use a file of the same shape as the tooth itself
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	And it is also like when we make nails; and when you file the tooth persistently and gently in the hands, if it does not move much, then at the end of the filing there will be no scraper, and if the root is too deep and it bites the tongue, if you do not file the sharpness until it is even, it will bite the tongue and corrupt the speech.
quant li dent lochent	When the tooth is loose.
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	When the front teeth loosen, by percussion or by pressure, and the patient cannot bear anything that touches them without groaning, and you must cure them with restrictive medicines, which is of no use; if you must restrain them with a gold wire, for the silver wire becomes green and corrupts, but the bone does not move; and let the wire be neither too thick nor too thin, according to the quantity of space between the teeth; and if you see the teeth shifting, if you take hold of the wire and double it between the two front teeth, then put the head of the shoulder between the other teeth, as many as there are, until you see it clearly up to the sound tooth on the other side; and then repeat the covering up to the part where you began, and strain your hand skillfully and cautiously, until it does not move; and let the ligament be fixed to the root of the tooth if it does not escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	Then grasp the head of the arm with one hand, and assemble the bones, and put them back between the sound teeth, and hold them so that they do not slip; and then leave them as tight as possible, so that if they should slip, or the thread should break, from the strain of another thread; if it should remain and serve its purpose, that is the form of wisdom and the manner of addressing the two front teeth, and the two lower teeth, as you see.
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	When the tooth aches, if you put it back in its place, fresh from fresh, as we have said; and let nothing intervene but what is wise and soothing, and never make its form like that of a tooth of whalebone, and put it in its place where the defect is, and strain it as we have said, and hold it firmly and serve for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	De coper, lou liien de la lengue.
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	In no case does the thread come from the tongue or nature itself, that we are born without; or by chance of a deep wound; the work is such that you must offer the mouth of the patient, and put your thumb in his teeth, and hold the tongue; then grasp the large nerve as much as the tongue is dislocated from its dwelling place, and if it persists or not, and that is the sign of a wound, if it breaks and grasps the thread; and keep that the wound is not too deep, for the artery that is from the tongue; and when you have done this, if you lift the pale or reddish liquid, or cold liquid, and put the tongue in, make a slight tension of the thread; and hold the patient’s hand firmly at night, so that it cannot recover.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	And if blood spurts out, if you do not move quickly, if you cauterize with the lentiginous cautery, which is good for this; then cure him of another cure until he is healed.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see pus, colored or black or hard, if the patient does not feel it, do not touch it, for it is a fistula; and if it is declining and there is moisture, if it is spitting blood, and you pull out the clot, and make a small incision, and deliver from both sides; and if it does not go away from your work, if you put a broken glass piece over it until it is stained, and then return to your work until you have finished everything; then lift the pale and cold liquid, and cure as necessary until it is healed.
des apostemes de la gorge	Des apostemes de la gorge.
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	Blood sometimes comes out of the throat, which is called "godath", and these are properly the two almonds; and when you cure them, as we have said previously, and they are not healed, take care: if they are abscesses of small size and of a yellow hue, do not touch them with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	And if it is red and the root is large, if you do not touch it with iron, even though it is bleeding; but you leave it until it stops bleeding by itself. Then you will remove it, or it will burst by itself; and if it is white in color and the root is slender, if you have seen the instrument to cover it, but first look to see if the abscess is settled and calm
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Therefore make the patient sit before the sun, and his head be still, and hold his mouth shut and grasp his thumbs between his hands, and press his tongue down to the utmost, as it is the form; and let it be of silver or gold as thin as needles.
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	... Press his tongue downwards with all the instrument, and you see the clot, take the sponge and press it into the clot, and pull it out above more than you wish; and do not put anything of the cloths on it, then place the bandage over the instrument, as is the form, which seems like a force; and all the time the chief is bent, and one place over another, and is very painful, and is made of iron inde or tin.
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument, if you can hold the wound tight, for this is the fashion:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les .ij. amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les .ij. amandres igament.	And if you do not have this instrument, if you can hold the wound tight, for this is the fashion: grasp the thumb and index finger of the hand which you will not incision, and when you have grasped one of the nails, grasp the other in the same way, and after the incision gargle the patient with hot water, hot and easy, and when the blood has drained out, if there is still blood in the wound, or blood clots like pomegranate seeds are cooked, or wormwood, or similar things, until the wound is clean; then close the wound when it is healed; and never again does blood appear in the throat except for the two nails, if you grasp them just as before.</start_of_turn>
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	And I treated a woman with an abscess that was not opening in the throat, that is to say it was a small abscess; and I held her throat very close, so that the woman could not breathe through the passage that was blocked, and could not eat or drink, and she died if she remained so for a day or two.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscess was so large that it had forced out two stones through the two holes of the neck
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.
