I had drunk much wine and eaten heartily; I was lying in one place when suddenly a fierce fire broke out, and in its wake a great portion of my bow was consumed; then I rolled over to the other side of the house where I found the mouth closed and the tongue pressed; afterwards I rolled over onto those abscesses, grasped one part and did not release it until a little blood escaped; and when I had loosened the lead from the throat, the woman who had been accompanying me recommenced to drink water and wine, and did not cease biting that abscess ever since; and the abscesses reappeared as before, filling the house as much as I could bear; then I bound them and cauterized them inside the throat: since then I have no sense of taste; and I departed from those parts, and only God knows what happened to me after that.
de l’uve	De l’uve.
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	When the limb descends to the glen, and it is fleeing and is long, if it is called "perpendicular"; and if it is broad and rounded, it is called "glen.
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	When it is cured as we have said in the division, and the cure does not profit, and you see that the postulations are appeased, and it is subtle, so you must cover it; and that which is rounded and not long; and that is bloody or of yellow or black colour, so you must avoid the incision of the latter
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great peril for the patient.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	Therefore, when you see it, as I have said, according to the manner that I have mentioned, you must set the patient before the sun and press the tongue with the instrument that we mentioned before; then hold the ointment in the glen, and pull it out, and close it with two instruments that I have mentioned in the incision of the two thumbs
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And you must not cover more than the excess which is beyond the natural limit; for if you do more, you will grieve the voice and the word; and after the incision, use what we have said concerning the incision of the two almonds, and cure it until it is healed.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient has fear of covering, you must know that you must use an engine in the cautery in the direction of the fear.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	And the manner of the cautery if it is acute is harsh and severe
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	And that the patient puts his head in his sound, and then presses the tongue to the instrument that we have said or the treatise of the cautery, and grasp with sharp scissors, if it is neither too thick nor too clear; and make use of the handle of this instrument, for thus is the form:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés .iiij. jors ou .v. Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	From the navel.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en .i. pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait .i. estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This cure is more secure than incision, for it is cured by fumigation according to this method. Take calamine and isospicum and origanum and rue and chamomile and avronne and similar herbs, and assemble all or some of them in a pot, and put in oil, and boil. And let the pot be well sealed with strong earth, and mix in the pot one instrument which is chevet according to this method.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	And whether of silver or gold, or whether one of the things be struck into the mouth of the patient as long as the vapor mounts up to the eye by the caustic, as long as the eye be mortified; afterwards it must be repeated often, as long as the eye dries, and keep that you do not do this at the beginning of the eruption of the caustic, because many things happen; do not make me do this except for the subsidence of the caustic.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And if this instrument is not present, if you take a caustic and put into the chief of the patient an eggcup of vinegar, so that the patient’s mouth does not become too hot; for the eggcup of vinegar does not make the vapor grow in the mouth, and this is a good cure in all respects.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou .i. morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge .i. fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren .i. estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Many times it has happened to the throat bone or a fish spine, or nothing; if you therefore think that you must do what you see, and press the tongue to the sun with all the instrument, so that you see the thing; and what does not appear to you and is returned in the throat, you must make the patient vomit the ailment as soon as the meat is cooked in the stomach; by chance if it is expelled by vomiting; or the patient swallows a piece of sponge, or a piece of navel, or a lettuce root, or a piece of dry bread; and bind the sponge with one thread, and then transfix it. And when it comes back, if it is expelled, and then you must draw out; and if it does not come out by this, take one instrument of sponge according to this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And let the tongue rest curved at the root if it can more easily enter the throat, and lift the head up; and guard that you do not touch the epiglottis, that all do not live, do not push the bone inwards; and must that the patient hold the instrument, because it is either moved or the matter is disturbed; if the epiglottis is swallowed, or he forces it out with all the instrument equally, as much as he is able.
de la sansue de la gorge	And let the tongue rest curved at the root if it can more easily enter the throat, and lift the head up; and guard that you do not touch the epiglottis, that all do not live, do not push the bone inwards; and must that the patient hold the instrument, because it is either moved or the matter is disturbed; if the epiglottis is swallowed, or he forces it out with all the instrument equally, as much as he is able.
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	Medicine is never without its risks, as I have said in the preceding division, by the treatment of medicines; and when this does not help, look at the patient’s throat in the sunlight, and then press the tongue to the instrument that I have mentioned
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	And if you see the limb without support, if it has a slight twist or subtle tension that persists.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	If this is not the case, take a needle and pierce the patient’s throat, then insert or pull out the needle with the cautery, and do this often.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	If the patient suffers from acute pain throughout.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	Then take a cold compress, cover the mouth and move the tongue forward and backward; do this frequently; if the patient groans with pain, stop immediately
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	If this does not help, if you suspect the patient has an aversion to safety, give him an aspergillum of asafoetida, with the instrument I mentioned in the fumigation of the eye; do this often, for it will be of great benefit
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	And thus the method of fumigation is this: if you take a pot or it has charcoal within, let the cover be spread over a coverlet perceived in the middle, and in that hole let the head of the instrument be; then pour the fumigation and the patient puts his chin in his mouth, closes his mouth, so that the fumes do not escape, but go up to the nostrils; and the nostrils will now sneeze, and if they do not sneeze, repeat the fumigation many times; and the patient will suffer thirst, eat dirty and foul things, and drink no water; and then he will surely vomit as a consequence of this government.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the form of the instrument is like this, which we use for the treatment of the eye; if one can see it, it is like tongs with curved handles to enter the throat; and it has a beak like a feather, and there is lime on it, so that whatever it grasps, it will not let go; and when you have made this form:
li chapistres des apostemes	it is possible to move forward with the following instructions:
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	Symptoms resembling abscesses are, as it is remembered from one place to another in this book, diverse in perforation and size; and there are two ways in which they occur, one of which is in their own image, and the other when moisture is present.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second method if the limb is hanging loose or fixed to the bone.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	for the swelling of the head is different from that of the bone, and the swelling of the limb is different from that which comes at the joints, and the flesh itself judges in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	and if the swelling does not disappear, we must not pierce it until the bone is dead according to its completeness; and if there are such things that we must pierce when they are raw, and they do not die according to their completeness, like swelling which is beyond the joints
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	for when the swelling comes from the joints, and we leave it as long as it is stiff, by chance if the bone and the nerve of the joint are corrupted, because of this there is contraction in that limb.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	Or the incision is made from the principal part of the limb; and if you delay the perforation until it is medium, it will go to the principal limb; or it is made from the root, if you do not perceive that it is medium; and one must only pierce the principal wound in a straight line with the digestion accompanying it, without that which is made from the root, which must not be pulled out, but must be along, and there will arise an fistula; and it will not heal in great extent.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And it is recommended that you wash the wound of the perforation of the wound that is dead according to its completion, when the pain is calmed, and the disappearance of fever, and the fading of pain and redness, and doubt and tingling of the head of the wound, and other signs; and that you make the perforation or more dependent on the wound, and the place where it opens. And let the perforation be long enough for the hand or foot, or for the joints and nerves and arteries, and for all the bones or if there is no swelling.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	In these cases, according to the location of that limb.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when the wound is open in flesh, if you do not perceive that it is confirmed in digestion accompanying it, as we have said
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	For if you pierce it before that, if there is along the edge of the wound a piece of the vein of the limb, and it is full of bad blood; and by chance you tighten the flesh and perforate it again.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And if there is no wound perceived according to the large wound mark, according to what the limb has suffered.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	And you must bring in small wounds, small holes; and in large wounds, large holes, and many cuts according to the size of the wound mark; and if there are such wounds or you must keep the hand steady, and cover; when it is already become like draping, and is softened, if you must do like we do with boils: and if there are such as are cleft in three angles, and such as we must cover like a nutmeg seed, like wounds; and if there are such as we make a circle size, and other sizes and similar covering.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	He who has no head, if there is a superficial wound, must pierce it completely; and you must pierce when the wound is great, and there is great swelling, and you must pierce, if you do not remove all the swelling in that hour, but only a part; then stamp the wound until the swelling has gone down, then do not touch anything again; do this many times until the swelling is gone; even if the patient is of weak virtue, or a woman in labor, or a young child, or an old man decrepit.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Eschew this chapter with great caution, and when you have perceived the wound, if it is small, observe whether the wound of the abscess is slight; and if it is a large abscess and there is much pus, if you fear that the abscess will rupture, bite in the middle of the abscess so that it comes together; and if you have grasped the abscess with a part of leather and have closed it in a knot, if you fear that it will burst, fill it with coarse wool or flaxseed from the root of linen towards the top; then the bone, and bind it until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if blood evacuates from your work, if you fear cold and ease, and moistness I drape, and take out the decorative limb many times.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If blood continues to flow, if there is governance and treatment, and the powders I have mentioned in this book are present, and if the wound is open or tense, or if the leus or apostemes are soft and nervous, if you must attempt to stop the bleeding, you must put on tight bandages soaked in wine and oil; and if it is evening, and the leus is fleshy, if you must, put on tight bandages soaked in water and oil, or in wine and oil, until three-fourths of an hour has passed, as we have said; and then remove the bandage and dry and treat the wound, as it is possible, until it is healed.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And this knowledge is sufficient for the treatment of abscesses: as you have said previously concerning the precautions before treating abscesses, and thus is this chapter.
des soros	And this knowledge is sufficient for the treatment of abscesses: as you have said previously concerning the precautions before treating abscesses, and thus is this chapter.
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	Or if small abscesses come out, and they are like those that are in towels, thus as the juice of a gooseberry, and there is resemblance in them.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	There are fat people and those who have moisture in the armpits; and if there are such ones who are hard and rough at the armpit, and there is no doubt if the artery does not make resistance.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And as for the work of the surgeon, if you suspect that everything that is called "entromissor" has come out, which thing contains what, etc.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	For if it contains moisture, it remains for a long time
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	And when the moisture is evacuated, do not leave the peel that contains that moisture, because it returns when nothing is left; then put cotton in Egyptian fashion, if it is present; if not, in water and oil, and apply the bandage, and leave it until the other side heals; and that will correct what is remaining that is delayed
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And thus when the cotton is renewed, as before, the second time, and the third, until you are certain that it has not been displaced at night; then cure the wound appropriately, as is proper.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	And if the abscess remains firm at night, if you follow this form, long; and let your ointment flow, and the eschar of all parts, and put all your care to draw out the clot or where it lies; and if the artery opposes you, do what I have told you afterwards.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And do the same with an abscess that is pierced, and cut and cure as I have told you
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And the size of the pierced abscess and the moisture, if it is less severe, because they are of little blood.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	And if in any of these abscesses or swellings or if there is no moisture, and if these are old abscesses that I cauterize or swellings from a woman of easy virtue; and I find the abscess just like a hard stone, rough and white, and cannot break it; and if no harm has been done, it is just as well to make an incision as if it were a stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	In other abscesses that come from the head of the shoulder and from the root of the ear, because these arise from the swelling of the limb and the loosening of the flesh; cure them as it seems convenient.</start_of_turn>
des scrophules	And the size on the pierced wound and the moisture, if it is less severe, because they are of little blood. And if there are some of these wounds or chieftains or it has no moisture, and of those wounds which I cauterize or chieftain from an old woman; and find the wound just like a hard stone, rough and white, and cannot break it; and if no blood comes out, it is just as well to make a wound like a stone. In other wounds that come from chieftains and have roots of ears, it overturns if it is kept too long, for it makes the wound worse. And it cures as it should.
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	Often these abscesses occur at the collarbone, and the armpits, and in the groin, and never elsewhere or on the bones, and are bloody, and are joined together.</start_of_turn
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	And if a scrophule is properly within its sheath, as when it has not burst and is incisoned at the head; and the semblance of these scrophules is often seen.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	There are also cases where the body contains moisture, and if there are maligns that do not wish to obey health.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	In that case where you see a bone in a good position at the touch, and that looks like the color of flesh, and is soft from one side and not hollow as from the ear, the artery or the vein, and is not deep; if you must remove it, you must cut off the soft part, and if two thumbs are sufficient, as we have said in incisions at the head; and the blood flows back and forth, and so be careful that you do not cover the nerve or the vein, and do not cause excessive bleeding, for the hands will escape, and do not speak too loudly, for you must not cover anything that you should not
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	And if thou copest the vein or artery, and this leaveth thee unable to work, if thou put in the wound a piece of vitriol broth, or any powder that remaineth bloodless, and restrainest the wound; and leave it until the swelling be appeased, and the wound be softened, and begin to carry on.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	And when the swelling is gone, if thou returnest to thy work, until thou hast completed it; then if thou must know whether it doth stay or no, if there be any small scabs, if thou dost cope and grind them.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if there is in the root of the swelling great pain, if thou canst not but cope that swelling at its root, but bind it with a strong double thread, and leave it hanging loose; then use the wound of white cotton plugged in Egyptian fashion, and then cure it
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	If you pull out all the pus, if you are certain that you have joined the two layers of the wound, and you sew them now, there will be no remaining pus because of the size of the abscess.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	If you are certain that you have grasped the root of the [disease], and that you have pulled out the foreign body, and you sew it as we have said
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	The abscesses which hold pus, pierce them either so that it dies; and the pierce with that which is before said, depending on the situation, and bring together with oil and similar things, so that what is remaining of the corruption is consumed; and when the wound is thoroughly cleansed, if the cure of the oil has been applied as it should be, while it is still sane
de squinance	When the swelling is reduced, and if you return to your work until you have completed it, then if there are any remaining small abscesses, press them and squeeze them out.
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The ancient ones spoke of the size of the gorge; but I have never seen it done in our land, and it is written in their words.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en .ij. amandres.	As for those who are obstinate, it is necessary that the fissure of the throat which is called the epiglottis be released; and this will not help, for all the veins and the blood vessels of the sick are at those who have placed their thumbs inside the mouth, or the throat or in the tonsils.</start_of_turn>
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the disease is in the channel of the blood vessels, it is necessary to cover the epiglottis to prevent loss of blood from strangulation.</start_of_turn
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	It is necessary, when our voices split the epiglottis, to cut it from three circles or four, a small incision through two circles or by the quantity of the incision at the side of the epiglottis; and if it is convenient to the section of the epiglottis that there be no swelling, and the veins are long.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	If the master is fearful, then he must stretch the skin of the throat to the chin; then open the wound as far as the nail; and avoid the blood vessels, if you see nothing; and then sew up the wound as we have said; and demonstrate by the section of the smoke of the nail that the jump will emerge from the broken bone, and by the defect of the voice; and leave the wound open for a piece.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the hour has passed since it was suspected that the strangulation exists, assemble the four limbs of the wound together, and bind them all around the cartilage; then administer medicines that cause new flesh to grow, as long as it is safe to do so
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	The wound is not made whole until the throat is completely closed, and the patient is judged to be dead, and the default is abandoned.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	Therefore he sews on the epiglottis for this reason that the patient cannot breathe, and he breathes through the wound; and thus is preserved from death; and for this reason they command the old man to leave the wound open until the malice of the disease has passed, and it has passed in three days or four. And then they command him to sew up the wound and heal, until it is healed; and I will tell you what I have seen.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	I saw a lady who had swallowed a needle, and had choked on a portion of her windpipe; and I went to her aid to cure her, but found her as dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I discovered the wound and found the blood that had escaped from it, and saw that there was no vessel or conduit other than the throat that had been injured by the wound.</start_of_turn
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	I hastened, and saw to the wound, and cured it until it healed; and the lady did not suffer any further, for she regained her voice and returned to her normal state; for in the cutting of the epiglottis I found no fear
de la grosse gorge	of the great throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	These abscesses are called "neck hernia", and are large abscesses of a yellowish color, and are very common in women; and there are two kinds: natural and accidental; for the natural kind has no cause
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere; et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire: se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point; et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And the accidental kind is of two kinds: one is like butter to us, and the other is like an abscess coming from an artery; and there is fear, and it is not safe to perform surgery except in a small area, and it proves and surrounds everything inside: if you find it just like butter, and cannot be grasped by any vein, if you cut, as we cut the nails, and take away the surrounding tissue, if there is none; and encircle well around, and cure as well as it can be, until it is completely healed.
des nous	And encircle all around, and cure him as it seems right, until he is completely healed.
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	Many ways are there for us, of which I shall speak of all; and behold that I tell thee all the difference that is between soundness and injury.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that dislocation is caused by heat and fever that persists, as long as the inflammation has not subsided, and is accompanied by pain; therefore rest the fever and heat.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros; et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	With neither wound nor fever nor pain, it contains the syfac, which is its own sack and is like the colour of wheat, and begins like oil, and becomes thick; and they are like grains or grease or moisture, and the colour of them is as I have said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It is necessary, when you come to the cure of the knot, to ask and inquire first about all the instruments which are called “instruments of extraction,” according to the form that comes or the treatise that follows.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme; puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	And the way to inquire about abscesses of the body is that you take more moisture from the root than you find in the abscess, and twist your thumbs and toes, until you feel that the instrument has grasped the cord; then do as much as the greatness of the abscess requires; then draw out the entrament, and take care that the spur does not break
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes; et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout; et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	If moisture comes suddenly and unexpectedly, as it often does in other abscesses; and if afterwards the surrounding tissue does not produce moisture, and is greasy, if you do not prick it with a needle, and burn it lightly with a cautery, and drain it gently from the root, it will swell up again immediately.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois; et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	If it does not drain, it swells up again many times; if a little remains, and you do not grieve it, if you use strong corrosive powders on the wound, hold the wound steady, and put soothing things on the abscess above; and if it is large, cut out two fingers of the wound and cure what is beneath.</start_of_turn>
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	If the wound is swollen, if it threatens life or some other urgent matter, and if you are in a hurry, use powdered vitriol and leave it for three or four days until the wound bursts open; then remove the clot of blood.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule; et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule; et sont de III manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	See here the forms of the instruments that enter the body, and there are three kinds: great, middle, and small; and there are three squares which are called "albaret", and one which is called "breb", and there are three kinds: great, middle, and small, to embrace the fistulas; and they are like needles which we sew wounds with, and they are made of saffron, or iron, or silver, and sometimes gold which is yellow, and they are more proven with black pitch to embrace the cortices of fistulas; and they are of three kinds: great, middle, and small, according to the quantity of the size of the perforation.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi; et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	The shapes of the needles are like the seed of appearances, as you see here: great, middle, and small; and if the needles have two cortices of three kinds each; and if the needles have three cortices, and they are of three kinds; and if the needles have two cortices, and a single cortex only, and they are of three kinds; and all these are necessary in their place.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf; et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes; et sont de III manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois; et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus; et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	The head of the humerus is fractured, and there are some that cut only from one side, from which we must eschew the vein and nerve; and of these intruders are the alemeles restored in gloves, so that the patient does not lose them at the opening of the abscesses; and there are three kinds: great, small, and middle, as you see; and we must not use them for any other purpose except in bones like the leg, arm, and shoulder, and the like. And in similar things.
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	And do not put it on any part which has recently bled, and has veins, and never again according to this great form:
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme; et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	Under no circumstances do the breasts of certain women swell when they begin to putrefy, so that they appear like female breasts; and they endure suffering and flee, and those who see them recover must believe that they must treat them as described in this fashion from line b to g inclusive.
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures; de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.; puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif; et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis. de la routure de l’artere	of the course of a vein
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme; et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont; et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans; et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	When the artery is closed, and the skin above is tough, if there are many abscesses in consequence, there is also bleeding from the vein above and below; if the surgeon knows that the abscesses are long and soft, he must pierce; if he does not, he will extract the abscess. This is foolish to close the abscess, just as when the spleen, the testicles, the liver or other parts are swollen, and the swelling is great.

des grosses boces pendans	When it hangs downwards, swollen, from the socket.</start_of_turn>
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans; et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	Never have I seen such tumors in the belly as these, and they are called "fungus" because of their resemblance to onions; their root is slender, and their head is large; there are both large and small ones. I have seen many people who have had two or more of these in their belly, and there was no difference between them, and they were all white, and had a soft root, and were split open by moisture.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine; si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	I saw them cut out and found one weighing eighteen ounces and another six and a third; and their work in incision is that if you look at the patient, you will see that they are moist, and the color of their arteries is pale and moist with a soft root; if the tumor is large and soft, and you are present, do the fire cautery immediately.</start_of_turn>
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer; et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors; et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	For at the shoulder comes often too great discharge of blood, and if it does not go away, if you are in a hurry, then do you burn; and if you see the patient groaning and fearful of the incision of the flesh, if you take a thread of gut well made, and bind the artery as we have said, and leave it for two days; and then the restraint, and do not cease draining the thread of gut until it has stopped the bleeding; and ask him to work by himself; and if the roots are large, if there is fear of the liver itself for the belly, but you must indeed cover half, then burn the other half, and cure the wound, and keep only the hair that is of dark colour and has little sense and milk-regurgitation.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For it is an inflamed abscess, and I will come to the cure of the abscess later.</start_of_turn>
quant li boude ist fuer	When the head of the shoulder is for.
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit; et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	If the belly appears swollen comes by burn of wound or fracture of cartilage, and is on the belly and there are some pus, as it happens in other ways, or blood which clots veins or arteries according to what is before, or windiness; and if it is by the route of the cartilage and by the discharge of pus, if it is the colour of the abscess resembles the colour of coral, and is a slight thing with little sense of pain, and has various discharges.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	and if it is from the bursting of the intestine, then it is more diverse, and when one presses it with the hands if it returns, and then comes back, and sometimes if it is caught, it swells out at the entrance to the bath and by great effort.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit; et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	If it is by moisture, it is an easy matter; open widely when you press on it with your hand, do not restrain me. If it is by blood, if it is open by these signs, the abscess is large and hard, and is fixed according to a quantity. If it is by wind, if it is blowing on the sufferer, and the work is being done, know that it is either the blood of an artery or a vein, or the wind.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	If you leave the cure like that.
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	For there is doubt and fear, as I have already said or as the chapter discusses concerning abscesses, concerning the artery and the vein.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude; puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains, puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile, puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine; puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz; puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine; se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre; et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit; et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren II aguilles, et i boute II fors filz, et boute les II aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier; puis estrain l’aposteme en IIII leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi; ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit; et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	If the intestine or the bowel appears, instruct the patient to hold his breath, and keep his head and shoulders stretched out; then mark with your finger the place where you have seen the swelling; then command him to grasp between your hands, then go around the limb that you have marked all around; then stretch half of the abscess downwards at the greatest point of the wound; then tie it around with a strong thread or strong silk cord firmly, and leave it alone; then put half of the abscess stretched over the thread, and put your index finger and the bowel; if you find the bowel caught in the thread, if you pull it out, and put the bowel back in its place; if you find the bowel stuck, if you pull at the wound, and cut off the excess; if the artery opposes this, or the vein, if it goes well around, then come back to your work and take two needles, and put in two strong threads, and pass the two needles through what you did in the form of a cross that you think you did pierce; then strain the abscess for three measures over the needles, and if you see, break the needles, and leave the limb as long as it bleeds, and cut off the dead tissue by itself; or you cut it when it is soft and swollen, and cure the wound of what it comes; and tie the abscess as we have said; and drain the blood or moisture that you find, then cure the wound of what it comes, and suture the limb.
dou chancre	And extract the blood or moisture that you find, then cure the wound of what is necessary, and suture the wound.
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	We have said in the previous section the signs of a boil, and how one should deal with it using medicine, and how to avoid the use of surgery; and we say that a boil often disappears in the marrow, and great caution is required in its treatment. The old people say that when a boil is in the flesh or can be easily plucked out like a boil that is in the marrow, and in the abscess, and in similar cases, it should be completely removed when it is in its beginnings; but when it is large and old, if one does not approach it cautiously, for I know of no cure for it; neither have I ever seen any cured before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide .i. boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when it is in the flesh or can be easily plucked out, as we have said, do not purge the black bile at any time; then make it healthy if it has shown signs of swelling, and then drain the ailment, that is to say, give the body a good dose of wine to make the work easier; then extract the marrow or boil, and the bone of all parts, and leave nothing remaining; and let the blood flow freely, and do not touch or move anything, and if the bleeding continues too much from the artery or vein, do not cauterize it until it is stained; then cure it with other remedies until it is healed.
de ydropisie	De ydropisie.

Et soit trenchans de II pars.	And let two parts be excised.
a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier; puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude III dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude III dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu; puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme:	And let two parts be excised at a point, and let there be no more pain than is necessary to bring them down to the intestines when one grasps them, and do not let them bleed; then look if dropsy is toward the intestines: if it seems that there is three ounces of bile above the navel, do three inches to the right of the navel; and if the dropsy is from the disease of the liver, do three inches to the left of the navel; and if it is from the spleen, do three inches to the right, and do not let the patient lie on the incision but only on the hardness that the superabundant [fluid] causes; then pierce through the skin with the instrument, and grasp the spleen, and hold your hand over the space between the skin and the muscle as if you were grasping the quantity of an nail or the thickness of an entorse; then pierce the muscle until the space between the thumb and the little finger is reached, which is the mark of the pain, then draw out the instrument, and that is the end of the operation.
Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz I petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, III pertus; et II d’autre part, et I d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	And it is similar to a silver nail, or an elderberry twig, or with a slight projection on the inside; or on one side three projections, and two on the other, and one on the other side; and the head of the shoulder is cut off like a quill, and this is the form of the incision that the writer makes for the quill.
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort; mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit; fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue.	At the top is the ailment, so that when the instruments come to the edge, if they go too deep now on the instrument; empty out a third or half, for if you drain more than that at once, by chance the patient will die from the resolution of his spirit from the weapon, or he cuts his hands, or he approaches death; but drain according to the quantity of its virtue, and according to what the dispositions of the virtue of the patient signify, and his pulses; then take out the instrument and hold back the blood, and it is held back now by the nerve that bites the projection which is on the surface, as I have said; so that you pierce according to this manner; then repeat the instrument the other way, if you see the patient suffering from this, and drain a small quantity of blood; do this under no circumstances, and keep using it until it stops bleeding.
Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre; et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	And if thou doubtest of the patient, and thou seest him mouthing blood, if thou art to cure him of a wound or of gravel scorched, and by mouthing sweat or bathing and with the sun, and keepest thyself from drinking; and let the cure of drying medicines be until he is well, and cauterize upon the stomach and upon the liver and upon the spleen after the extraction of the blood, as I have said before.

Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera.	If the opening is small, if medicine is applied with lead weights, as we have said, and it swells up.
Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	Those who have no hole in their limb are pale, for none are born who have a hole at the head of the bone, because they cannot urinate before they elevate their thigh; and they cannot endure this because the material cannot come up to the marrow, and this is a bad disease.

des pustules de la verge	Des pustules de la verge.
