The cautery helps in two situations: with discharge of blood and with corruption; and if the head of the shoulder is corrupted and retracted, if you bite or pull out the hair a thumb's breadth, and the patient urinates; and when the hair has become loose at the root of the hair that has not been circumcised, or if there is a wound or incision, then you must burn with the instrument that chews until the ligaments are loosened and the hair is freed from all parts; and if it is necessary to divide this, if you burn at the sputum without any hair at the root or on the nail, then dry carefully between two, and put a bandage of fine linen moistened with cold water on it, so that it does not move.</start_of_turn>
de la circoncision	except in the case of circumcision.</start_of_turn>
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Circumcision is not merely a continuation of the other wounds; however, when we perform this work of our will, and properly apply it, if it is necessary that our hands do the best work, and the most gentle for health.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancients did not teach us circumcision, for they did not use it in their laws, and we have only what we have learned through experience
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor .i. dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a .ij. toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	For I have seen the greatest part of masters and doctors who made circumcision endure great pain, force, and all sorts of novelties; if they fled from the heat because of two towels, and by chance if they were to cut off one and leave the other behind.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	Or the covering returns, and the pain is doubled, and with the support which is too slight to assure the tip of the limb; and with the support of the cord by chance escapes the iron, and completes the work, and many times it happens that they are born without any support and I want it.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en I tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz I poc a I autre liien; et la tien as II dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les II liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge; puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre I drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	When you press your hand, if it is equally taut in all directions, but the thread is well twisted around the skin; and if the procedure is such that the child understands, do not force him to bind the thread around the limb only lightly, but bind it firmly in all ways; then hold it straight between your hands or suspend your fingers so that the child cannot see them, neither any of the instruments; then hold your hand at the base of the limb and breathe or cough, and pull up as much as the head of the limb is ensnared; then thoroughly cleanse the wound that is assembled, then tie the limb with a double thread, and tie it once again at the other end; and keep two fingers by the second loop and thumb, and press between the two loops, then withdraw the thumb gradually and bring the head of the limb forward; then leave the blood to flow naturally, for that is the treatment; and put powder on and over the powder I drape a cloth glued with a yolk of an egg moistened with rose oil and resin, and leave it on until the bleeding stops.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	The shape of the forces at the circumference is like this: the two thumbs should be tense and stretched, and the fingers should be as great as the thumb equally:
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	The error of the mundane is when the spur of the kidney follows the incision; therefore it is necessary that you extend it to your nail, even though it causes an incision; and hold it equally, and if you do not wish to hold it at your nail, if you hold it with your hand, and then hold it.
Et s’il trespassent .iij. jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement; si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	And if they trespass for two days, and what is below the rib is swollen, if you leave it as long as the spasms subside, and the swelling is slight; if you hold it as you wish, and keep hold of the part of the rib, it will not harm you in any way
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point; cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Cure then the body of things soiled with powder, as we have said or treated with powders, and if we hold it too much, it will go away; cure then it, as we have said, until it is healed.
dou retenement de l’urine	Dou retenement de l’urine
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division; et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e; et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	The urine is retained if it is due to the stone, or blood congealed, or a wound, or a swelling, or anything similar, as we have said in the previous division; and if the urine is not discharged, and you see that the retention is caused by the stone which is in the kidney or the neck of the bladder, if it is possible, let the patient bend his knees; and let him put his feet on the back, and extend his belly from the part under his back, and restrain the patient as much as he can; and then constrain the neck of the bladder to the expression of the stone above, so that the urine is discharged; and if it does not come out, as we have said, and the patient feels great pain, if it is possible, administer an extraction with all the instruments which are called "syringes"; for this is the form: either of silver with a fine edge like a bird's quill; or the caine of a palm of long and a half; or fine silver.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede; puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine; et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	And thus for the issue of urine, if you take one double thread and tie one end to the chief of wool or cotton, and pass the thread through the syringe; and drain the excess wool and pass until the chief of the syringe, then join the syringe with oil or butter and eggshell, and make the patient sit on the chair, and raise the bladder and the testicles with oil moist and oily; then put the syringe smoothly into the testicles, until it reaches the root of the testicles, then double the testicles upwards towards the buttocks; then withdraw the syringe before it reaches the bladder, and feel the patient coming until the thing is empty, and that is not done except in this order except for that which leads or goes out is twisted; then let the thread go entirely from the wool and the wool, and the urine follows the wool, and then draw out the thread, and correct the urine; and repeat the syringe until the bladder is empty, and be sure the patient is aligned.
des maladies de la vessie	Des maladies de la vessie.
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When there are dropsy or blood in the bladder, or putrefaction is assembled, and you see urine and medicines distilled, if you do everything that is called the «clepsedre», which is its shape:
Elle est close, et si a III pertus: II d’une part, et I d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est; et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens; si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens; si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	She is closed, and if there are three holes: two on one side, and one on the other, as you see; and the head of the shoulder is grasped so that the medicine may be struck firmly in the direction of addition, if we can manage to drive out the moisture, and push as much as necessary; and when you see the medicine slipping in the bladder, put the chief physician in the moisture, and drive out the one who is in front; if you drive out the moisture from the chief, and then push strongly the one in front; if the moisture enters the chief, and comes to the bladder now, if the patient feels it; and that is the form of the subtle cluster from which we clusterize the bladder: if this is the case:
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut; et desoz a I sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les II seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe I poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie; et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai I cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute I fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble I dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	She is of silver or gold, and the head is higher; and from the first joint or the shoulder blade; then take a bladder of a goat and put the moisture which you see clustering the bladder inside, and tie it between the two breasts forming a double bow; and burn one part of that moisture on the fire; then draw out the head of the cluster from the belly, and strain your hand over the bladder until the patient feels that the moisture has come to the bladder; and if you do not have a bladder, take a piece of parchment, and make a circle, and pierce it round the edges; then draw the string firmly through these holes, and assemble the circle as if you were assembling a wheel, and put inside what you see of oil, moisture, and water, and tie it in the instrument; and do as if you had made a bladder, pressing your hand until the moisture comes to the bladder.
de la piere	De la piere.
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have already mentioned in the previous chapter the methods of extracting stones, and the medications associated with this; and we mentioned the difference between a retained stone and one that is not, and the signs of each; and when a stone should be removed in size; and in the bladder, and in the kidney. And I will tell you openly and briefly about this.</start_of_turn>
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont .iiij. ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that a stone that is retained in the bladder is often as painful as when it is expelled; and this is a sign that the stone is breaking from its root, like the pain of a splinter in its subtlety. And it opens gravel, and grinds the patient’s side, and causes them to urinate frequently, and then becomes cold; and from these spurts there is often a discharge of pus. And it is light to cure these spasms until they are about three years old; and it is more painful in old people, and is like a woman in her youth, to those who are between youth and old age; and the cure is easier for those who have a large stone than for those who have a small one.</start_of_turn
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	And when we come to the treatment, if it is necessary, we must first cleanse the patient by blistering, to drive out all the evil that is in the intestines.
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	For it never hinders to inquire about the stone.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche dedens; se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	Then take the patient by the limbs, and loosen and move downwards, so that the stone descends to the bottom of the bladder, and does not rise up again; then make it sit between your hands, and let its hands be placed on its buttocks, so that the bladder is completely emptied downwards; then inquire and touch inside; if you feel the stone in the space, then hasten to cut above the stone immediately
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	And if it does not bleed at the touch, then moisten your left thumb, if the patient is an elder, or your middle finger, if the patient is young and robust; and hold it in its foundation, inquire for the stone, and when you feel it with your finger, if the bladder is tense at the navel; then press above your finger, and remove the stone when you see it or when you feel it slip out
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	And instruct the minister to press the bladder with his hand, and command him to extend with his right hand the intestines upwards, and with his left hand to grasp the skin which is below the intestines in the part where the size is taken; then insert the sponge covering, as it is formed:
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans; par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	And be between these two that are between the coions and the foundation, do not go into the middle but along the left nave; and be two above the stone, and two below either the aditus or the foundation, and be the size of the traverse if it is large by excess, and narrow within, according to the quantity of the stone, do not go too large; for in doing so the press if it must be upon the aditus or the foundation, that it leap forward in work; and the nails that are in the stone or the angles, and margins: if it is gripped to burst; and if there is any that is squeezed, it is like a gland, round, from which there is little issue.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole; et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	And thus when there are angles and margins, make the size greater; and if it does not leap, it is likely that you will tear the nails which are like a file at the head, for it is necessary to tear the stone if it escapes; or you can break off the instrument which is bent at the head; and if you do not manage to engage it, if it is too large, the vessel will be burst, and if it is not well done, it will be as if it were a vein of vitriol; and if there are several stones, first take out the largest at the neck of the bladder, then go over the top, and finally the bottom, and the smaller afterwards if there are several of them.
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	And if it is large, if you cover it with silk, and make a greater wound.
Car II choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces; et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	And if it is large, if you cover it with silk, and make a greater wound. For in this matter two things happen to the patient: or he dies, or the urine comes down excessively because the testicles cannot support; but whatever you do, if you pull out the nails, even if you take them out piecemeal; and when you have completed your work, if you apply incense, aloe and dragon's blood, and hold it tight, and put above it a wet bandage soaked in oil and wine, or in oil and rosewater and cold water, to soothe the burn; then raise the patient up on his collarbone, and do not release the tie until the third joint.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have pulled it out, if there is any blood remaining in the wound from oil and water, then cure it with beeswax ointment and linseed oil, until it is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit; puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	And if blood clots come into the wound and corrosions, and freezing of blood in the bladder, and either because of retention of the urine, which is known in part as a lack of jumping with the urine: burst then your belly in the wound, and draw out that blood, for if it remains, it will burst the bladder and carry it away; then lift the wound with water and comfort and silk, and help him in every way you can until he is healed; and know that all the times you treat him, that you bind up the two cuts and gather the medicines on the limb.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	If the stone is small and lies in the passage of the bladder, and is fixed, and the urine cannot issue; if the physician performs what I have said above, that you will listen to the size of this treatment.
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	I have already seen this proven to be true
Pren .i. foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a .iij. angles fichiees en .i. tison:	Take hold of the forceps according to this shape and be at a right angle with two teeth fixed in one socket:
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge. de la piere des femmes	If you cannot do this for any reason, take hold of the bone at its upper and lower extremities, then place the thumb between the two tendons, and grasp firmly; then extract the foreign body, loosen the tendon, and solidify the blood that is in the wound; and cure until it is healed.
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por .iij. choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	When the bone is loosened in a woman, and if it does not happen again, it is a grievous cure and is defended by two things: the first is that perhaps the woman is a virgin; and the second is that one cannot find a woman who knows how to uncover her breasts as well as she does.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier I caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere; et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge: adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere; et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	And thus the third method is that if by chance one cannot find a woman well learned in this art of hands; and the fourth method is that if the woman’s stone is more prominent than the man’s, for it can be made deeper, and great fear is in her. If such is necessary, if you take a prudent woman well knowing, and prick her thumb with the needle, and if you do not find her, do not cast aside the subtle art; and present her with a wise woman in the life of women, or a woman who knows a part of the art, and command her to do what you command her from the inquiry of the stone; and look well whether the woman is a virgin: for if she is, she must push out her shoulder or foundation and ask for the stone; and if she finds it, if she constrain her shoulder blade, she must command her to keep her shoulder blade or with the patient, and desire and press her left hand on her bladder.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite; puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains.	If this is true, it must be known that if it is moved from the entrance of the bladder to the knee, as far as it reaches the root of the thigh; then cut upon the thigh at the root of the thigh and find the middle of the bone there where it is usually hidden, and feel the thigh in that part; and do not move your hand above the thigh or below, and let the size be small at first; then gradually increase it until you feel the thigh become painful as much as the bone can bear, and that many kinds of stones are like this: some small and large, sharp and smooth, long and round, and which have many rains.
si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	if the stones resemble these in appearance, it is known that they issue from the bladder.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre; et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	If it does not go away, if you put at the root of the bone a little piece of vitriol, and hold it for an hour until it is stained; then return to your work, while the bone is still flexible, and have the instruments that I have told you about for extracting the stone as your help in this work; and if it does not go away, and it is the artery that has been cut, if you put powder on the wound and strain with needles and thread, do not resume this work again, and leave the bone alone, only by chance will the patient die; then cure the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	When the bleeding has ceased and the limb is restored, if you return to work while the bone is still stiff, as long as the bone is firm.</start_of_turn>
de hernie carnouse	of a hernia.
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit .i. autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	Ramice aquouse is nothing else but an assembly of moisture or white fat, which is as soft as the seeds of coriander, that contains the egg; and it is called "syfac", and never is it properly in the belly of the egg if we take care that this is not the case; and it is the skin of the seed between the white fat that we have said.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the generation of this moisture is from weakness that comes from the seeds, and it is spread through that material.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus; et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	And under no circumstances should percussion come upon the joints, for this moisture has many colors: or it is pale yellow, or it is without redness, or black, or bluish white, and this is more; and these are the signs of gangrene in this assembly, for if it is pale yellow or white as we have said, if there is swelling around the wound, and the joint does not open, for there is moisture all around.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef; et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	And if there is moisture in the flesh itself, if there is swelling around the wound with some of the bone exposed, and because of this some think that it is a fracture; and if the moisture is between the skin of the joint and the white substance, if it feels soft; then when you see the color of the moisture, if it seems to have all the qualities mentioned before.
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	According to this, therefore, that which follows the introductor, judge of that which is within.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz; puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des II costelz dou keur des coions; puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir; puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a I large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue; et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les II leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When our curer employs iron, if it be that the patient is sound in body and limb; then he should place the heel of his hand upon his back, upon something somewhat high, and put a cloth over his hand; then he should sit on his left side, and command the minister to sit on his right side, and extend his thigh to the second rib from the navel of the costae; then he should grasp the testicles with his left hand, and with the right hand he should split the skin of the costae as far as the white line, and carefully eschew the bone according to the master’s order; then he should pierce the white membrane with a needle at a large hole, and drain all the fluid, and then put in his sponges, and elevate the white membrane; and do not touch the testicles, but only the white membrane; split the entire costae or in pieces at your leisure, for if you do not split it thoroughly, the fluid will return; and if the owner of the work should happen to leap up at your work, let him remain in his place until you have finished the work of the white membrane.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	And if you find the spleen corrupted by another disease, if you must tie up the blood vessels that are suspended, doubting the decay of blood; then remove the bone at its entirety, drain the spleen, and stitch it up as we have said.</start_of_turn>
Et se aigue est assemblee en II parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont II ramices; si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset; et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les II coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	And if the swelling is collected in two parts together, its sacs are two branches; if you press the other part as you did the first equally, then wipe the blood, and put into the wound a piece of cloth soaked in rose oil; and put on another cloth soaked in wine and oil, and put on the two testicles, and put under doubled cloths, and bind it up according to this fashion:
Puis pren II drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil; et li autre dui chief sus les II angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier; et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes I cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers; si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	And take two cloths, and use coarse wool thread as in this semblance and join them together at the groin; and one of the ends grasps on the foundation up to the loin, and the other at the blunt part; and the other two fingers grasp on the two angles, and be all assembled so that the restriction is in the loop of the groin; and never is medicine used for this burn except for the size of a needle, and take only one burn like a needle, and prick the skin of the testicles, and if there is a white spot that contains the blood is discovered; if you take the burn as we have said, and pierce that spot as with a needle, and burn it with this subtle burn.
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout; et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef; et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve; et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille; et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	And take care in every way that you can, until you have made him whole; and keep that the fire does not touch the egg; and take care that this work is more salve; and keep guard of the discharge of blood, and do not fear the work of size; and if anything hinders you, or an abscess or discharge of blood or anything else that may be harmful, if it be possible, cure that which hinders you, according to what is before said.
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai, si fai seoir le malaide sus I siege leveit; pues perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors; et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer; puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee; et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant; et eslarge I poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés VI mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	And if the patient is pale and does not wish to wait for this work because of its horror, if you deem it appropriate, pierce the abscess at the lower part with a broad knife, and make the perforation long from the nail; and if the wound is large, let the blood flow freely; then put cotton on the wound, and tie it, and leave the remaining blood to drain away naturally; then cure the wound until the wound is healed; and if the wound does not drain all the blood from the wound, as you should know, drink a spoonful or the instrument used for treating hydrophobia, for the form is as mentioned above; and widen the wound and ensure the blood returns, and assemble after six months or when the tissue has healed, and when it is assembled as before, and he will then be able to pass his days.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the testicles.
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse; et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	Wounds that in this section of the twig have fear in many situations, for it seems to me that the must is to leave them alone; and I will tell you the work and the signs of the abscess.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	I say therefore that most abscesses come from wounds or sores, and sometimes from boils; and it is by experience.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion; et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief; et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	It is known by superfluous swelling and heat, which is spread as coions or by percussion; and the color of the abscess is like the color of honey; and there is no pain, and it is abscess; and sometimes it is a large abscess that is painful and bloody, and has a foul color, and never comes from an artery, or from swelling of a vein.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois; et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	When it is not from an artery, if it is known by the disposition of the abscess wound, when you press it with your hand; and it must not be touched by you.
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois, et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars; et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	He who makes an incision in a vein is known by his position at the expression of pain in the two hands; and he can make as well the size of this resemblance as of the others; and it is that you must close like nails, then the head is up, and the thread is from white silk, and deliver the suspension from all parts of the head.
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope; et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	If the head of the vein is already clotted with these thorns, if you must then draw out the vein, and close it; and if it is under the silk or in the blood vessels, if you must draw out all that is taut, and close it roundly.
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	If the cartilage comes loose from its root or behind, if you must clamp it all, and withdraw the yolk, as we have said.</start_of_turn>
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	When your work is done, if you are using a woolly bandage soaked in rose oil and wine, then treat with other remedies until they are healed.</start_of_turn>
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the testicles.
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a I borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions, et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait; et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant, et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	This is an abscess covered with a covering similar to a berry, with the softening of the nails, and the patient groans greatly when he walks; and the cure for this disease is well known just as much as this one that we have just mentioned, and all of us say that it is the work of an old man according to what he himself did
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois, a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment; puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert, et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples; puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait I fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief; puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues; puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions; car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz; si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	You must make the patient sit down in a comfortable chair, then suspend the ligature of the tonsils from the two sides of the throat, to all the vessels that are protruding from the edge, and grasp them firmly, and stretch them out; then cut through the tough membrane covering the opening of the blood vessels, until they are uncovered, and then remove the clot from the surrounding area, as we said in the extraction of arteries in the temples; then insert a needle or there is double thread, and tie it to the first loop or the knot has passed, and tie it to the other end; then cut around the middle directly, according to the length of the bone, and remove the corrupted humors; then cure the wound as with others or apply a bandage, so that no vessel tears except for those that have bled, for by this means there will be no harm; if all the vessels have bled, then it is enough to drain the abscess from all the vessels; if there is no loss of blood from the incision of the vessels, and if they are dry and do not bleed any more.
de la routure dou syfac	from the root to the surface
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions; et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces II manieres de mout de causes: ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses; et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement; et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	The event of this root is by incision that comes or by swelling above the belly in the part of the flanks, for the intestines descend from that route to one of the hips; and this route is either by fracture or swelling of the bone, or comes from these two humors of causes: by percussion, or by jumping, or by pressure, or by the elevation of a wound, or by some similar things; and the sign when it is by fracture of the bone is that there is swelling and swelling in a long stretch, and does not come immediately; and the swelling is equal on both sides up to the navel, because the bone presses the intestines.
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	And the sign is when the jaw is fractured, that it causes sudden pain at the start, and the abscesses are diverse in appearance, such as bursting skin and exposed bone, because of the escape of the intestine and the hardness of the jaw.
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	And never should the limb be moved with the intestine, and is retained when it is held, and causes great pain to the patient, even when it is pressed
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	And in these treatments with fire there is fear, for it is known to escape.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir; puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes; puis estent le keur au desus, et cope tout le cuir des coions dou lonc; puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir; puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars; puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac, et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac; et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille; et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement; et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz; puis pren une aguille ou il ait I gros fil fait de X filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions; aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait IIII filz; puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de II pars; puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de II pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne; et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc II dois de celui, et aprés ces II liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi; et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte; puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant; puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	If you command or the patient must retain the intestine at its root in the wound if it can be returned; then either sew above its collar between your hands, and keep the thighs; then stretch the knee upwards, and cut away all the skin of the hips along the length; then draw inwards the livers as large as you must to open the wound, and so on until you have reached the bone; then remove the fracture of the bone that is under the skin of the hips, as long as the soft bone remains covered with skin; then place your thumb in that place which adjoins the hip, between the white bone which is under the skin of the heel and the second bone, and pull out that which is behind the heel, and between the second bone; and then move the thumb of the hand towards the hip, and the white bone is at the top of your left hand, and keep the heel at the whole of the hip; and command the minister to stretch out the heel, and unfasten that which is behind the ligament; and ask if there is any intestine or white bone remaining, and if you find nothing, if it is in the belly again; then take a needle or make a large thread of X threads, and pass it through the back part of the bone, which is behind the skin of the hips; after the thread, then cut the nerves that appear from the thread, until there are three threads; then gather the threads together in the shape of a cross, and bind the bone, as we have said, with a strong thread of two parts; then cover the nerves with thread and bind them together in two parts, so that no vessels that support them can enter, except for the vein that comes from behind; and put on the dressing as before.
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	And never is the bladder cauterized after the incision, out of doubt of the discharge of blood.
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui; et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece; puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	For in this work, there is often the evacuation of blood, and leaving the limb long as it desires; and if it delays at the seat, if so it is raised from hot water, and put on what we have said, until it desires; then treat the wound with another treatment, until it is perfectly healed.
de hernie carnouse	of a hernia.
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this limb I have never seen anyone who dared to cure with fire.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz; puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the old men say that it is done like the bark of a twig that is bound to the nail, in part as you bind the veins, after the size above lightly to the outside; then cut in half, and treat the abscess of that which causes it, until the veins cease to bleed; and treat it as we have said, until it is perfectly healed.
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres; et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent; et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert; et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere: et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de III dois; et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac; et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les II leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre; puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines; puis le cure par la cure des plaies.	Never comes rupture in anger, as we have said, and open the eye; and do not cut any intestines as stones, and if there are any, it is because of that, and repair them every hour; and all the blood that remains too long in this place, if you believe the wound or swelling, until the intestines are evacuated; and this comes from the extension of the sinew that is in anger, as we have said, because it is stretched, then is softened and pulled down from the eye; and treat it if by cautery, as we have said before; and never by iron in this manner: and let the patient lie calmly on his back between your hands, then cut the limb of the rupture inflated with a width according to the quantity of three fingers; and then draw out the sinew that is outside the leather that covers it, and take the needle and bring it out from the limb appearing from the sinew; and press at the belly, then cut the two ends of the sinew appearing from the sinew on the head of the needle; and cut one and the other; then draw out the head of the needle, and do not cover the sinew or extend the yolk of anything, as I have told you in the treatment of the root of the intestines; then treat by the treatment of wounds.
Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And when you have closed the wound, if the pus and cure the wound, as long as it is healed.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The shoulder joint is constrained, and shows no outward displacement; the burn is mute in this limb and is more distant from health.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	from the softening of the skin of the armpits.
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les .ij. levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a .iij. costures ou .iiij. fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	Many times the skin of the armpits is softened in sick people, because the fat that is inside is softened, and is seen; and it is necessary, when we see it cured, to make the patient sit up on his back, and to stretch the softened skin over the natural skin; then to join the two layers together with a suture, and if you see, close the superfluous softened skin at two or three sutures firmly; then close between the sutures, and cure like the others wounds, until it is healed, and cut the thread.</start_of_turn>
dou chastrement	of great suffering.
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por II manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes.	That which is scraped from the wounds is esteemed in our law, and for this reason I do not wish to speak of it in this book; and it is not necessary to force anyone to do so. For it is often necessary to castrate certain beasts for our assistants, as for example, goats and sheep and cats and other beasts.
Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc II manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.	I say therefore that castration is done in two ways: by traction or by incision
En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.	In that which we do it by traction, we make the beast sit in warm water, until the testicles are softened and limp; then we grasp them with our hand, until they are set and no longer cause pain
Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a I cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	From the caulking of size: command that you keep the best, and press the leather of the nails to your left hand, then bind the suspension, and hook onto each loop with a hook, when you have well secured them; and leave no trace of blood or thin blood which escapes from the vessels; and this method of caulking is more effective than that which is made by traction, because traction remains by chance no thing of the nails, because it desires luxury; then cure the wound until it is healed.
des hermofrodites	Hairs that are scorched with fire are commanded to the patient to leave them long and even; and if they prick at their root, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Hermofrodie est selonc II manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les II coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.	Hermaphroditism is in two ways as at home: one if between the two nails appears as the figure of the nature of a woman, or if there are hairs, and sometimes in court it urinates.
Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et II coions.	And the other way is in women, and has on the navel as a rod and two nails.
Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	And the treatment for worms and fever is that you burn the carbuncles that arise, and treat them like other wounds; in the second method, for those whose urine spurts through the skin of the buttocks, if there is no cure.
de la tentigene	Hermaphroditism is in two ways like that of women: one if between the two testicles appears as in the nature of a woman, or if there is hair, and sometimes in the urine.  And the other way if it is in women, and has on the navel like a beard and two testicles.  And the cure for the shame and the fame if it is that you cut off the testicles altogether, and the cure is like other wounds; in the second way, of those homes whose urine spurts through the skin of the testicles, if there is no cure.
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure.	The tinder is a charred piece on the natural part, as long as it is too heavy to see; and many women have it as much as a hand, and that is the cure.
Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee».	It is necessary to keep the superfluousness of the tinder at your hand or armpit, and to grasp it lightly; and do not be too rough, for blood does not come from there, then the wound is cured by other means; and for another mark that appears at the mouth of the marrow, and the spleen, and by chance spurts out, and is like a cow’s foot, and for this reason it is called the old “mad cow’s disease”.
Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If you manage to hold it firmly, as we have said, and cure it until it is healed.
de erratique	De erratique.
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile.	If it is fickle, as when the nature of a woman is not clearly known, or if the rupture is slight; it is natural by birth, or by accident from illness, or it is caused by injury from a broken bone, or a wound, or a burn, or by poison, or by eating too much, or by excessive drinking; and it is finished by conception, and by childbirth, and by chance the flowers have become diseased. And this knowledge is obtained by experience from the dance.
Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait.	If the swelling is close to the surface, if it is at the shoulder or at the elbow.
S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as II leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes II dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les II leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder.	If it is of a subtle wound, and if it is close to two fingers or the elbow, if you are in a hurry, hold the two fingers together, and let the woman lie on her back, spreading out her legs; then stretch the two fingers until the subtle wound is round, and cover it over with oil, and place it on the limb, and keep the woman still until it has healed.
Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte.	And if the scapula is hard and thick, it is prudent that you use a sponge resembling a holly leaf.
Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if there is swelling of the bone, if you suspend it at the incision and support it; and have the medicines that stop bleeding, such as alum, dragon’s blood, incense, and abundance of eggs; then mix in a quantity of lead plaster, so that the wound does not adhere; and let it be long, and mix in a little thread of linen; then do other cures until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez.	And when the marrow comes swelling, if you cover it according to this manner, it is not abscesses that form.</start_of_turn
Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	For the swelling of the marrow, do not touch with fire.</start_of_turn
des emorroides	From hemorrhoids.
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	Emorroydes are openings of veins which, without a cause, are usually harmless; and when they are old, they become thick; and we have already mentioned in the preceding chapters the signs and symptoms, and I will now tell you those which indicate a cure.
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	I say that hemorrhoids and thrombi, when they are pressed down in the rectum, and are not felt, if not treated by force.
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	Those which are at the mouth of the rectum, we can feel, are those which we can cure.
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	It is necessary therefore that you put the woman in a cold house, then hold the armpit tight, and press down on the swelling with your thumbs, and sprinkle on medicinal powders such as chamomile and dragon’s blood and incense, and similar things; then close your eyes for an hour, and then bathe her in cold water; and if there is still swelling, make her sit in a decoction of sumac and pomegranate seeds and barley and similar things, and then take barley flour, and mix it with honey and anise, and make I a poultice on her back
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	And if it swells, that is good.
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.	And if that does not happen, if air is blown through the wound and there are worms at the surface; then take linen and soak it in juice of plantain or in juice of elderberry with old wine, and blow air into the wound.
Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the abscess is settled, if the wound is cleansed until it is healed; and that which is called “albathir” is red, and is like a black eye, if you cover it as I have said before; and then heal the wound until it is healed
des apostemes de la marris	Emoroids are openings of veins which without restraint usually occur; and when they are old, they become thickened. We have already mentioned in the division the signs and symptoms; and I will say here those which resolve the cure. I say that emorroids and thick blood, when they are mixed in the marrow, and are not perceptible to the touch, if not treated with iron. Those which are at the edge of the marrow, we can perceive, are those which we can cure. It is therefore necessary that you place the woman in a cold house, then extend the ankle and grasp the heel, then sprinkle on medicinal astringents such as acacia and dragon’s blood and incense, and similar things; then remove the pieces an hour later, and put them in cold water; and if there is any bleeding, if you make her sit in a decoction of sumac and pomegranate seeds and saffron and similar things, and then take barley flour, and mix it with honey and assails, and make one plaster on her back. And if it is fainting, that is good. If this does not happen, if there is still bleeding at the edge, make a wound there with a needle; then take lint and moisten it in the juice of plantain or in the juice of elderberry with wine vinegar, and make the wound bleed. And when the wound has healed, if the bleeding has ceased, that which is called ‘albathir’ is red, and is similar to a rough chief, if you cover it as I have said the thickened blood; and then the bleeding will cease. And when the wound has healed, if the bleeding has ceased, that which is called ‘albathir’ is red, and is similar to a rough chief, if you cover it as I have said the thickened blood; and then the bleeding will cease.
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	There are many kinds of abscesses that come in the belly, such as carbuncles and pierced abscesses and herpes and worms and tumors and fistula and hemorrhoids and burnt abscesses, and other diseases that I have mentioned in the previous division
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	It is incumbent therefore that I say that I die in this treatment of the boil that comes in the marrow, which is not merely a boil that collects pus; and if you know the work of iron, behold if the boil is already in the beginning of its coming, and full of heat and fever, and if it becomes red, know that you must see it.
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	Therefore do not urge me to pierce it, but let me measure as long as the pain is eased; then seat the patient on a seat and put two little seats or he slumps, and support him on his back and bring together his limbs so that his thighs are spread apart, and put his arms down by his knees, and bind them firmly with a bandage; then take the bail towards his breastbone, and bring the instrument from which we expel the pus from the wound, so that this comes out; and know that when you bring this instrument, that you should first feel the depth of the wound, so that what enters with the instrument does not go deeper than it should, and does not harm the patient; and if the instrument is large, you must cover the depth of the wound with cloths, so that the instrument does not hurt it; and know that you must put the horn of the instrument at the bottom, and hold the instrument.
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.	And when the abscess bursts open, and we have washed the hand well, if it covers the head, at the spleen's root; and when the wound is emptied, if you wish, put into the wound some soft materials in rose oil or dry green oil; put the dressing firmly on the edge of the wound and put on above the dressing and on the heel of the bandage a clean linen cloth wet with vinegar or mallow that has been boiled; then cure it after two days following that, until it is healed; and never raise the wound and the dressing by means of an aquaplast and honey, and then of water or long rootwort and alum.
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	And if the wound has been closed in the wound, if you wish, that you take care not to burn it, but cure it as we have said in the division.
de l’enfantement	From infancy.
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	The master is first at the play when he knows the figure of natural childbirth, and the signs are when you see the woman pressing down her belly, and desiring to smell the head: then the child will be born immediately; then withdraw your hands from the belly as soon as the child is born, and support it with the other hand; and when you see these signs, if you press slightly on the belly, the child will be born; for when it descends on the head, if you support it with the other hand, the head will be delivered of its superfluities by natural force.
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	For it never comes from its pieces, but comes for the horn or the shoulder, and the arms, or it comes on the belly or the side, and is changed by an accident from its collar, and by other harmful figures; if the master is at the play that he be wise and discreet in these matters, and beware of error and deception, and I will show you all the figures how one must help them.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	When the child comes out of his head naturally, and the woman gives birth and her strength is weak, if you make her sit on a chair, or the women hold her; and she gives birth of oil or fennel or whatever is pleasing, and then you must hold the child between her two legs, which is his natural shape:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.	And open the secondine, and grasp its nail as long as the moisture that is inside comes out; and press the woman’s belly until the fetus descends, and if it does not descend, then it is necessary to perform a curettage of the woman with fennel chaff in sesame oil; then make her drink and vomit, and hold her mouth and nose for an hour: if the fetus is gone now.
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	If the two hands go out too far, if you must command her to let them go lightly and gently; and if they do not enter, put the woman on a chair, and hold her feet high; then withdraw the chair from under her, and hold her, so that she does not bleed; and if the hands still do not enter, and the fetus is dead, if you grasp the hands at the collar which is in front, and pull out the child, and comfort her equally.

de l’issue des gemelz	When the dislocation is slight
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent .iij. ou .iiij.; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	When there is a fracture of the bone, it often happens that the blood vessels are ruptured, and sometimes the bone is split in two or even three places; and this is not a strange thing, and often happens.

de plusors enfans	Furthermore.
