Aucune fois sont formez en la marris I ou II ou III ou IIII ou V ou VI ou VII, ou plusors jusc’a XV, et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious, et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient; si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	Never are they formed in the first, second, third, fourth, fifth, sixth or seventh degree, or more, up to the fifteenth degree; and are all formed like children by the measure of their glorious age. And it is prudent that the glorious dance should consume all of this, because by chance there are similar things; do as it is commanded
de l’enfant mort	From childhood death.
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains; si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort; si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees; et li ministre la teigne de II pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant; puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges; puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere I leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu, et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief; si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez, et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes; et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide; et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	When you cure a woman of a dead child or of a belly, if she does not come into labor, and you are compelled by the work of your hands; if you believe that the woman is of sound virtue, and has no accident or fears of death; if you believe that the woman is consoled on her back, and her shoulders are flexed forward, her legs are lifted; and you support her hand for two parts, or bind her to the bed if she is not being treated for the descent of the child; then wipe the mouth of the matrix with oil moistened with slime of alum and fennel seed and flaxseed; then anoint her hands with these oils and these slimes; then put her on the matrix lightly, and ask her if she feels any movement that may be seen; and take care that the fetus is not delivered before its time. If she delivers before her time, if you insert the fingers into her eyes or nose or mouth or stomach or under the breast or beard or force her chin or raise her costae; and if she delivers while her feet are on the ground, if she grasps or cries out and has pale cheeks; and you must keep the finger on her dominant hand, and put her elbow between her two hands, and support her hand lightly, and insert the finger into none of the parts that we have said, until it comes to the thing in void; and this is the form of the finger:
puis fiche encontre I autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz; et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	Then the hand finds another bone, or the third if you are involved, if so the extraction must be equal; and then extend them equally by moving from side to side, in order to stretch, or grasp the nails if necessary.
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie; et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	And if any part remains, if one feels some of its two nails, and holds them in that part, and treats the other part; and if no part remains, if you put this bone or higher up again, and do this until it is completely healed.</start_of_turn>
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement, si covient que tu envoloupes sus I drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote; puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as II piés.	And if one hand comes before the other, and it cannot be returned by stretching, if you must cover over the drapeil, so that it is whole; then grasp at the joint of the thumb or the little finger, and then you must make in the other hand, and have two fingers.</start_of_turn
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue; ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui; et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment; et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles, et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer; et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues; et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	And if the head of the shoulder is great and it is twisted at the issue, or if there is a sharp pain put together, if you can put the spinous process between your two thumbs, and hold the shoulder and draw out the pain; or you can bind it to the instrument which is called "almidach," from which comes the form with the instruments or chapter which is after this; and in the same way make the limb naturally swell with great pain; and then treat the bones as tenacious, and if the shoulder leaps up and strains at the forcele, if it is fractured, as long as the moisture which is either coming out or remaining leaps up; and if it cannot be cured, if you must break the bone at the neck as you please; and if it is swollen in the belly or at the ribs, if you can lose as much moisture as the moisture comes out.
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	and if the swelling is on its pieces, if the attraction is strong, and the address at the mouth of the marrow is weaker.
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a I drapeil envoloupeit sus la main; et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre; et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure, si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris; puis i boute I oncine ou II, et le trai fuer; et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier, ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses; et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	And if it is strained in the belly or the arm, it is fitting that you extract it with a drape wrapped around the hand; and hold the belly or the arm, until the moisture that is causing the pain has subsided. And if another limb is stiff and immovable, and the bone is fractured, if the hand is grasped firmly by the thumb and index finger, and is pulled out as far as the thumb will reach; then there will be one or two fractures, and the limb must be forced out. And if the mouth of the wound is closed by a thick scab, if it is not possible to pass anything through, it must be scraped off, for it brings forth thick and fatty things; and it brings forth pus, and becomes soft and moist.
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif; et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	And if the limb is on its cost, and you must set it straight, if you must do what we have said about the living child; and if it does not yield, if you must force it out piecemeal, and leave nothing of the second.
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris; et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	And when you have done this, if what we have said concerning the wounds comes to pass, and blood appears, whether by means of an aquapressure or other cure.
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut .i. autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman whose belly had two fetuses inside, one died and the other remained.
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After a long time, there came a swelling in the belly, and it burst open, and began to swell greatly
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I went for help, and for a long time I thought, and could not stop the wound.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I put on strong dressing, and out came a bone, and after a while another.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I marvel indeed, for in this belly there is no bone.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	I thought it was the bones of a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em millor point; et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu; et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	And I saw the woman long tense in the belly; and it was indeed a great burden for her; and I have never known of this chapter except for the fact that whenever the master finds an unusual thing, he calls for help.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	when he had to reset the shoulder joint to its place.
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a .ij. tornans as .ij. chiés des .ij. liiens.	And after that comes the form of pressure, which we find in the books; and to-day there are two tears of blood from two veins.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux; et soit li bouche dou fust I doi de large, et li marge des arbres I doit, et de lonc une palme et demi; et enmi les II liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus; et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les II cornes.	However, the horns should be more subtle than restrictive, and should be made of ebony or boxwood; and the mouth of the vessel should be wide open, and the margins of the trees should be wide, and long a palm and a half; and between these two limbs there should be two anchors of the same kind, which are firmly closed one against the other, half a palm long or more; and these two anchors are placed in the mouth of the vessel to open when the two horns are twisted
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles; et ait as II chiés II ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et II dois de large; et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor I lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes, puis boute les II ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes; puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	Another form, more subtle and lighter in appearance, is made of ebony or boxwood, according to the shape of the nails; and has two chiés and two ajostemens, as you see, of a palm of length, and two of width; and when you open the mouth of the instrument, if you make the woman sit with her legs together and her feet apart, then insert the two ajostemens together into the mouth of the instrument, and hold the head of the instrument between her thighs; then grasp the instrument with your hand, as if you had made the nails even, according to the quantity you see open the mouth of the instrument, until the bail makes what it wants.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	These instruments are all very burdensome, and their resemblance is multiplied; and when one sees them appear, one is more hasty in their work and more anxious about the quantity of them.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	If one does not despair of the instrument when it does not appear, for its necessity is not easily excused
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis; et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	When the second is retained in infancy, if you command the patient to keep her breath, and then make her cough forcefully, and hold your hands over her mouth and nose; and if she spits out, that is well done
Se ceu non, si prent I pot, et fai I pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire; toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris, et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	If this is not the case, take a pot and make a hole or break a vessel, and put herbs in it that can open the mouth of the mare, like chamomile, rue, anis, camomile, cassia and centaury; all these herbs, or any of them, should be boiled or cooked in water over the fire; then put in a camphor or broken vessel at the bottom, and the other head in the mouth of the mare, and hold it tight until the vapor comes out of the mare; then make her sneeze, as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	If the second joint is seized with pain.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature, et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction; mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	If she remains after this treatment and there is no further pain, as I command, tell the patient to moisten her left hand with oil of sesame or mush of alum, and then put it back in its place, and repeat the process; and when she has found it, grasp and stretch it towards the front and towards the back, so that the mare does not neigh at the extraction; but it is permitted to move slightly to the left and right, and then treat her. If she comes and becomes quiet.
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes; et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire; mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon; si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	If the mouth of the marris is swollen, we have said the treatment is to stop the discharge and fumigate with herbs; and if it is not of all that we have said, do not use anything else; but it is necessary that what is at the mouth of the marris, that you bind it to the woman's hip, then clip it with oil tetrafarmaçon; if she will hold and restore, it will come out; however, whenever she has pulled, if there comes a bad smell from the stomach and the head, and bleaches the patient.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	If it be necessary, then fumigations are useful in this case: neither of the ancients have proved the efficacy of fumigation with fennel and dried figs.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The form of the instrument in which we fumigate the woman is to retain the flowers and secondine if it is this:
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu; et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	It is like a wasp, and put the head under in the nature, and the large bones over the fire; and either fumigate over the charcoal, and the cloth as long as it is consumed, and start another.
de percier lou fondement	From the root to the ground.
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac: si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche; puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many children are born who lack the firm support of a proper foundation, and they have been stamped with a subtle mark. If you wish to cure such a child, do not prick him with a sharp needle, and do not pull out the mark; keep the dressing in place so that it does not touch. Then put on a soft layer of linen soaked in wine and oil, and then apply the poultice until he is healed.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	If you doubt that it will stay in place, put or draw a weight on it, and hold the hands still, and let the limb rest until the pain subsides.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	Under no circumstances must you stop treatment for wounds or abscesses; if you do cover the treatment: if either is cured, as we have said concerning the weight.
de la fistule dou fondement	of fistula from its foundation.
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	Fistulas that arise from the foundation are nodules, and those that arise from below the foundation are more serious. If there is a fistula or several of them; and when the nodule is old, if it is to the rear, and has abundant moisture or a pale or swollen mark, and never are these fistulas harmless; they are known by the fact that they cause vomiting or diarrhea whenever the patient vomits or passes urine, and by chance when one leaps forward.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	If there are fistulas which break through to the bladder, and half way up the thigh; and reach as far as the joint of the hip, and even to the knee.</start_of_turn>
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant: et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	And thus one knows about the fistula persisting at the root, and not going away: that you bite your thumb index or root and insert a subtle needle of spider or iron into the fistula when there is no swelling.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou I poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit; et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit: saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	And if there is swelling, if you insert a soft pad or a horsehair, as long as you feel the swelling or pressure at your thumb; and if you do not feel it, and there is no pain or discharge of pus or wind, as we have said: the wound that does not pierce does not heal; do not delay the cure.</start_of_turn>
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula persists up to the bladder or the urinary tract, if in a leap the urine escapes, and cannot be retained by medicines.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu; s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement; et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	If it is pierced up to the joint of the shoulder, if there is a vein there; if there is no swelling and only the pain of the wound, if it has been correctly diagnosed, and there is no other medicine or support by oil; and in these persistent fistulas there is no cure except labor, and the folly of the fools who interfere.</start_of_turn
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre; puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	In that which is neither new nor old, hope of health lies by fire, as I have seen; and that the patient lies between your hands upon his back; and let the legs rest upon his thighs, and incline his thighs towards his belly; then make an attempt to pull, or to plunge if there is torsion, until you grasp or the attempt comes.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans; si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	If the patient feels pain at the root, if you must bite your index finger, if you sense that the attempt has been perceived; or if the scapula or bone is discovered or if you feel between your thumb and index finger the flesh or bone, then grasp that it is natural; if that does not suffice, we cannot heal it.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc; et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit; et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil; et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	We can do nothing to heal it well, but this is what is done; and the help that we make, if we scald the cautery gently as it is said beforehand; and put all around in the fistula, until it comes out from the root; and do this twice or thrice, until you grasp that these hairs must be burned, which are like a bundle of hair; and then treat with soft compresses until that hair is gone, and then treat with ointment covering the wound and stitching.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If he is unscathed, that is well.
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez; et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur; si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente; et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	If he is uninjured, that is well; and if he tries between, and does not pierce until he has reached the root which is either the foundation or the nail, and between his thumb and his index finger put on a thick covering of hair or chaff, and you will see the fistula at the root of the covering as if from a wound; if you cut off the commencement of the fistula, and hold it down before attempting, and then burn with the cautery afterwards, until it reaches the head of the attempt; and the attempt will be delivered, and he will recover.  Then defend those hairs that appear like a bundle of oilseeds, and there will be nothing left.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if he does not move from you, and stands between you and the work, if you cauterize with fire or medicine at its peak.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor; puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe; puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	For the fire cautery brings together two things: namely, the burning of these hairy hairs, and the stopping of blood and drying out moisture; then the treatment of soft swellings filled with blood, which are either burst or broiled with broken bones; then cure wounds with oily ointment applied in abundance, and these are the dry medicines
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For when it is restored, if it is sound and does not return.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if a fistula comes up to the root of the bone, and is pushed out of place, if its bone or root is fractured, inquire about that.</start_of_turn>
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres: ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit; puis le cure, si com nos avons dit; par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé; puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues; puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	If thou feel the attempt, and between two fingers is the nail or the thumb or the carpus, or it is near to pierce, if there be no other remedy but the passage of time and hope, by the administration of one of the three methods: either thou cauterize it as we have said, or thou bind it until it is healed, or if thou wilt, thou shalt put on some attempts and cure it as at first; and do not delay too much, for thou wilt cover only that part which holds the foundation, and bring forth the discharge in its natural order; then cure it as we have said; by chance if thou art cured, or thou remove the covering and the mucus then when it is bound away from the foundation, or by attempt or by any other pointed instrument; then defend that which is forced from the wound, as thou wilt; then study to restore the wound and to stop the fistula in the part following the foundation: if it be a less grievous thing for the patient.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	And never are fistulas according to this method: when you bite the attempt in the fistula, and it is either costs or lies deep under the skin of the underside, if you take a bite pierced at the head according to this form:
Et i boute .i. fil tort en .ij., et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And there is always a thread torn in two, and you must hold the attempt at the very end of the fistula until it is at the head.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement; et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II; et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent; puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	And never are fistulas according to this method: when you bite the attempt in the fistula, and it is either costs or lies deep under the skin of the underside, if you take a bite pierced at the head according to this form: if it is grasped in the margin of the foundation downwards, then draw out the thread of that which is pierced, so that you bite your thumb or foundation; and pull the head of the thread, and gather the two ends together, and constrain one to the other, and leave it one or two; and do not restrain at any time, until these threads cope these hairs that are between the two, and cease to prick; then cure the wound until it is healed and healthy.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not perforate, if you force it to perforate in every way you can, it will not be too much harm.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it is not proper to make the wound wider by force, and then to cure it, as we have said, while it is still healthy.</start_of_turn>
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans; et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	The spine is formed of a spiny column which, if it is moist and soft from one side and hard and rough from the other, will not hold together. For this reason it is not worth attempting to hold it together.
des emorroydes	Des emorroydes.
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors; et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz; si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines; et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot; et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere; ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement; cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere; et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	There are two kinds of hemorrhoids: either they are fixed to the foundation like grains of resin, and are small and large in number, and adhere to the stool; or they are detached from the foundation and the root of the foundation. But those which are detached have some moisture, and are accompanied by blood or yellow bile or stool, and have a yellow color; and the cure for those which are fixed to the foundation is for the patient to strain to pass feces until the foundation is forced out and the threads are visible; if you are hasty and grip too tightly, or if you hold it with your finger, then it will split at its roots. If it cannot be held by its moisture, you must support it with a drape or cotton wool or a piece of chamlet; and you must pull it out, then grasp it, and powder the area with hot powder instead of cautery; or you can cauterize it as it is described in the treatise of cautery, because the cure of other cures is when it is healed. And if the foundation cannot be cured, if you bite the patient with a biting and rough clistere, you can extract what is above the foundation, if it can be extracted openly; but if the patient cannot endure this, and if the threads are forced out of the foundation, if the cure is simple, you must grasp it with your finger or grip it, and pull it out, then cure it as described above, until it is healed and the incision is closed by the iron.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc; puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose; et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If you wish to bind the shoulder according to this method: take one thread and pierce it through a needle, then pass the thread through below and remove the needle from the other side; then take two threads from the needle and if they are large, strain the thread taut. Then knot the thread and remove the needle, and make sure to secure all the others. Leave one thread to correct the excess blood; then place upon the foundation a bandage moistened in rose oil or cerate, and place upon the foundation. Command the patient to rest; and then leave him until he screams, and when he screams, if you apply the remedies for swelling and other remedies, until he is healed.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	When the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	For in the work of this chapter, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient; et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If you notice a bruise on the side of the heel or at the nail, which does not let it swell; then cure it until it is healed if it is possible; and if it does not heal, if you must repeat the scraping more forcefully than before, until it becomes soft, and is bleeding; then cure it until it is healed.
dou fremit	When the physician hears the patient groaning.
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont; et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	Formice is a small fleshy growth that appears before the bone, and goes out from it like a worm; and never does it leave the bone, and it is felt as if dead from its weight, and comes throughout the body, and more so than in any other part.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor; puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	And the cure is that you take a splinter of goose quill, or a strong feather, and put that splinter on the wound, until it circles the wound all around; then pull your hand back until you have grasped the wound all around, and put it out, and scrape the wound from its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	If you see that he does it with a spider's thread or iron in this fashion, be subtle and withdraw your hand.
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	If you see that he does it with a spider's thread or iron in this fashion, be subtle and withdraw your hand, for it must hold firmly and press.  If you see that he does it with the fire cautery, if it is before or alongside the cautery.
de la forme dou clistere	of this fashion.
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	Never make a blister of silver or gold, or of spiders’ thread melted or twisted; and never make of these instruments small or large, as they are presented.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Those who are feeble and painful in the treatment of children are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	Their form is small and great if it is excessive; or the belly is bound up in this manner:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I; et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre; et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	And if there is a swelling or the belly is tied up, if you see, and if the head of the shoulder is either pierced or cut; and if there is one perforation on one rib and two on the other; or if the belly or the intestines contain medicines from a bladder or parchment, and if it is cut all around, there must be between each perforation one space, then pass in these perforations one strong thread of strong thread twisted into a cross or around like this; and assemble the belly as if it were a hoop. And when the medicine is inside, if there is an instrument before a strong thread, then clench. This is the shape of a circle.
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement; puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	And let neither the medicine be too hot nor too cold; anoint the head with ointment of olive oil or beeswax, or something similar; then press it lightly; then grasp the minister with both hands together, until it is well seen; then draw out the ointment, and leave the patient his legs exposed, and if the medicine sees that it suffices, if the bite has become smaller; and if he sleeps all night long, if it is more effective.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see him lying in sickness with a swelling of the belly, and the physician hastens to leave, if he resumes as soon as he is well.</start_of_turn>
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	And if there is bruising or swelling, or an abscess, if the ointment is as subtle as for a young child; and this is the form of subtle ointment that is applied when the skin is taut:
des plaies	wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have already said in this chapter the treatment of wounds; or you may call it the treatment of hands and medicine, according to their completion.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse depending on what causes them, and depending on the limbs or wounds that are made, and how they are made
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	The things that cause wounds are biting of stone, or of nail or tooth, or lance or spear or sickle, or similar things; or that are made in accordance with the laws of the body, as for wound that bites on the cheek, or on the head, or the ear, or the belly, or the liver, or similar members; and I will tell you the cure for a wound of the head, and I will begin with simple wounds, for the memory will come back to you in this chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	I say that when a simple wound comes or a fracture occurs, and the bone is not broken, if you take care that it is not from a stone or other similar things, and the skin is completely ruptured and the wound is large, and you doubt the cause of the wound itself: if you do it too soon after the fracture, it will make the head of the limb even sicker if it comes from the wound itself; or let the blood flow in the opposite direction of the limb; and listen to the patient’s swelling of wine and fatty foods.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it does not heal, if it is becoming withered, and does not drink wine, does not eat meat, do not put anything on the wound, except to soak it in oil or wine that has been stipped; and if there is no further bleeding, put on the wound, while it is fresh with all its blood, and it is not moved by air, dust, or anything else; I will tell you about that later. If it has been moved, put on some ointments, until it is healed
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is great like the size of a spear and similar, and the limbs do not naturally unite, if you unite them with sutures, as I will say, for wounds of the belly, with sutures.</start_of_turn
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	If the wound is exposed by the bone, and is raw, and holds only by a thread, if the head of the bone has slipped; then cure the wound with medicine, and restore flesh in place of skin, and command the patient to eat coarse food, such as meat and bread, as well as poultry, and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	And if you find or skin putrefying, and there is no sign of bone, if the head of the bone has slipped, and the wound bursts forth; then cure the wound and if there is an artery in the wound or vein, which cannot be held by medicines, if you cannot stop the bleeding, and if you find it dislocated, if it is held by a thread; and if this does not help, then cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, if it is a slight cure: put on this powder that solidifies just as well as it was moved.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	The method of the powder is as follows: take incense one part; dragon’s blood two parts; live chalk three parts, and grind the powder finely, and apply it to the wound, and hold it firmly, until it is well closed and reunited with all its blood; and then bind it well and leave it to drain, if it does not swell; for we do not apply medicine until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And never shall one do this treatment alone, when there is neither incense nor blood of a dragon, but only when the wound has not moved.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound has moved, even in this state, if one does not put on this powder; but put on some unguents digestible, or poultices made of flour of barley with water and honey, until it evacuates pus; then cure with other cures until it is healed.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	And if a fracture occurs with the wound, and it is small, if you grasp the wound slightly; I will tell you about the fractures later.</start_of_turn>
de la plaie dou col	of the wound of the neck.
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If there is no difference between the fracture of the head and the fracture of the neck, but if the neck or the artery is cut
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	If the nerve is affected, if there is no other injury except to leave the wound open, and do not put anything restraining, because it hinders the nerve and makes it shrink; do not put anything rough on the wound, for the substance of the nerve is cold, and its continuation is with the brain, which is the most tender limb; but if the medicine is strong, like hot water in sweet water, and mixed with rose oil, and rue that is washed in sweet water, and other stones of mine according to this manner, and moist unguents.</start_of_turn
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, if the blood vessel and the nerves are torn, then cure as long as it is healthy.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu; et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est; et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel; et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier; et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue; et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	If the wounds are deep and bloody, and the edge is chipped or swollen, if the artery is cut, and blood flows freely; if the bone is fractured, and the marrow and the cautery mix, if the cartilage of the throat is cut, or the nerves, and the thread is grasped, by which the meat goes; if the nail of the thumb is fractured, or the bone is fractured at the root of the thumb, do not touch the throat but restore it to its natural position; then strain it immediately, and leave it untouched for some days; then cure it with oil until it is healed; if the wound has made an imprint in the bone, if there are pieces of bone, if the fragments are too numerous, do not remove them; leave them as long as the wound persists, and let it drain naturally; if the wound is fresh, sprinkle it with powder as I have said.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there is bone in the wound and there is fistula, if the wound must be closed as I have said in this chapter.</start_of_turn>
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of a wound from a lance or a knife.</start_of_turn
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	If it be of lance or of knife, and the wound is deep, if you see that from the wound wind comes out violently, that the patient cannot endure: draw out the arrow immediately; for if it is not deep and is fresh throughout its extent, if you do not put in at the first hour the powder, do not bind it up with the flesh any more, but return to the body and comfort the patient; but put in an astringent, and bind it twice round; if you have no astringent, put into the wound fine cotton to absorb moisture, and make the patient rest upon the wound for three days, or four, or more; if there be no spasm, do not move the body or cause any straining. When you see the bones in their place, draw out the arrow that is saved.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	Cure the tonsils and other cures, as long as they are sane; and if they cannot be cured, and if there is an opening, remove the pus that there is fistula; if the cure is like this.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	And if the wound is from a cut or a knife, and it is simple or deep, at the front or at the back, if the cure of what is before; if it is great, with stitches; and if it is small, with powder, and if it is pressed into the bone, and has broken pieces, if you wish for the wound, and the surrounding tissues are inflamed; and if they are not inflamed, if you leave the wound open, if it will align the extractions; and for other wounds, as for other members, it is judged like this.
dou derrompement dou ventre	indeed
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	The swelling of the belly is great and medium and small; from a great wound never does the intestine go out, or does it remove the intestines, because of the introversion of worms; and the suture is more painful, and never is it worth more than a small wound than a great one, because in this case we must return the intestines more often, and because of this the intestines swell up so much that they feel the fruit, if we do not return them gradually; for this reason the smaller wound is better, because we can keep the intestines in their place as with other things. And pus that comes out of the belly is according to three methods: the two common sutures come together in the suture of the belly, and the suture of the other wounds of the flesh and two other sutures are common with other wounds; and all of them are more proper with the suture of the belly. And I say one thing and declare.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	I say that when the wound is small and nothing of the intestines is pressing, and only a little pain remains, this may be remedied in two ways: either by the smallness of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestine is distended by the fruit.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	When it is cold, soak the part in a mild manner: moisten a sponge or drape it in lukewarm water only, or boil in lukewarm water stinging and spiking, and elevate the intestine until the swelling subsides; and never do this with excessive force, for it is harmful if you overdo it.</start_of_turn>
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	And when you see the swelling subside, if the intestine is moistened with water or elevated and the veins are cooked, for by this is the entrance to many things aligned; and if it cannot enter, if you make a hole in the wound with the instrument, grasp the blood clots; and the first cure is to make the wound small, for we must not cut excessively without necessity. This is the instrument for cutting: if you cut too deep in the curve and it does not come out, and if you do this too much:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is swollen, and the intestines protrude outwards, if you stop bleeding in accordance with the natural form in its place, know that you have done well, for this is enough.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	And when the wound is large, and it is in the lower part of the belly, if you order the patient to lie on his back and raise his legs above his head; and if it is in the lower part of the belly, put his head and shoulders above the lower parts, and in the same way if the wound is in one of the two lower parts, put your hand under what is above so that the upper part is higher than the lower. And thus you must manage what I have said in great and small wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	In small wounds, put on what appears to be between the hands, I mean a bandage which holds all the edges together; and this is the common method of stitching, and take a needle or several, according to the quantity of the wound, then leave a space at the head of the wound equal to the width of two fingers, and pierce the two holes of the leather with the two holes of the needle, which is from the inside of the leather, as long as you make it pierce through that part, and gather the two heads of the needle together with three threads; then strain with a double thread around the needle at two parts, then gather the two edges of the wound together again, and then leave a space, and pierce another needle; then tie the thread as you did for the first needle, and do not cease doing this until the wound is completely held together; and let the needles be neither too fine nor too thick, for the fine needles will hold all the flesh, and the thick ones will not penetrate well: for this reason they should be neither too fine nor too thick; and do not push the needles too far into the flesh and leather, for they will not hold and will open the wound before it is sutured; and then gather the edges of the needles, so that they do not hurt the patient while sleeping, and put on patches or bandages at the holes of the needles to prevent them from slipping, and leave them on until the wound is healed; and this method of stitching with needles is more convenient in small wounds, for there is only one needle or two at most for the second stitching, and that you gather the two holes of the leather and the two holes of the needle together with one needle or with a strong middle thread. And when you have pierced these holes together with three threads, gather the needle at the part or where you began, in the manner in which one would cut the threads; and leave space between each stitch equal to the thickness of a finger; this stitch will hold the flesh, and I stitched a wound once which had a cut or wound from a knife, and the wound was more than a palm of good size, and it was intestines well two palms of good size, and the wound was in the middle of the belly.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I shall bring back the intestine when it has been out for twenty-four hours, and the wound has healed for fifteen days; then I shall cure it, and it will be healed.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	And he had thought that it would die, and this was a miracle; and I did not cure him with medicine, for I was in a place where there was none, neither drugs; and I put on the wound two times a day, and bathed it with honey until it healed.</start_of_turn>
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	Or you will say the two proper ways of stitching: take the needle and pass it through the part behind until you reach the nail on the right side; when it has pierced the nail head straight through, if you have pricked the skin or if you have pulled the needle, and you have passed through from the other side of the part behind until you reach the nail; and you will understand this stitching if you stitch like a skinner, and that you leave once the nail head on one side, and you take hold of the nail on the other side, until the stitching is complete.</start_of_turn
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	The second method of stitching, which Galiens does in this fashion, if it is done without any other, that brings together the two parts naturally, and joins one of the ends to the other end, in this manner: pierce a needle or the end of a thread close to the next, and pass it through only the lower part, and leave the two ends; then withdraw the needle and pass it through from the back to the front until it reaches the middle, with two ends; then pass through one and the other from the back to the front until it reaches the middle, with two other threads that are on the other side; and this is the most perfect and common method.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	Galiens says this by experience, and no one can testify against him; we must suture the belly with two needles, or there is yarn in the hanks; and we must push one needle from one side and the other from the other side, in the manner of those who suture wounds; and if when the belly is turned inside out, the suture is tighter than the others on the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	The judge of the wound is like the judge of other wounds: and it is that when you find the wound fresh with all its blood, even if it has moved, if you stop the intestines and the cost, then put on the healing powder and charcoal; and if it has moved, do not put on any ointment that is present, until the wound has healed; and close the wound, and solder the edges, and the surrounding area; then cure the wound like the others, until it is healed. And if you have no medicines, put on only what will cause the wound to ooze blood, wool, and move twice the amount that it would otherwise.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	You need no other medicine in many cases where wounds are simple; and if you doubt that the wound will not heal naturally as it should, cover the principal parts with coarse linen soaked in warm oil of tempor or rose oil, and bind the edges firmly; and if there is pain or swelling in the belly, and this happens often, if you give the patient wine vinegar, in the same way as if the swelling came up to the intestines; and if it comes up to the large intestine, it is easier to heal than the small intestine.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The intestines which are called "jeuns" cannot recover when they are swollen, because of the swelling of the veins, and for the subtlety of all the body, and for the proximity of their nature to nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres; et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres; puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	And if blood spurts from the wound, if you bring it back again as soon as the intestine, while it is fresh; and if it is black and has become towards or black, if you must tie the black part, for there are veins and arteries there; then close what is between the bone, and hang the two ends down from the edge of the wound until the bleeding stops, in order to align the extraction when the blood spurts out, and the wound contracts.
de la routure dou boueil	Of the root of the boil.
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance; et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez; je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	When the intestine is round and the wound is small, if you can restore it among the ribs, because I have seen that one bone has been swollen or pierced by a lance; and the wound was at the stomach and became filled and turned into an fistula, and in this there was evacuation and vomiting; I treated it according to what I could, and did not cease to soften until it was healed, and the wound healed
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre; et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans; et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere: pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus; et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise; et cout la plaie.	And when I see it soldered, I doubt that the patient has no harm in his belly; and there is no point of harm, but there is delay in many conditions, and foods and drinks; and they say that no physician has ever observed that when there is a small wound in the intestines, it must be ligated in parts: take tweezers of great capacity, then gather the layers of the wound, and when the tweezers have passed over the mouth, if they are put on the second layer, if it stretches its mouth upwards; then close the mouth, and this is kept until it can be released, and put another suture afterwards in the same manner as before, until the wound is whole; and close the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere: pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure; et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance; et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	If the chief [of the intestine] burns in the intestines, and there is no nuisance to the patient, and it can be ligated with a fine thread which is cut from the intestine of a beast, in parts: take the chief of this thread of intestine that is quite free, and then tie at the chief of this thread one thread of linen turned, and pass the thread through the needle, and in sew the intestine, and retain it in its place; and this manner of stitching with tweezers is not fierce but according to the way of fate and hope; and if the wound is large and wide, just as it is in one of the large intestines, if there is no danger or infection, except for subtlety.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	Of fistula or that it be
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	Wounds and abscesses, when they swell, if they are called universally 'fistules,' and even when they are sewn and rent bowe.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil; et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse; aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez; et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes: c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors; ou por sa malice; ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char; ou il i a trop de bowe; ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit; ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure; ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence; ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature; ou il i a voinnes ou os: et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	A fistula is truly a nodation that is hard and white, or one for which there is no pain; and it is just as tightly closed as a bird's quill; and never completely closed, sometimes loosely closed, sometimes tightly closed; never half-closed, sometimes rather open; and I have already spoken of this in the division of wounds, that every wound that is not healed, and there is no swelling, is only cured by one of the seven causes: that is to say, by the smallness of the wound or the swelling; or by its malice; or because there is a hard swelling within, and on the edges, which does not allow new swelling to arise; or because there is too much swelling; or because the blood vessels are contracted, and the matter is of poor quality; or because the medicine is not good in the cure; or because the corruption is of the nature of pestilence; or because the property of the region is late in digestion and late in healing, and flees by nature; or because of veins or bones: and I have already mentioned all these causes, and their signs, and their cures in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	Or you must know that I will tell you the cure of fistula which is made by an egg of hands.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors; car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez; et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	Wounds that occur in all limbs with pain; for there are wounds that arise from great veins, and arteries, and nerves, or at the hip, or in the intestines, or the bladder, or in some of the ribs, or on the spine, or at no joint of the hands or feet; and if they reach the property of the main limb, and the rest.
