Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance; et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier; et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit; et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie; puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent; et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens; et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons; et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	All the wounds of this kind are grievous and do not readily heal, except by toil and ignorance; and if there is no wound that does not reach beyond what I have said, and you have hope of a cure, and you see it diminishing, if there is an opening like an hair, for the wound is straight; and if the wound is deep, if the surrounding tissue attempts to cover, for the swelling will fill the cavity around the curvature; and if the wound has opened wide and you do not know how to close it well, if the clot comes loose from one of the openings, for the moisture is short from one opening to the other, and it softens; then leave the clot quietly, that you may know if there is bone or nerve, and is chewed out, and ask the patient of the pain he feels at the touch of your hand, the place or where he feels it; and when you know truly the place or if it is far from a joint, or a nerve, or an artery, or a vein, or in any of the things that I have said, if the dressing adheres to what I have said, and bones that are forced out and corrupted that are within; and then cure until it is healed, and if the wound is well deep and straight, if you can close it as well as you can, then put soft patches on medicine water, and keep them until the medicine consumes the superfluous that remains at the bottom; and then put oily dressings on the wound, until it is healed; and if it is not healed by this, if you must cauterize as we have said, and if the bone is corrupted from the wound, if you can close it.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit; et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font: si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu; et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If the vein or nerves are not affected, or the principal limbs, as we have said; and if the bone is discovered to be fractured, with corruption and blackness, if the limb remains as long as the corruption is throughout the bone, then cure the underlying cause of the fracture as long as it is sane; and if it is not sane, and if it cannot be restored as before, extract the bone until it is level with the surrounding parts; if it is fractured and the bone is exposed as much as possible, uncover the fracture and restore the limb as before; and if it is finally sane, it is well.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir; si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature; et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un; et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	If the corruption is too deep, it will not recover; if there is no other remedy except to leave it to its natural course; and if there is only a small fracture, and you wish to handle it with tension, if the extraction is made with a suitable instrument, and if there is still a bone remaining, do not leave it there without support; and if moisture opposes you, and there is no doubt or fear, then hold, moisten and support, and deliver the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os; et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie; et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os; si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez; et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	If thou dost not hold them fast at an hour, set upon the wound some things that cause putrefaction, and leave them until the flesh is quite consumed about the bones; then there will be less pain in the bones. And if it be a great bone, as a limb or thigh, if thou dost stretch the corruption as much as the marrow is whole, then restore the wound; and if there be much of the bone that is corrupted, go right up to the marrow; if thou dost cover it with silk and cover all until the corruption is gone, then cure it until it is healed; and I will tell thee of a fistula that happened to a man in his leg, so that thou mayest take example and help in thy work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir; mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors; et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors; et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	There was a young man of about thirty years of age who had pain in his leg for a cause that came from within the bone, as the matters went up to the leg, and he escaped from a great abscess, but found no cause to fear from opening; but he thereupon went mad with fear of opening more than was necessary, and they corrupted a great deal of matter, and there became a fistula, and there came out much pus that all the physicians thought would kill him. And he remained sick for two years, and there was no skill in the hands of the physicians, as far as I remember, until I went away from there, and saw his leg and the medicines they were giving him, and what cured him of the abscesses; and the color of the bone became red, and it had the color of citrine.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I bound a loop in one of these holes, and then circled around all the holes, and found that one followed the other throughout all the parts of the limb.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens; je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai; et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder; et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu; mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	I then bound it in one of the holes until I discovered a portion of the bone, which I found corrupted and rotten, and it extended from the corruption to the marrow; I took away that which appeared to be corrupted bone, and I thought there was no further corruption, except for that which I had seen; and I began to restore the wound with soothing medicines for a long time, without being able to close it; and then I repeated the process, and again I discovered corruption in the bone as before, and I treated it, and then I stopped. I thought I could close the wound, but as long as I bound around a palm of the bone, I could not do so without damaging it, so I left it as it was and restored it with medicines. It healed and closed without any further recurrence, except for the weakness of the patient, who could not bear the pain, and for fear of death which I had avoided for him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	For often is blood evacuated with the opening of a vein, but it was entirely sound, and in place of the bone there grew a hard scale, and it was in good condition and suffered neither pain nor disadvantage of any kind, neither from the fear nor from the coming.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere: pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut; et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char; et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue; et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	And if the bone is fractured in no place of pain, if you wish to bandage in this manner: take I thread and strain at the head of the bone which is open, and command no one to extend it upwards; and put I another thread of cloth more coarse than the first, and bind it upon the scale which is departing from the bone, and extend the head, so that you tear the corrupt scale away from the bone, and uncover the scale above the place where you see the bandage; and put I cushion or a plug of lead behind the bone to cover the corrupt scale; and bandage as much as you can see and feel the corruption, and bandage again.</start_of_turn>
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute; puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit; et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part; et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper; et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert; et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire; et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce; et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument; et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies; si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	If the bone is corrupted and will not open, and the corruption is in the middle or in a part, uncover the marrow all around; then put on a pair of gloves and with one hand from the one part to the other, spread the corruption as far as you can; and if the corruption is in the joint, if you join the corrupted joint, join the bone or what it contains from the other side; and if the corruption is in the continuation of the two joints, if there is no other vein except the one that covers; and if the corruption is in the palm of the hand or in the heel, if that is strong, but whatever you do, inquire about the cause of the corruption, how it appeared to you; and explain it in every way you can, but let neither the vein nor the nerve hinder you; and cut the skin and the hair covering these bones are many, according to the strength of the bones and the appearance of spots, their thickness and thinness, their greatness and smallness, and their hardness. And for this reason it is necessary to look like the work of an expert in this art, and to rely on the testimony of the methods of diseases; if you think the instrument is appropriate according to this, then believe it.
dou feu	indeed fire.
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer; et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre; et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	The head of the shoulder is dislocated by moisture, by pressure, or by violence; and when you have treated that corrosion by the means of medicine, and it avails you not, if you cover that limb until the corrosion comes, for if the patient escapes by this means of death, or by the greater malice of the defect of the limb; the sign is that the limb becomes black, as if it were burnt by fire, and afterwards comes the blackening, because that corruption of the limb extends throughout the limb and seizes the whole body; if you are hasty in covering, and if that is by the percussion of some venomous creatures such as scorpions of the sea and vipers and the like, if the corrosion is at the top of the bone, and you do not give it space to come down to the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras; et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut; et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe; et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet; et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil; et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort; et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers; puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	If it comes down to the hand, if the cope is at the joint, so that the corrosion does not come down to the forearm; and if it comes to the forearm, if the cope is at the elbow; and if it passes the elbow, that is death, and there is no remedy but the quantity of its virtue; and do everything that the corrosion comes or does not come: if it comes in the first joint, if the cope afterwards comes in the second joint; and if it comes or does not come, if you cope all the limb; and if it is in the thigh, if you cope at the knee; and if it comes below the knee, there is no other remedy but that the patient should die; and you must bind up the limb tightly from below and above, and extend one minister from the lower line and another minister from the upper line, and you must dissect the flesh between the two lines to a span of one thumb, until the bone is exposed; then you cope or bind, and put a bandage on the part that is stripped of hair, so that the bandage does not touch the sound limb, and comes to the patient other injury and incision.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet: il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet; et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez; et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions; et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere; et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez; et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	If blood flows from a wound when working, if you cauterize the flesh immediately, or put on some restraining powders; then return to your treatment until it is complete, and bind the limb securely with a strong ligature, and treat it until it is healed; and I will tell you that at home one time: there was a blackness that seemed to burn like fire, and that corrosion began in the heel of the foot, as far as it spread throughout the whole limb; and when we saw the corrosion, if we covered the limb, it healed; and when the corrosion returned to the heel or the foot, we repeated the procedure after the inflammation had subsided. And we could not stop the corrosion; and we had to amputate the limb, and I did not wish to give up hope of saving the matter; and indeed I doubted that if I cut off the limb, it would not die, for the power of life in the body was weak. And he awoke, returned to his home, and covered his limb, and was healed; and I have never heard of anything like it ever since, except in this case.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe; et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz; et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»; mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»; et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz; et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	Never comes abscess in flesh alone, and remains so long as it makes great swelling of the bow; then it bursts and breaks, and in leaping the bow, and it bursts the vessel, and remains bloodstained like a vessel; and the leather that is under is as fragile as a cloak unfurled, and does not move until it reaches the bone, not until the nerve, and such is the disease called "sain," and is not called "fistule"; but if it is so long as to reach the bone and burst, it is called "fistule"; and if the leather is such that you press it, even though it is fragile, like a cloak; and it does not yield.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi: regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite: prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel; et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus; et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant; fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor; et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez; et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet; ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain; et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin; ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens; et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez; et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	If you suspect that the leather has hardened, and the corruption is not in the bone, and the leather is thick as flesh, if the surgeon of fistula is present: look if the abscess is large, and the swelling that is in it is foul-smelling, then make a plaster of Egyptian medicine which is made like this: take alum, oil, and alum, equally, and mix the leather in the vessel over the fire, until the medicine is red, and becomes as thick as honey; then take some of this according to your need, and make it in water and honey, and in plaster, and strain the pus; and leave the medicine for two hours, then strain it out; do this several times, until the abscess is drained, and the swelling is gone; and never plaster with vinegar, when this medicine is not present; take vinegar of pomegranate seeds, and vomit, and the pus will flow out, and plaster, until you are certain that the abscess is healed; and if the patient cannot tolerate it, neither the Egyptian medicine nor the vinegar of pomegranate seeds, if the plaster is made of vinegar and honey or there is a little bit of alum broken; or plaster with honey and wine, which has the property of softening and washing away, and the wine makes the abscess dry out; and when you have done this, and you are certain that the abscess is healed, if the plaster that you made brings pus to the surface, take powdered diaphoretic, and make it with oil of rose and wine; or plaster with any medicine or unguents, of which I have spoken of their properties or how to treat them; and if the pus that comes out of the abscess is little, and the can of the plaster will not enter, if you expand a hole with a needle, and put in a patch of Egyptian unguent, or basic balm, as much as it is expanded; and if the wound is too wide, if the edge and it leaves only a little skin or the plaster can enter, and if the pus that comes out is below the surface, if you press or lower the wound than it is.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char; et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe; et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain; puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois; et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste; et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez; et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	When the bow is in the joint, if you do not leave the hair, it will stick; and if you do not cover the root of the hair as you see, it will appear in such a manner that the bow will go down lower than it is, for when the bow is in the joint, if you do not leave the hair, and if you do not cover the root of the hair as you see, it will appear in this way: that the bow will go lightly forward, and will leave nothing of the hair; and take solidifying medicines to put out the blood, and keep over it a layer of lint that covers all the blood; then close up the force at the place where it was opened up more widely than before, because there are often soft things under the other drape according to the quantity of the opening, and put the other drape over the blood to align the bow, and do not open the great drape more than once; and the one who is outside the blood often bones the bow, and tears off what is left of the hair, if it is poison or blood or enough, or digested or indigestible; and take care if the patient feels pain or not, and if there is swelling or not, and when your medicine has reached its limit and you see the nature that comes out on the blood, if the blood has already clotted, and approach the health; and then take off the bandage in the morning, or the third day, and when you take off the bandage, if there is another drape, renew the dressing.

Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire; et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie; et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine; pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance; puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu; et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire; et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use; et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens; si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	For in some cases, there are late inflammations of carbuncles in their wounds, and those that do the opposite; and if the pulse is too late in rising, the veins do not swell; and if the veins are too late in emptying, they are stretched, if there are excessive medicines containing moist and dry substances, as diapnit; for there is a great part of vitriol in it, which is the last medicine; take diapnit and mix it with rose oil and the juice of five wines of equal substance; then confit and use. de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the abscess of the boil.</start_of_turn>
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois; et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute; et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	Panarice is an abscess that originates from the swelling of the pouch of the hand, or the armpit, or by chance arises in other places; and when it is inflamed and no precautions are taken, if it comes to an abscess of the thumb, it swells and protrudes so much that it reaches the root of the thumb, and by chance it swells all the way up to the bone; and there comes pain that is like a wound, and the head of the thumb is large, and the colour is dark.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	When you have treated it as we have said in the division, and the cure does not help, if you must, you must do everything that remains to be done from the swelling, and then cauterize the wound afterwards.

des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	And never has this vein had hands rain, even when it opens at the elbow, or at the wrist, and there comes forth blood spurting; cure it as we have said before.
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	This ailment is called in our land "buffalo disease," because it often causes swelling of the buttocks, and is a small vein that originates between skin and flesh, and runs throughout the body, upwards and downwards, and is felt on all parts of the limb, until it breaks the skin or comes out, and spurts blood; and is accompanied by the discharge of various humors, such as blood clots, worms, and pus or belly-ache; and there is doubt of its malice, because when it travels through the body, and reaches the head, and comes out at the oil, by chance it returns and destroys the oil; and this often happens.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture. Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis. Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles: je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	Leave the hairs long and even; if they prick at their base, keep the eyes still until they grow.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit; et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition; je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	And take out an arrow from the home, that was in the flank or belly, and I thought he was dead; but when he had passed XXX days, if he had not recovered his former state, I cut on the arrow, and I engaged it, and I pulled it out, and there was no mishap.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus; et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	And if I see an arrow in the home which has fallen out or back, and if the wound is deep; and I put the arrow back into its place, and I do not confine its natural inclinations, I find no discomfort in any of its natural works.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie; et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	And I saw another man, who had an arrow in his face, and the wound was deep; and he suffered great pain; and there were other symptoms.</start_of_turn>
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	And I pulled out an arrow from the king’s prince who was lying in the middle of the night, and it was a declining sickness to the lower part; and the arrow was perfectly healed. I went to see the doctor afterwards when it was evening.</start_of_turn>
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	If I find the wound very painful.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie; et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	I shall take hold of it with all my might, and will not feel it; and there will be no sensation of pricking or pain in its vicinity.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast; et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	I thought it was an arrow wound. I put on a supportive dressing to digest the swelling, because of which the wound did not swell; and I saw the arrowhead emerge
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	I put on the dressing with my hands, and restored the wound to its proper position, and kept the patient long in tension, until he felt the arrow still inside him; and he confessed it to me
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement; et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir; adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	I put on the corrosive medicine on the wound with my hands, until it was burnt through, and held it, and felt the tip of the arrow that was in the flesh; then I closed the wound with the medicine, until the tip of the arrow became visible; and it remained in that state for three months, and then it grew so wide that I could not keep the nails on, and I had to remove them from one side and the other, and I could not bear it; and I did not cease to suffer and groan in various ways until I had set the nails firmly, as it is written at the end of this chapter, until I had treated her, and restored the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	And the physician judged that the cartilage of the nose could not be restored; I restored it then, and the wound was sutured, and the patient was completely healed.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	Or you have spoken of the quality of the extraction of some arrows, if you place your cure on that which I do not tell you, for the books do not teach me all; but you masters know well many great things, and what is present and lacking, find nine works, and a new instrument, according to the things which happen in this art.</start_of_turn>
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	I say that the arrows do not come out of members or are hooked except in two ways: either by the root or by the head; and that which comes out by the root or enters, is an arrow which has pierced flesh, and never comes out again.</start_of_turn
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And if it does not move now, let it grow until the hairs are fully grown; rejoice in its issue; and if it is fixed in the bone and cannot be moved, leave it alone for a few days, and move it little by little; and then it will move. If it does not move, pierce through the entire circumference until the limb is fully swollen, and then draw it out.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	If the hair is caught in the bone of the shoulder and goes up to the belly of the brain, and there are some things which I have already mentioned to the patient: if you do not draw it out, but leave it alone until it is even after a few days, for if the hair comes up to the surface, that is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	If the hair is only caught in the bone and does not come up to the surface, and remains fixed in the bone for several days without any other mishap, do not force the drawing out.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is firmly fixed in the flesh and cannot be extracted, if it has been there for a long time, as I have told you; then cure the limb until it is healed.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente; et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble; et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans; et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire; et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	And if the splinter is lodged in the flesh and cannot be seen, if it has all its force; if you feel it, if the wound has no visible instrument covering it; if you cannot grasp it by the edge of the wound, and by the depth of the splinter, and there is no bone or nerve or vein, if the pain is as great as the wound itself; then draw out the splinter as you can. If there is an ear in the splinter that holds it, if the cartilage that is attached to two parts of the muscle that you grasp is broken or bent, break or twist the ears of the splinter as much as you can, until you can withdraw it. Be subtle so as not to break the splinter, but draw it out more firmly.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you do not do it once, if the limb is already swollen, then grasp it more firmly, for the extraction will be joyful.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre; et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	If bleeding from a blood vessel contradicts the treatment, if there is contamination of what has been said in this chapter; and beware of the incision of the nerve and the vein, and put in place what you must do to remove the splinter without danger, or straining, or tearing, or rigidly or limply; and keep the patient in the position in which the splinter was when it was evacuated, for that is the greatest aid that can be given, and if you do not succeed, let him remain in the position that the sign shows you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment: taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	The bandage comes forth from another place, or it shows no mark of having been opened, or the skin is swollen in that place where it is seen or felt: let it be known therefore that it must be cut off as soon as possible.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is retained in the bone, if you twist your hand round and round, until it enters the bone, and widen the bone, then withdraw it.</start_of_turn
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer; et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust; et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	If it cannot be grasped, if you leave it in, and then resume the extraction until it comes out; if it has been pulled out entirely, if you pulled out all the hair; if it has been cut, and you see it slipping, if you see it slipping, you must immediately administer some instrument with a hook, so that the point of the bandage enters the hook; and then pull out, and if the bandage is hooked, if it is hooked on the point entering, to relieve the extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	And if the bandage is soiled, if you must cover all the surrounding fat or the venom is there, if you wish, then cure the wound as it should be cured.</start_of_turn>
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope; et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est; et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If the splinter or piece of bone is close to the skin of the belly or bladder or ribs, and it is near, then you must cover over it with your hand; and hold the wound and the nerve firm, then extract it, and then close the wound, if necessary; and cure as long as it is healthy.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	And the shape of the tweezers with which we treat the wounds is similar to the beak of an osprey, and thus is the form:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And there are various kinds: large, medium, and small, according to the quantity of the wound
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The shape at the end of the bone is like that of a bird's beak, to push out the tip of the splinter, as it is like this:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	For to stop the bleeding at the tip of the arrow, if this is the shape: the form of a clamp to stop and to hold if it is like this.
des voinnes dou cors communes	it is common for veins to bleed when they are opened or cut.
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir: II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»; et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans; et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»; et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis; et les II guindeges qui sont ou col; et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»; et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	There are veins that one should not touch, which are sixteen in number: two veins that are behind the ears, which are called "herbaces"; and two arteries that are in the temples that appear; and two veins that are in the armpits, which are called "aspirates"; and the vein that is in the forehead; and the vein that is at the top of the nose; and the two veins that are at the collarbone; and the two veins that are in the arms above the mouth, which are called "augeheriches"; and two veins that are under the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras: l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	The veins which we commonly speak of are five in each arm: one is the cephalic, and is on the left side of the costae, and they call it the lying vein; the middle one is called the fast, and is composed of the cephalic and basilic, and they call it the lying vein; and the basilic is either on the right or left side of the costae, and they call it the lying vein of the belly, and is above the epigastric, and it is that from which we speak, which appears manifestly above the pouch.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains; et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei; et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	And the saving vein is the one between the auriculaire and the annular, and if there are two veins; and in the leg and the foot there are three veins: one is on the inside of the cuboid of the left costae, and the second is the saphenous which is at the ankle of the right costae; and the vein which is called the “nesse”, which is in the ankle of the other costae; and in the other leg there are three veins like these.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine; et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief: quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche; puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues; puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee; et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	The blood of the veins that are behind the ears is useful for ancient purges and emigration; and the quality of the blood, as I have said, is that you raise the head of the patient, and wipe the hand or the veins are of a rough texture; then stretch the patient’s neck with a thumb, until the two veins behind the ears in two leaps depend from the head: that is to say, when you feel the pulse down there, if there is swelling, then take the lancet, and prick through the skin until you reach the bone, then hold your hand over the entire vein, and compress and the skin and the vein well together two must pass through; and make the bleeding cease as much as you see; then strain and bind, until it is healed; and I have already said the incision and the cautery or first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz; et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis: et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement; et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche; puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit; puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton; et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	The blood of the two arteries that are in the two temples, if it is like an ancient emigration, sode, and obtalmia accustomed, and at the root of the tears that are salty, is as follows: if the patient strains his neck, so that the two veins open widely; and he feels the pulse stop in his thumb, then he should sign with his thumb on the vein at the top of his thumb, and remove the lancet from his thumb, and the vein at the top, and the clot, as he has done in two other veins, and correct the bleeding according to his need; then he should loosen the patient and put his thumb on the vein for an hour, then put on a compress; and then the swelling will subside, and let it stay until it is healed; and we have spoken of this in the book concerning their swelling and extraction, or their beginning.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor; et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere; puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	The blood of the forearm in front is worth as much as that of the cephalic vein has ancient diseases of the face, has an embolism, and has redness; and the quality is that the patient strains his neck by twisting, as long as the vein opens. Then take the instrument which is called the "burr," which is like this:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues; puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	The blood of the forearm in front is worth as much as that of the cephalic vein has ancient diseases of the face, has an embolism, and has redness; and the quality is that the patient strains his neck by twisting, as long as the vein opens. Then take the instrument which is called the "burr," which is like this. Place the point on the vein, and hold it with your hand, or with something else, and let the blood flow as much as you see fit; then release the patient's neck, and ligate the vein until it is firm and never let the work be done with a broad flame.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	Whatever, I say that the flames must not be too strong; and the same through, because the bone is close, and by chance breaks the flames when it is subtle.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice; et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant; puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	The blood of two veins that are two cubits in length helps with the swelling, pain, redness, and swelling of the armpit, and with facial ailments; and the quality of their blood is such that if the patient strains his neck by twisting his head, as before; then the same, and let the blood flow freely, for there is no char.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	If the flame is stubborn, by chance if it breaks; then draw out blood, as much as you are able, and then bind it up tightly, and bind it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree; et c’est li forme dou flaime:	The blood of the vein that is nearest to the armpit is worth as much as water, and has bad swelling, and facial ailments such as migraine and redness that comes to the face, and the same even when it is old; and the quality of the blood is such that if the patient strains his neck, and then strains his shoulder on his left side, and grasps the flame subtly long, and puts it between the two nostrils, for the vein does not open very well inside, and it will not begin to correct now; and do not push too much, and correct the bleeding according to your need, then bind it for a night, for it is much better to restore it then; and this is the form of the flame.
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit; et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est; puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	The blood of the second pair [of veins] helps in the swelling of the groin, in the beginning of mumps, and in many diseases, and in swelling, and in corrosions, and in herpes, and in stones; and the quality of the blood is that when the patient strains his neck alternately, as we have said; either the master is standing above the patient's head, and the patient sits on one seat, then grasps the vein long and widely, then pulls out the blood gently, or as much as is necessary; and then repeat the operation in the other vein, then release the thread, and strain moderately the middle veins, so that the patient does not strangle; and leave it until morning, so that the wound is healed.
de la sainie des leivres	The blood of the armpits helps in the swelling of the groin, in the beginning of mumps, and in many diseases, and in swelling, and in corrosions, and in herpes, and in stones; and the quality of the blood is that when the patient strains his neck alternately, as we have said; either the master is standing above the patient's head, and the patient sits on one seat, then grasps the vein long and widely, then pulls out the blood gently, or as much as is necessary; and then repeat the operation in the other vein, then release the thread, and strain moderately the middle veins, so that the patient does not strangle; and leave it until morning, so that the wound is healed.
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The blood of the veins of the upper limbs helps to clot in the mouth, and to corruption of gums, and fissures of the lips, and toothaches and pains.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit; puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires: cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	And if the quality of the blood is to make the patient sit before thee, and restrain his neck as I have said; then turn the liver, and look at two veins, one on the right side of the liver and the other on the left, and know them by this that they are black, and that they have small black veins running through them: so do one and the other; and if you do not know them, and you are in doubt, if one of the largest parts of the spleen is pale, and both veins that are below and above are pale, for this is the same method.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	And if the quality of the blood is to make the patient sit before thee, and restrain his neck as I have said; then turn the liver, and look at two veins, one on the right side of the liver and the other on the left, and know them by this that they are black, and that they have small black veins running through them: so do one and the other; and if you do not know them, and you are in doubt, if one of the largest parts of the spleen is pale, and both veins that are below and above are pale, for this is the same method.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche; et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire: saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	The blood of the veins that are outside the tongue helps afterwards the blood of the cephalic vein; and it is at the widening of the throat, and has diseases of the eye, and has diseases of the mouth; and the quality of the blood is such that if the patient touches between his hands before the sun, and he touches the tongue, and looks towards each cheekbone, he will see a black vein: both of them, and do not go too deep, for they are the arteries.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres: ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»; et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	The veins that we commonly liase are bled in two ways: or by making a large, blunt incision with a knife, or by making a slight incision like a trench, and it is called "anesil"; and they are large and slight according to the size and widening of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The flame of fire is soft if it is mild, and is broad as you see.
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble; et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	And must be skilled in opening the veins that are full of thick blood that shows, and that contain much blood and trouble; and this is the form of the olive flame.
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and is more pointed towards the tip, and is for the healthier veins, or where there is little yellow blood.</start_of_turn>
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre; et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	The blood of the basal vein, which is one of these veins, helps to cause diseases such as hoarseness of the throat, swelling of the jaw, pain in the feet, and swelling of the belly; and it is necessary for the patient to remain calm and to staunch the artery that is causing the bleeding.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit; et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	And if it severs the artery, and blood flows profusely, if it is necessary to check, as I have said; and it must not be grasped too tightly, but held as gently as an aneth.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre; ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement; et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	And if the basal vein does not open visibly, if you must grasp it, and tie another; or you wish no more blood to flow, or you substitute for it the vein below the arm: it opens visibly; and grasps the flame gently, as we have said
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz; puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil; et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	If you see the blood vessel swelling, if you must draw the arm, touch the vessel until you know its size; then mark the vessel, and then bind the arm, and apply pressure to the vein with the flame; and beware not to pierce the artery when you see the vessel swelling, for it is the artery: shut off the flow.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere: haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient; se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	If you see blood spurting like the urine of a child, and it is white and transparent, know that there is no artery involved: hurry then, put your thumb on its length, and press your thumb until it stops bleeding; if you leave it untouched, it will happen again; bind the arm, and leave it still, do not move the patient; and be cautious, do not move until it is healed
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	If it hangs loose and does not bleed, and the physician is not present, if the artery bursts open, for the shoulder joint recoils; grasp it without touching it.</start_of_turn>
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor; se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc; et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	And take a piece of sponge, and wet it, and take half of it and bind it well up to the other end; if it is without stain, it is well done; if not, if the physician wishes, as we have said, powdered substances which stop blood; and the clotting does not occur in many different ways for the small quantity of the wound, and the tension of the limb.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit; et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner; et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	The blood in the vein in the middle helps to stop bleeding from the head downwards and from the ribs, because it is composed of the basilar and cephalic veins, as we have said; and it is proper for the patient to keep warm for the nerve that is below, and if it does not keep warm enough, and it finds the nerve, it swells and the blood is either clotted or by chance cannot heal; and this nerve opens many times, and if it does not open in some people because of its slightness, it is necessary to cauterize the vein with an instrument that is able to stop bleeding; and withdraw the nerve from your hand.
Et se il a voinne entre les .ij. ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is a vein between the two nerves, if it has a long loop.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz; et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	The blood of the head helps, that it draws blood from the chief, and helps the eyes; and it is recommended to cauterize with the olive flame or the myrtle flame, for these are the safest of all veins, for it has neither nerves nor arteries.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence; et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	However, it is recommended to inquire cautiously the first time, and grieve nothing if it does not succeed the first time, and we begin again; and by chance it swells up at some homes, which cannot be remedied the first time, but it grieve nothing.</start_of_turn>
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the blood is according to your thoughts.</start_of_turn>
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir; et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique; et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent; et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	The first thing you must know about healing is that blood must not be let out except to preserve health and to ward off future diseases; and it should be taken from one of the three veins which are either close or connected: namely, the cephalic, the facial, and the basilar.  It should be let out at the beginning of the prayer, and after meals and during yawning, when the sign of repletion appears; and it should be let out in the morning or in the evening, after two hours or three hours after sunrise.</start_of_turn>
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens; et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	The blood that is administered for diseases has no fixed dose, but when necessary is for the most part in the morning or at dusk; and it must not be given to children under twelve years of age, nor to women who have been menstruating for more than four months up to the seventh month.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez .lx. ans.	One must not strengthen the ones who have passed sixty years.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz; ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques; et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors; puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir; puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit; et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses; et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans; et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on; puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	When anyone sees a physician, in whatever way, if he commands the intestines to be evacuated with a mild enema, if he has retained a fever, so that the veins do not draw out the humors from the principal parts; do not give him more food than is necessary, neither too little, for it is harmful; and if you give him medicine after eating, vomiting, and purging of the belly, and many times at night, and from working, from keeping watch, and from journeys, and all that is like this; then subtilize the humors, when they are not too great, by food and drink and medicine, if you can; then give him a bath or sponge, so that the blood is withdrawn from the lower third, as we have said; and keep him from work, from eating, and from luxury, and from other things; and bind and soothe him, and let the physician be above him, and wipe his hands twice or three times, and then draw out the thread gently, because if it is too tight or too loose, it cannot be corrected without; then wipe the blood from his hands, until the veins swell and he feels them; then moisten the physician’s hand with a little oil, then place his thumb of his left hand on that vein below the elbow for a moment or two, until he sees the blood flow.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus; et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	For there are veins which flee even as strings to the physician, and if there are such as are filled with windiness, that when one puts on the flame, it retracts from the flame, and cannot open the vein, and thus is this; and if one opens the vein, if the wound is too wide, for this one must advise the physicians in these matters.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	If the vein bursts the first time, that is good; if not, if you start again, take hold of the limb or the patient, for if it does not swell.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras: par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait; et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement; et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	And if the limb is inflamed, and the patient groans, and leaves one hand or two, and does not bind the limb: by chance there will be abscesses of nails; do not enter or bathe, then restart the bleeding if it is slow; and if the wound is slight, or without any notable swelling and you doubt that there will not be as much blood as you see, if you believe in that wound itself with all the flame directly; and the work a little patient, even if the limb is inflamed; for this often happens when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile; et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc; et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	If you see the limb inflamed, if you do not wish to renew the bleeding, put on a patch of lard of oil, for it softens the flesh of blood; and it sticks to this limb the lard that is in the oil; and give the lard of oil in the wound that you may stop the bleeding of the veins, to stop the course of blood; and this itself makes a scab and swelling of the eyes, when it is put on the limb; if it is too subtle it will tear when it is too thick.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre; et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie; et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	And if there comes a large abscess, which often happens, even if it is not seriously infected only when the opening of the vein is small, if you are in a hurry, put on the limb a soaked sponge in water and a little charcoal, and hold it for an hour; and cover that you make this after the bleeding of the vein has stopped, and if it remains in the limb after a few days no blackening or greening, if it does not harm me; and if you see that, do not put anything else of aloes or mastic, but show the monster, or something like that.</start_of_turn>
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	Many times there is swelling and blood appears at the root of the hair: put your hand there, and if you feel the root is loose under the pressure of your hand, that is a bad sign.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai .i. emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Do not put anything on it that we have not mentioned, for by chance without an artery; but make it dry again with another dressing, until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	Treat each wound according to the quantity of its virtue, and the color of the blood.</start_of_turn
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if it is black, leave it to fester as long as it is red; and if you see it large, leave it until it is delicate; and if it is too thick, let it cool down.</start_of_turn>
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges; et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant; et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And it is to be commanded to the one who is calm and strong, and has the skill of extracting blood, to make the wound larger, and let the flame be great; and to the one who is weak, do the opposite, and keep him sound rather than risk it, and must be kept sound by cutting through, not by pricking; and this method of bleeding is better than leaving the wound large.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And to the one who needs food during bleeding, it is commanded to give soft bread soaked in pomegranate juice; if he is exhausted, let him bleed three or four times. And if he is pale of complexion, let him beforehand soak the bleeding with soft bread in mustard, or in aromatic honey with spices, such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and cloves, and a fragrant syrup.
