Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	If he pricks at the blood vessels after the evacuation of blood, it is necessary to know that he will spit frothy bile, an odoriferous sweat, and use other things that we have said in the division or chapter of syncope for the evacuation of the vein.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if he sees his arm turn pale, and recovers again, if it is known, when he is filled with great blood, that he must rise up and rise up again, according to the quantity of his continuous virtue.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine .vij. houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And whoever has seen his arm swollen after the first bleeding, and has great pain, if he stays like this for three days after the first bleeding, or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And whoever has seen himself recover from the other side, if he must recover by the second or third day.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson; puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens; et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus; ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz; mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	For there is blood in the body which is already pale, and causes fever; if you are to draw out a great quantity, and expand the wound as much as it bleeds; then that when you have stopped all bleeding, and put your hand on the pulse when it is well, the blood does not reappear in place of the blood that has been drawn out; this often happens when the patient is negligent; and you must not do this if you see the arm slipping, and make the wound bleed for the second time, for the wound is closed; you must press firmly upon it. If it is crooked, extend the arm fully, for that would be bad; but leave it as it is until it bleeds for the second time; or prick at the tip of the flame, until the blood that is congealed at the wound is expelled from the vein, and put some water on it, and press lightly.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein has escaped, if you leave it and do not restrain me, as long as the incision is calmed.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if necessary is to drain blood a second time, if the same in this limb or in another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein in the arm is stained in leu of the vein of the head because it is composed.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges; puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc; et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez; et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit; et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	And thus the manner of the blood is such that if the patient grasps his hand in warm water, until the flesh is red; then it is to be bound moderately, so that the wound opens well; then draw it out again, neither too wide nor too long; or make a large perforation, and bind it close to the joint of the hand, and if it cannot be drawn out, grasp the hand in warm water and leave the blood to flow out until enough has drained out; and if this is done, do not draw out the hand in warm water again, for more is put into it than in this state; and the blood of this vein is more saving than all the veins, for there is neither artery nor nerve in it.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere: estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie; et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	The blood of the salivary vein of the right hand is useful for all the diseases of the liver, and this is the method: strain the hand and grasp it in warm water, until the vein is emptied if we see it; and if it is drawn out, and if you touch it throughout, do not grieve anything; and do not move too quickly, for the nerves are almost naked of flesh, and then grasp the hand in warm water, if it is not frozen in the wound, and cannot be drawn out.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have treated the blood as much as is necessary with the cautery, if you put oil and lint on the wound to close it, do so carefully.</start_of_turn
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The blood in the left hand is worth the disease of mice, and do the same as I have said before for the upper part.</start_of_turn
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The blood of the armpit is worth for all diseases that are in the chest, as with diseases of the marrow, retention of flowers, disease of the reins, and of the calves and the ancient legs, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains; saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	And the quality of the blood is that if the patient has become pale in hot water, and has frothed on the vein until it goes cold; and lies under the joint where the bone is affected; and the vein is at the ankle, and from under the bone go out drops of urine; the like or more the rain, or at the ankle, that the blood is worth.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you keep it healthy on the bone, if you guard against the nerves that are over-moistened, and the limb remains whole just as if you were grasping; and let the flame vanish.</start_of_turn>
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if it cannot be kept in place, if you reset the bone in water, and let the vein drain well.</start_of_turn
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz; ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	And if the patient must urinate for the first time, if he begins the second time from under a little while, because the urine is salt; do not doubt, as we have said, and do the armpit of the other side equally
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The pulse of the sciatic nerve is at the ankle of fire, and its blood is worth the pain of the groin, when it is for blood that is hot.</start_of_turn>
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant; et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	And if the patient be sitting or bathing, and he strains downwards to his ankle three times in bending, for otherwise the vein will not open; and if it opens, he must do so in all possible ways, both straight and across; for it is better to burst the vein than to leave it unclosed, for it is bloody and will swell up at home.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners; et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	And if you do not find that any blood flows from it which will open or drop out, towards the little toe, and you keep watch over it; do as much as you can for the blood, and then loosen the ligature, and put on a bandage, for it is now healed.</start_of_turn>
des sainies de ventouse	of bloodletting
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc .ij. manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Ventuses are made of horns, or hair, or glass; and the suction must be performed according to its manner: either by cutting and drawing blood, or by cutting alone.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu; et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col; et II autres en II costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton; et li ventouse des II espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies; et les ventouses emmi les II bras; et les ventouses des II jambes; et les ventouses des II chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne; et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	And this bleeding which is done according to two methods: either at full speed or slowly; and the bleeding which is done by cutting and by extraction of blood is done in twelve days from the commencement of the disease, of which one is at the top of the head; and the other is at the back of the head; and two at the cost of the head; and the bleeding from the chin; and the bleeding from the two shoulders; and the bleeding from the armpits; and the bleeding from the two arms; and the bleeding from the two legs; and the bleeding from the two ankles; and the bleeding does not touch any great veins which are spread throughout the body, and for this reason it does not cause death, as is done by the bleeding of a vein; and it must only be administered, neither at full speed nor slowly, in no disease which comes from repletion, until all the swellings have disappeared.</start_of_turn>
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens; car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief; et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz; et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc; et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	And if necessity of illness compels him, or by custom, if the physician notes that the patient has choked for an hour at the beginning of the month, or at the end, and sometimes throughout; for there are some who, when they must vomit, have a heavy head; and there are some who feel swelling and redness in their face, and in their head and neck, and dark circles under their eyes; and some who have a mouthful of blood, and have spat out the tongue and vomited blood; and some who dream, and see blood and vomit and death and other things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés .iij. houres dou jor.	When these signs appear, and even if it is only lightly moist, we command the patient to wind after two hours.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors; et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement; et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	The patient’s blood if it helps with the headache … comes from the eyes; and it must not be done until after the evacuation of all the humours; and this vomiting is useful in place of the cephalic blood, and must not be done by those who have a cold complexion or who have choleric temperament, for this makes them suffer much discomfort; and for this reason it must be done cautiously in those who have cold or choleric diseases.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And for this reason I advise you not to use it on patients suffering from cold or severe diseases
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion; et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	The air of the head is in place of blood and fat, and because of this it is worth the stretching out of the head, the incision of the neck vein, and all, and bloating; and it is enough to push, for if it holds too tightly, it causes aversion or nausea of the head or belly or body.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	The air of the head is worth as much as the pains of the head, vomiting and fainting, strangulation, and toothache; and it is in place of the blood of the fat; and it is enough that you order the patient to raise his hand to prevent him from spitting, that he does not cut the artery, and does not vomit blood.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des .ij. levres.	The vomiting of the stomach is if there is a disease of the mouth, and corruption of the gums, and similar diseases that are in the mouth; and is in place of the health of the two upper teeth.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The winds of the spleen are harmful to health, coming from heat and congestion.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes; et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	The air of the armpits is worth as much as three veins of the arm, because it draws blood from these large veins; and order the patient not to press too deeply, because it is full of flesh, and knows nerves and arteries.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The wound on the buttocks is of great importance, as it brings swelling to the foundation and causes diseases. It is therefore necessary that the vacuum be large and of fine mesh, and that it be well applied; for if it is too subtle, it will break and cause great damage.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des .ij. sophenes, et des .ij. chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The wounds on the legs swell widely, for they draw blood from all parts of the body, and cause ancient pains of the rains, and of the marrow, and of the bladder, and soften the flowers; and are in connection with the joints of the thighs and the calves, and all of them weaken the body after a long time, and cause vomiting in various positions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The method of applying the vacuum is that you must first empty it, and then put it on quickly and firmly, and move it equally, and do not cease doing so until you see the red liquid and swelling, and open the wound of the blood; then close, and put the vacuum back on, and take care of the body, for there are such people who have a very tender temperament, and clear pores: if you must cut once only, it is better to make large wounds and a deep incision; and do it gently
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir .ij. fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if it is not large, it is sufficient to wound it thrice: the first time to uncover the great blood vessel.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if it is not very thick, it is sufficient to wound it thrice: the first time to uncover the great blood vessel. And when our veins swell with blood too much, too little, if we only suffer once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif: se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite; et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	If our veins bleed excessively, if we renew the process often; if the wound is not suspected, if it is fierce and deep, and if it persists even when the cause has vanished, it befits one who has thick skin and hard veins, and who has many pores, that you apply the leeches of oil aperitif and dissolvent: if it is in summer, oil of violet, or sweet almond oil, or oil of pumpkin seed; and if it is in winter, oil of cresson, or radish, or chamomile, or similar.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the swelling is large and cold, if you take amaranth oil, or balsam oil, or rue oil, and the like.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	If he has a tender pulse and large pores, one must not put oil on, but it is necessary to wash afterwards with rose water, or cold water, or lime water, or pumpkin seed water, or porcelain water, or something similar.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And if there is moisture in the mouth, if it lifts easily, or with vinegar of myrtle, and sumac, and similar things.</start_of_turn>
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans; et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	And those who have excess of humours rise from wine strong, or from the water of sedge, or from a decoction of rue or chamomile, or from other things similar; and do not let the physician put on a vacuum before the bath, but after the bath an hour or two; and do not sleep after the ventosation, but let him wake, when he should wake and when he is waked.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez; si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses; et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	And guard those who are pale are bilious, and if they are not too great and inflamed; if it is to be taken that they take cold things, as with pomegranates and radishes and lettuce at ease, and other things; and eat barley meal, and mutton broth, and moist meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons; et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier; et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz; et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	And those who have a cold complexion, if they take syrup of honey, and fragrant wine middle between strong and new, and eat poppy seeds, and eat barley meal and small oilseeds and grapes; and when he is to be purged, he must drink more than eat; and let him give to others no more than three times at a time before or after the ventosation, for to comfort the principal members; and be discreet about it, but let him drink only those who are hot drink it
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	The wounds which are made to bleed are those which are made upon the liver, and upon the spleen, and under the kidney, and upon the belly and the groin and the thigh and the heel, for in these members no wound is suffered above the joints, and it is done only to draw blood from member to member; as when we put them upon the nipples when they do not bleed; to remove the viscosity which is in the member; as when we put the cautery upon the belly and the groin to shorten the member; and to stop the pain, when there is an opening or stone, for it attracts the opening by its attractive power or evacuates the stone from its place; and thus it is raised up when it is put upon the liver and the spleen when there is retained moisture. And these cautceries are administered empty without any liquid, and never are they administered together with water, except in cases of pleurisy, and in such a manner we fill the cautery with warm water or with water or with herbs which are suitable for this.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the wound administered with fire is as follows:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	And he has two large and half palms of barley, and has or costs almost a whole penny, as much as to push out an awl; and let it be of rye, sow before if it does not bleed the patient when putting it on the limb; and in the middle put a thorn of rye or iron, to put a bandage firmly in place, and be large or small according to the ailment and the degree of these who take it; for the blisters of the sick are other than fat, and leaner than fat.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	And must put this bandage on the limb: grasp the bandage of silk or linen, and put it into the ventouse through the thorn that is in the ventouse, so that it does not burn the patient; and then put it on the limb, and must put either on the puncture that we said, so that when it is seen, if it goes up, take off the ventouse; and grasp the linen as before, and do it often, if you must.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	In the ventouse therefore which is administered in the disease of pleuresin, at all intensity, there is no point of vein or perforation, and is only administered when it is full of water, and is placed upon the limb only so much; and this is its form.
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	They are not administered for any limb where we cannot place a ventouse because of its small size, such as the liver and the gums, and similar things; and where the hair is removed by shaving, such as the groin or the nose, and other things; and the quality of the user is such that when you find veins that are soft and smooth without any puncture, if you take them; and put them in fresh water, until they are limp, and do not have anything in the belly; and then either drain the vein and the ventouse, or massage the limb until it is red, and put the veins back on; and when they are full, and swell, if it is possible to put the ventouse on, put it on, for this is worth more afterwards.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	If not, if you lift the limb easily, and then with some sharpness, moist well, and then stretch it out; and if the limb still moves too much afterwards from the bones of the shoulder, if you moist a cloth of linen with cold water and put it on, as long as the bones are not extended; and if the bones are multiplied, if you put on ground vitriol, or splints, and similar things, as long as they are extended; or you take out half of the marrow bones, and leave them until they burn out in the limb, if you stop now; and if you have done more work than this, take other bones.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	If the bones do not cease to move, if you rub the limb with fresh blood, or you pierce it with a needle until the bone stops moving, and then put them back in place; as long as they feel the blood, if it stops bleeding; and when you see that they are bleeding, if you sprinkle on some alum and blood agar, or charcoal, they will stop bleeding now.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	This is the end of the text.
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	This chapter is often necessary in the art of medicine, and is restoration of fracture and displacement.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	Hear now, my son, for this treatise speaks of matters which none of the former books or letters have mentioned; and therefore it is strange in our land, for I have never found anything like it. I know of no other way to learn it except from the books of the ancients, or from my own studies and experience. And I have set forth in this chapter what is contained in them, and I have abridged it at the end, and I have made the forms of the instruments clear, as I have done in the previous two chapters.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	Therefore, I say that the prologue of this book and the chapters contain the essence of the word and that the learned man who reads and comprehends them will find true understanding, for those who have been proven to be skilled in this noble art and have learned it well.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	I say that when there is a break or dislocation or twisting or fracture comes to no limb, if you command that the patient hasten to recover the limb on both sides, if nothing else hinders, if there is weakness of the limb, or swelling, or old age; or if the tension is not very strong, or too cold; and mix with cold baths, that is to say cold showers, and fat of fish and herbs, and do not drink wine, do not eat greasy foods, and do not eat too much meat which fills the veins of blood, until you are certain of having stopped the bleeding, neither of the expansion of matter in the limb; if the patient recovers before the first management which he used.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bones begin to restore, if you must know that you must nourish the patient with foods that make great nourishment, or that have viscosity, such as barley cooked in broth, peas, and beans, fish, eggs, cheese, and fat, and similar things.</start_of_turn>
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For at a part of nourishment, rest returns muscle and more easily breaks the fracture.</start_of_turn>
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	Know that bones that are fractured in pieces and decrepit do not easily reunite or fuse according to their nature because of the drying out of the limbs; neither those which are too tough, like bones of small children; but there is no cure, you must rest above the fractured bone a strong support that has occurred and join the limb together, so that it strengthens as if it had been before; and do not move it at all, for this reason it is recommended to nourish with abundant food, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that fractures are of various kinds in many ways.</start_of_turn>
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the fracture of the skull is different from that of the limb, or of the bone, and I shall tell you in this chapter all the ways of fracture.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there are fractures that go only skin-deep, and others by cutting, like the size of a needle to write with.</start_of_turn>
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if there is a fracture with a wound, and a fracture with a small tear.</start_of_turn
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	And at times like this, it has its own instrument and its own remedy in its restoration; as one remembers from its place. It is known that the fracture of the bone is recognized by its twisting, which opens well by pushing, and by the pressure of the hand; and when there is no twisting or pain, and the patient does not feel great pain, there is no fracture; but there can well be twisting, or fissure, or a small fracture.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	If you do not know with certainty whether it is twisted or broken, but only that the hand is moved, but put on medicines that will come afterwards, and then strain it now subtly.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	And the nails that break that go into the armpit, which are the two parts of the joint, it is now necessary to put them in order equally, even as after the postumous discharge; and if the postumous discharge comes again, if you leave no trace, as long as the postumous discharge is appeased; then put them in order with the muscle as you wish calmly and quietly, and the nails that restore the limb are lighter than the restorations of those who have pieces; then strain it, as it is necessary afterwards.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	And if there are broken bones in the bone, if they extend from two parts, as with hands or feet, or at your hand if it is a small limb, or at two strings, or at a string and at your hand; put the limb in its natural position, so that when the parts of the limb that are broken are unbound, if you remain by all means the adjuncts to the muscle as you wish, and keep that in your work does not cause the patient pain or injury; and adjust the two heads of the bones according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And feel well with the hand if you think that it is not well: if the limb is well stretched, and is not strained too much, do not press as those who make it come by their work to cause swelling and contraction of the limb, as we have often seen
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere; et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	And when the limb is at a point, if the patient is seized well enough he must not move it, neither while awake nor asleep, neither while turning over, nor in any other way; and take care that the limb is so securely positioned that it feels no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor; et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez; et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	For when it feels no pain, if it is not at a point, and you must put it in a position where it feels no pain; and take care that it is placed straight, that it does not twist when restoring it; and the quality of the limb depends on what I tell you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	The fractures of the limb are diverse in small and large size and in shape.</start_of_turn>
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz; et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche; puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure; et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet; puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus; puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	For there are small members, as hands and feet and similar: if you can cover them with soft linen and thin veils; and those that are large, as bones and legs: if you can cover them with a broad and hard cloth, because the large cloths embrace the whole great limb, and constrain it equally from all sides, so that there is no tension; then you must put on light compresses, three tours or four according to the limb, and constrain the hand one inch above the break, then go down to the break and constrain less, than the break has gone; and soften the limb above and below, as much as you take a large part of the limb back, then take away another cloth, and twist the bandage around the break; then put back at the bottom of the break, and constrain moderately, neither too strong nor too weak, as we said at the first hour above; then put between the bandages soft linen or veils, until they are even, and then bind everything up with a good knot, and put on your boots well made above, if there is no abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors; puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	And if there is swelling or abscess, if you put on something soothing for the abscess, and which softens the swelling, and leave it in place for some days; then strain over your eyes, and keep them half of a large cane's width apart, or of a fist of the kind that is made into cloves, or of barley-straw, and be in this position.
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres; et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor; puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure; plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol; car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	But it is necessary that the eye which is put on the fracture is larger and wider than the others; and be as long as it is suitable for the limb in breadth or length; then strain over the eyes just as you did at the first hour, and then support under a thread that will hold firmly; the more tightly it is stretched, the less; and let the thread be neither too thick nor too thin, and be of flax. For if the thread is thick, as if one wanted to make knots of coarse thread, it is a great mistake, for the thread will not be even if it is too subtle, and it will not hold firmly except when there is less space between the bones.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	If the patient is scorched by the nails after the stretching of the limbs, if you put on stockings of linen or coarse cloth, so that it does not bleed.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with a splinter, and the bone is fractured, I will tell the cure of that later.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And the wounds which he cannot restrain must be stripped off from these bones to break them first in order.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant; et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	For when the limb is great, it is not permitted for me to put these stakes in except after five days or seven, or more as you deem necessary following the opening of the wound; and when this is done, the method of ancient compresses must be restored to break fractures, dislocations, and twists: take flour that is held at the walls of the mill, and mix it with abundance of eggs, and make this confection, not too fine not too thick, and use it. This is the common method of the plaster that restores the fracture in various positions, and even among women and small children, for it is neither too harsh nor too rough.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .v. З.; alechil .viiij. З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another method of plastering which restores the fracture and dislocation and torsion: take three barley grains and linseed and acacia and asafoetida and gum arabic and mugwort, and mix them together; mix in half a barley grain of mirre and aloes, and half a barley grain of alech; and grind them up together; mix them with a lot of eggs; if the patient’s complexion is hot, use this plaster, for it is made of good materials and will quickly restore the broken bones, and is worth more than many homes.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.; acaice VI З.; bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another method of plastering that is worth for a twist: take mugwort and vinegar, nine parts; myrrh and aloe, nine parts; acacia, six parts; Armenian bole, ten parts. Grind them well, and mix them with water or eggs, and administer them.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Another method of treating joints and bones that swell, relieves pain, and reduces swelling of the bone and marrow: take new linen, moisten it in oil and put it on the affected area.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	These treatments do not restore health, but are good for relieving post-cautery pain, and bones properly relieve the pains.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Other methods of immobilization that restore fractured bones: take dried fig leaves and terrestrial poppy leaves, grind them together, and make a dressing.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another method of treating is to restore the fracture of the bone and to diminish the remaining post-cautery swelling.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Take root of chamomile, camomile flowers, violets flowers, barley flour, and marigold one part; grind them up, and mix with wine, and if the limb is bruised, mix with vinegar or water, and apply
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Other methods of restoring the limb are more forceful than the first, when an abscess hardens during restoration of the limb.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Take root of chamomile, flaxseed, balsam, melilot, and gentian, violets and chamomile flowers, all of which make one part; and grind them, and boil with salt water, or sweet water, or with wine, according to the heat of the limb and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	Ypocras in his book does not put anything on the broken limb to restore it except for some wax and oil, and nothing else, and he says that it should be between two things not too soft not too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems Galen recommends placing something dry and warm upon the affected limb to restore it, such as myrrh, aloes, incense and the like, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another method of dressing that is valuable for both pain and swelling: take mugwort and chopped onions, or pine resin, beeswax and smear them evenly, and broil them, and make a poultice from them.</start_of_turn>
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor; puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut; et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then loosen a little afterwards, and take care that the patient feels no pain, nor has his bone moved from its place; if you do not loosen by hand for days. And if pain comes to the limb, or swelling, without rest or inflammation, if you are hasty, loosen it and fix the displacement immediately; and put on a lighter bandage, and a wet sponge, and immerse in water, and lift the limb until the swelling ceases, and the pain is appeased; then let the limb rest for an hour, then put on dry linen, soaked in water or oil of rose, and bind with a nut, until you are sure the abscess has drained; and rest the inflammation of the limb, and be sure the pain is gone, then recommence the gentle binding, and a little displacement, and do not strain it so much as before; and take it slowly until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	If you see that the abscess is inflamed, swollen, red, and painful, and that it returns again after you have placed it and bound it, as you did the first time, then you must repeat the procedure.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir; arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	And if nothing comes to the limb from what we have said, if one must force it out, do not do so before three days or four or five or seven; and never leave it for twenty days, as we see, until the swelling has subsided, and the joint has adjusted to the limb’s position; then you must bind it more tightly than before, and swell the limb, as I have said before; and if you see the limb drying out more than usual, that the wound has become infected, do not attempt to remove the foreign body; then let the wound bleed profusely, every time you move it, until the blood flow returns to normal: thus you will correct the infection in the limb and restore the limb to its proper position. This is bad, and if such things are neglected, I see no other remedy than to leave it alone and do it properly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	from various breaks
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	Many are the causes of fractures, and diverse are their figures; for there are fractures which are made by percussion of a spear, and the collar of bone is fractured throughout to the sy facet which is the marrow of the bone, as in the case of a flake or splinter; and for this reason this kind of fracture is called a fracture of the flake.
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces .ij. brisures grans ou petite.	When the spear pierces the bone from the underside, and is called this kind of fracture "absolute"; and is the wound of these great or small fractures.</start_of_turn>
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is embedded percussion, or fissure or split of the bone, or dislocation of the shoulder or fracture of the bone, or other similar things.</start_of_turn
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a burst vessel, which approaches the gut that is adjacent to the bone, or it is on the bone, this wound is great or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»; et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	And if there is a wound which is closed in the bone just as subtly as a nail, and the fracture is slight; for this reason this kind of fracture is called a hairline fracture; and if the wound is made by a wound of stone, or by thorn, or by anything similar, and makes enter the piece of bone under, and is the bruise so great as when they make over a cauldron when they are boiling; if between the stones.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	And this often happens under those who have soft bones, like children; and in all these ways, small pieces break away from them like stars; and I will speak of this later.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And we know of all the ways of breaking due to the subtraction above them, the inquiry into tentatives, and the corrupted flesh which is above.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The capillary appearance is known by that which when we have discovered the bone, and we wipe on it, if there appears a black break.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of the break, take care of the patient’s condition, and if you see no bad accident, such as vomiting of bile, loss of understanding, extension, and swelling, and fever, and the eyes to become pale and flushed, and other similar things in various situations, if you cannot do otherwise
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	If you do not see an imminent mishap, and you hope for health, if so, commence the treatment.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	When you come to the aid first, and it is in sweat, if so, it is necessary to obstruct the bone before the fourteenth day over the muscle that you must support.</start_of_turn>
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	If it is in this state, if you haste to obstruct the bone before the seventh day over which the cloth of the bone is corrupted, then comes the accident that we have said.</start_of_turn>
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset; et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	And if a break in the bone comes up to the skin that covers the brain, if you must open the fractured part: take hold of the patient's head and uncover the bone in every way you can, and on the figure of the wound more roughly than you can; if blood comes out from uncovering the bone, or opening the abscess, if it helps, and fill the cavity with moist cloths soaked in rose oil; and rest the wound until the abscess is calmed, and be sure of the evacuation of blood; then as you start to bind up the bone, this is done in two ways: one way if you grasp the narrow end in front, and that is the form:
Et puis i boute .i. autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then there is another fracture more extensive than the first.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And thus if you have several different-sized lesions, some wide and others narrow, and some pointed and some blunt, and in an easy matter, without bleeding the head,
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou .i. cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des .iij. manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is firm and hard, if you must pierce through it, do not pierce it too close to the bone, but must leave a space or circle above the point, which does not allow the point to pass beyond the bone; and you must make several of these holes, for if pieces of bone come out in the place of the thickness of the bone, if you make holes too close to the test, they will break through the bone. And this is the form of the two methods of drilling holes:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes .i. tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The qualities for piercing through the bone quickly are that you put one hole on the bone, and turn the screw until you feel that the bone is pierced; then put the hole back in another place a little later, and do the same all around, and close the incision between the holes, making it more subtle than you could, and gently, as we have said, until you have moved the bone from your hand or from any instruments that you have like pincers; and keep your hand away from the brain or the jaw.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire; et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	And when you have grasped the bone firmly, and treated, if it is possible, reset the fragment which has been loosened from the bone to all other instruments resembling an incisor, but make it more firm and subtle than the other incisor; and if nothing remains of the small bones, do not remove any scales, if the bone is slightly fractured by the instruments; then close the wound with sutures and dressings as we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And another method of treatment is that of the Galenicians, which is more useful; and the load is very great, and this is its word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is necessary first that you uncover a portion of the bone, either where it is fractured or broken, so that when you have uncovered that part, put on gloves and grasp the handle of this incisor lens, for this is its form:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz; s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	Do not split the bone from one end to the other, for the part that is split into two coasts, if the cutting reaches the bone; then put a small mallet on top, so that you can grasp the bone lightly and hold it firmly in place; take care that the cloth that is soaked does not touch the bone, for if it is torn by the bone, the bone will be fractured unnecessarily, for it is well fixed in its place without pain.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if a bone breaks without piercing the skin, it is only slightly fractured from above; there are small pieces [of bone] which, if necessary, can be removed with a rasp of various sizes, to bring about the greatest possible healing, according to the work and the nature of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If there is a great deal of razing beforehand, and after that more subtly, and it does not cease to do so until it is well done.</start_of_turn>
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In some other capillary and subtle fractures, it is necessary to provide the cause according to its location; and this is something that is not usually known to anyone who has studied this art.</start_of_turn>
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie; puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement; et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication; et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	If the lip is discovered, then take a layer of linen, according to the size of the wound, and soak it in oil of roses, and place it on the wound; then take another layer of linen doubled in two or three, and soak it in wine and oil of roses, and place it on the first layer; and do this more gently than you would dare, that you do not damage the lip; and administer from above another layer of lint, and do not bind it more tightly than is necessary to hold the wound only; and leave it in place for one or two days, until the swelling subsides, then remove it, and administer medicines as follows: radix of herbs, flour of times, and incense powder, and an apothecary, and similar things; mix these things together, and apply them to the wound, and administer appropriate medicines in moderation. And keep the wound clean, do not leave it dirty, neither do you leave it to gather pus; for when pus gathers on the head of the lip, if it is pressed, it bursts, and causes great harm to the patient; for when anything biting is placed on the lip, if it is not held in place by something.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Beware then, if no other misfortune befalls the patient, as we have said, if there is any doubt or suspicion.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac; puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If black bile does not come forth violently except by the medicine that has been put on, that some part of virtue has, if you take one part of honey, and three parts of rose oil and in glue one drape, and put it on the surface; then you shall cure it in like manner as it is cured, until it is healed.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les .ij. parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont .ij. os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Then come the treatments in various ways, as long as he is sane. The veins that are never broken in the joints, or one by one, because these are bones; and when they are cartilaginous, they do not break, if not by swelling or twisting, and then they are well again.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil; et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	If one of the two parts is broken, if you can drink a little wine or vomit what you do not want, and put the break of that fracture into your index finger and in the pouch by force, until it returns to its natural position; and do this gently, and keep the patient from feeling pain by your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	If the fracture is in the upper part of the limb and cannot be brought down naturally, as is often the case, you must assume that the limb is fractured at the root of the bone like the head of a club.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues; se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	If the fracture is of two parts, if you do it again, and hasten to restore the first joint if you can; if not, after the seventh or eighth day, when the inflammation of the wound has subsided, then bathe the head of the limb where the fracture is in a linen cloth, if the fracture is in a part.
Ou tu boutes .i. autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	Or you must bite another part of it, if the fracture is there; and let the attempts be so violent that they fill the hole in the limb.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And they say no restorer should mill the tents in the burrow, and die every other day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	I do not think it is good, but it is necessary that they be milled in the making of an egg-aubun and powdered meal; then leave the tent until the bone is whole and the cartilages are hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a .i. souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	Under no circumstances should one or two goose quills be substituted for threads, and if there is much snow cover, and the wind blows, and the patient is suffering; do whatever you see fit.</start_of_turn>
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en .i. poc de dyaquilon.	If blood clots come to the surface while you are working, if you put some lint or gauze soaked in rose oil, or some alum, on it.</start_of_turn
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis; et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu; et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if abscesses do not come, if you put on a poultice of flour of lint and incense powder, confirmed with egg-aubun, then put on clean bandages, do not bind tightly; and if the break is small and it is broken into small pieces, if you have suitable instruments, then cut the wound and cure with useful things, and close with stitches if necessary; and if there is no wound in the break, then cure the tent and put on linen patches until it is healed
de la routure de la mandibule	Of the root of the mandible.
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the mandible is fractured without any wound, and there is no fracture displacement, and the fracture is not displaced too much, except for the curvature inwards, if one knows it lightly
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	It is appropriate, if the fracture is in the distal part, to bite your right index finger in the mouth of the patient; and if the fracture is in the left mandible, if you take your right index finger of the hand, and touch the fracture lightly, and hold it in place with the other hand by force, and keep it even.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en .ij., si covient que tu aministres extension de .ij. pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the fracture of the mandible is displaced in .ij., if you must administer extension of .ij. parts, as long as they are even.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus .i. drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	If movement of the jaw comes loose, or if there is displacement, if the teeth are strained by a golden or silver or silken thread, then put a broken mandible cerate on and put over it a double drape; and over the drape put a large well-made staple, or a piece of leather equal in length and width to the mandible, and tie it on the tooth that you wish, and command the patient to rest, and eat soft foods.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en .iij. semainnes.	If you see that the figure changes, if it comes loose at the jaw joint, and then reset it in its place; put on a plaster, of powdered alum with a lot of egg or rye flour, after you have set the cerate; and put on the plaster a soft linen dressing, and if the plaster comes loose, and the patient’s condition does not change, leave it as it is until it is healed; many times it heals in two weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if postmortem comes, if it is as we have said many times before.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is a fracture and wound together, repair so that no part of the bone is left unboned; if slight from the bone has been broken, cover it with appropriate instruments.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, if it has flared up as required.</start_of_turn>
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus .i. des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have boned all these fragments, and there is no more displacement, if the wound is wide, put on appropriate dressings to protect the wound, as long as it is necessary.</start_of_turn>
de la forcele	because of force.</start_of_turn
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc .iij. manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en .ij., et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.	The strong force breaks several times before, over the shoulder, and if it breaks in two ways: either it is broken and loosened in three, and there are pieces, and it is the lightest to restore; or there is a break with a wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies .ij. ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.
