And if the break is when the wound is facing downwards, have two assistants; one should hold the arm that feels the strong force; and the other should extend the limb towards the part; then set the break even, so that it forms as it should, and there is neither appearance nor movement.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you have to extend more, put under the arm of the patient a round ball of lead or linen, which should be thick as you need; and hold and steady the strong force, and hold the ball in your hand, so that you can set the break even as it should be set
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule .i. oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	If you do not manage to push back the head of the shoulder, because it comes out of its socket, you must know that the patient lies groaning on his belly, and put a cushion under the shoulder blade, that is, the middle rib, and support the shoulder from below, until the bone of the shoulder is raised.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	Then address the fracture to your side, and if you find debris, if you can, make an incision there; and pull out the pieces gently, and if the bones cannot join despite any effort, if there is a fracture at one of the incisors that you have made; but that you put a cushion under the shoulder bone to prevent infection.
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os; et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	And it seems like a spoon, neither crooked nor straight, and be as wide as it seems convenient, according to the size of the bone and the nature of the work; and has two holes, as you see, one large and one small, as is the course of the wound that you made when you treated the bones; and when you are certain of the apposition, if the wound is small, or if you doubt the apposition, if employ the wound with bandages and sutures, according to its quantity.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille .i. drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	If there is moisture in the wound, if it is oily, apply cloths soaked in rose oil and balsam, and wine, and put on top.</start_of_turn>
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier; puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant; et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint; et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors; puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	The hardening of the bone, when it is accompanied by wounds and swelling, is that you put on the bone a plaster of fine powder and egg-white, and put on soft bandages on it, and put a sponge under the armpit if you are able; then take a very large bandage of a palm of a hand width, and put on two layers of cloth on the bandages, and plaster it; then take a needle of three threads of the width of a finger and wrap it around that bandage, so that the head of the bandage is tensed; and put the needle on the fracture, and twist the bandage around the collar, and take away the armpit bandage, and take away the painful armpit; and leave the chest part alone, and when you see that the bandage holds the fracture steadily, and you see clearly that the needle does not move from the broken bone, if the fracture is mended, if the reduction is unsuccessful; and do manage the patient on his back, and put under his armpit when he sleeps a small pillow to lift up the shoulder; if it aligns the fracture by aligning the shoulder blade, or you bind the arm to the collar, and do not loosen it unless necessary for some other reason that does not arise, until XX days; then repeat the plastering, if you see that there is need for it, and strain and leave it on, until it is restored; and it is restored in about eight days, and in less time for many people.
de la brisure de l’espaule	Then resume the displacement, if you see that it is necessary, and hold and leave it in place until it is restored; and it is usually restored in about 26 days, and less in most homes.
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en xxv, Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	When the scapula is fractured or displaced, do not move it until its position has been determined; if the limb appears according to the fracture pattern and is restored to its natural position in all possible ways, then put on a powder of mill-powder with eggshells, and apply gentle pressure, and put on a double drape; then place a broad and firm splint, a little wider than the scapula itself, and if the heel of the splint is fixed in no part of the scapula, use the heel of the bandage of linen, so that the splint rests evenly; then strain the limb with a strong band firmly, so that the splint does not move from its place, and look at the mark of each joint; every time it relaxes, strain it again, and put the splint back in its place if it has moved from its position, and leave the patient lying down; the scapula will be restored in twenty days or less. And when this number is completed, if the limb is straightened out, and be joyous, for it is not bone that easily breaks.
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	And if a piece of the bone bends forward, and not a little, if it persists, and the bone, do as we said at the bursting of the forceps to calm the abscess.
de la brisure dou pis	And if a piece of the bone bends forward, and not a little, if it persists, and the bone, do as we said at the bursting of the forceps to calm the abscess.
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer.	The weight never breaks in the middle, but this often happens; but it often breaks at a headlong rush.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	When it is broken in the middle, if it declines downwards, and causes the patient great pain, and there is no marrow, and swelling, and by chance vomiting blood, and opens the marrow cavity in the broken bone, and all this is felt.</start_of_turn>
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met .i. cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des .ij. costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en .i. drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is that if the patient lies quietly on his back, and places one cushion between the scapulae, then press the scapulae, and assemble the bones of the two ribs with the hands, and slightly put each in every way that you can, until the bone is as it should be; then put on patches and bandage the area with fine salt, or other soft matter, and cover with a cloth, and bind the fracture tightly, so that it does not move; and turn the limb round on the back, and stretch it gradually, and give the patient something to drink every hour, and if it loosens, because of corrosion or swelling that comes to the limb, or pain or abscess, if you are in a hurry, and loosen it, and scrape off the patch, and address what has come from the way of treatment; then remount the patch and bind tightly until it is healed.
de la brisure des costes	Of the fracture of bones
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	Bones that fracture do not come forth except behind the loin and at the head downwards; and they do not bend forth except because they are glassy; and one feels them well at the inquiry of two fingers.</start_of_turn>
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	The restoration is when you put the fracture back in its place as it should be.</start_of_turn
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And then put on the dressing and bind it with an elastic bandage if necessary.</start_of_turn
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And if the fracture of bones is downward, if one feels great pain and swelling, just as if of blood, because the bone is pointing at the membrane; and there is swelling, and vomiting, a great quantity of blood, which is a great grief, and they have put a great burden.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And if any of those who say it should administer food that swells the belly, to push back the pangs of hunger.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We do not do this, for after these things have been eaten, they do not go away unless they have already begun.</start_of_turn>
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if they have already begun, if they are well.</start_of_turn>
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And they say that there is no need to put on stockings on the limb for its swelling, because it is similar to reason; however, there is doubt that the stocking will not collect the superfluous matter from the limb because of its weakness.</start_of_turn
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And they say that on must not cover the limb with coarse linen soaked in oil, but put on bandages between the ribs to measure an even inch of the circumference, then either cure with the cure for pleurisin, meat and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient feels great pain that he cannot bear from the bone that points towards the spleen, and there is doubt in the patient, if it is necessary to cut above the fractured bone, and if it is necessary to put in a foreign body to support the tissue; then one must drill the bone, and remove the foreign matter, and then suture the two layers of the wound, if it is large, and cure it with dressings, until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If blood spurts from a wound, put on wet cloths soaked in rose oil, and hold over the wound; and cure while the limb stops bleeding, and do not move the edge of the wound until it is healed.
de la brisure dou col	of the fracture of the collarbone.
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	Never comes a sudden break of bone from the collarbone, and often it rains; and the same with the spine.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	If this happens to anyone, and you know whether it will heal or not, take care if you see his hands softened and limp and dead, and do not move them or extend them, and when you prick them with a needle, do not feel it.</start_of_turn>
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	The veins that are deadly in many situations, if you move them and feel well when you stretch and pull them, the veins that the joint of the bone is saved, and the patient will be cured, if you put on cure.</start_of_turn
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	And if something similar comes to the spine in the back, and you see whether there is blood or not, if you take care that the piece is softened, and if the accident is what is in the hands and on the back, and on the belly the wind of a sneeze and vomiting violently; and when it has been soothed on the belly, if there is vomiting violently.
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	When it is soothed on the back and it vomits, it cannot be stopped
Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	Blood that is mortal: if it does not work in its cure
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	If this mishap does not occur, then the matter is lighter.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	If this mishap does not occur, then the matter is lighter. If there is swelling, put on a rose-hip ointment or egg yolk oil until it is calmed; then put on a comfortable and absorbent dressing, and bind it with a thread, and instruct the patient to rest; do not lie on that part where there is pain, until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If bones break, if you cover on it like this; and unite the edges of the wound, if it is large, with a splint, then bandage with lint, until it is healed; and if the head of the bone is broken, which is called the "shaft of the arm", if it is to the left of your hand, and put it equal to the other hand at your side, then put on the dressing and the bandage, if you need to; then strain it, and if there are broken bones under it, if you notice it, unite them, and cure the wound until it is healed.</start_of_turn>
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	Of the fracture of the thigh bone
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	When the thigh bone is fractured, and if so, if there is no sign of improvement at the head; and if it persists, there is a long-lasting pain, bending forward, and comes to the patient pain at the limb, swelling, and bursting of that which was fractured.</start_of_turn>
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And the restoration is that if you extend your hand over, as long as you are over the fracture; and grasp what is fractured and the figure of it; and if the fracture is only at the head, if you make it equal to the natural figure.</start_of_turn
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the fracture is long, or it bends inwards, if you make the patient sit on his belly, until the restoration of this fracture is apparent.</start_of_turn
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	And when you have set them even, if you put on the support, then put on a ball of fat or cork, and tighten the bandage, so that it does not move; and use the liquid dressing to support the costae, until the ligature is even.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	And instruct the patient to sleep on his side, or on his back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	And if the swelling comes, do not touch it, until the swelling subsides; then put on what we have said before; and then return to the restoration, and tighten it as it should be, if there is no other mishap; and that is the remedy.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	De la brisure de l’ajutoire.
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des .ij. manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren .i. fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	From the dislocation of the shoulder
Et lie as .ij. chiés .ij. liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus .i. siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	And there are two ways to reset the dislocation: one is to take a fist full of moist earth and form it into a cone-shape; then put the limb over the fist, as far up as the armpit, and hold it there with the fist under the armpit; then put the hand over the break without any weight or support from the attendants; then put the patient’s hands together, so that the break returns naturally.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a .ij. ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout .i. liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	Or the other method is to hold the patient’s arm at his collarbone, and bind the hand to his neck, and command the attendants to hold the part above the break at his hands, and the other to hold below at all the joints, and extend the chest towards the part.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	And if you see that the extraction is more forceful, if you strain the limb from the shoulder to the elbow, and from the elbow to the wrist, extend the thumbs of the assistants to their part.
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	If the shoulder blade is close to the head of the shoulder, then put one finger between the shoulder blade and the arm, and another between the shoulder blade and the chest, to hold the shoulder blade in place; and if the shoulder blade is towards the chest, put one finger lightly, with some effort, until the shoulder blade is even on both sides; then put the shoulder blade back in its place if possible, and hold it.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a .vij. jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	If after straining there are aftershocks, do not strain for more than thirteen days. Put on soft linen and rose oil until the aftershocks have subsided; then strain, and keep the position of the strain as if you put in the pad on the splinter. Then assemble the arm on the shoulder and put your hand on the shoulder or on the chest; put on the bandage and strain the shoulder and the arm, so that the arm is in its place, without any hindrance, or that the bone is not fractured.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele .i. doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure .iij. dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	And if you doubt that the bone is not moving, use splints, and on the splinter put on a splint wider and stronger than the others, and put between the splints two spaces, and let one splint be as long as the splinter extends two fingers; then strain on the splints, as I said at the beginning of this chapter about the splinter, more strongly and less loosely
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	If you see swelling of the breastbone and the ribs, as we have said, when restoring the limb from dislocation, if you are in doubt about the displacement, leave it for seven days; as we have said; then look for three days whether the swelling subsides or does not appear in the limb, or whether the swelling comes back to the limb because it is too tight.
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	If the sufferer persists, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	If no such accidents happen, if he does not vomit for at least three days or more, and the patient sleeps on his back with his hands on his stomach; put a cushion about the size of a hazelnut under the arm, and watch for an hour or so to see if the limb is stiff or relaxed. If the sufferer responds by the power of medicine, and does as we have said before, in part as we have said before; when he starts to recover, even if it is somewhat.
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	It is customary that the arm and limb must be taken down in forty days. Then one must retake the dressing and administer oil baths and ointments to the affected part to restore it properly.
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	And if the constriction is painful and embedded, if it stays for more than a day or two, it must be loosened.
de la brisure du bras	And if the fracture of the arm is displaced, leave it undisplaced for one day or two months.
Li bras est compos de .ij. os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm is composed of three bones, which are called the «flescle», because one is small and the other is large; and the small one teaches the pouch, while the large one is hollow, towards the little toe; sometimes the large bone fractures alone, or the small one, and sometimes both together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	When the small bones are fractured, restoration is slight, and healing; and when the large bone is fractured, if the healing is poor, it is more painful than when it is fractured whole.</start_of_turn>
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	If only the small bone is fractured, if the limb is slightly extended and put in its place.</start_of_turn
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	And if the large bone is fractured, if the limb must be tightly bound; and the thumb is placed above the wrist, and the little finger below the wrist, and the patient is placed crosswise over itself, with the thumb in front and the little finger behind, so that the patient does not suffer any pain; then extend the limb from the elbow to the wrist, or to the shoulder, and one assistant at the other end.</start_of_turn
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And then he sets the eye equal, following its best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if in the burst (dislocation) it breaks into pieces, if you place some support in its place, and if there is no slippage that pricks like before, you shall not be able to restore it to its place; then leave it as it is and support the bone, as we have said before.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	And if with the burst (dislocation) it breaks into pieces, as I have mentioned in the singular case; take the cure
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	And as he begins the restoration, drops of blood sometimes come out; if they are sticky I cover them with rosin made from rose oil and white wax, so that they are neither too hard nor too soft; and I cover them from above secretly, until the blood clots are calmed down.
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	And then I put on the cerate, and I put in the dressing of powder from the mill with an abundance of eggs; because I put in the stars, and let the star of the brisement be more strong, and a little wider than the others; and the thread that must be taken up must have six stars or arms in various positions: whether the brisement is in one of the bones, or in two; and it is more strained above the brisement than elsewhere, and all the days less by aligning, as I said at the beginning of this chapter; and let the drapes that are on the brisement be soft and moist, and not too hard or rough; and let the thread, which is being strained, be of linen, neither too thick nor too thin, as we have said
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And rest the limb and the tendon afterwards for some days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	And if any other bad accidents happen to the limb, as if there is swelling that happens to the limb, then you must elevate the limb with warm water, until the swelling has subsided; and leave the limb still until it has recovered.
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	And then resume the traction, and if the tendon is softened and the bone is loosened, and similar things, if necessary
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses .i. poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	If you take care that the nourishment does not come to the limb because it is too stiff, then you must soften it somewhat, and leave it for a while, until the nourishment returns, and then strain it.</start_of_turn>
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	And if none of these things that we have said happen to the patient, keep it detached for twenty days.
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	or when the wound has healed, then he can keep his hands at his collar, with his collars even, and take care of movement and spitting, and sleep on his back; and that the wound has healed in thirty days or in fifty, and sometimes in twenty days, according to the composition and the temperament of the virtues.
de la brisure de la main	Of the breaking of the hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	The nails on the back of the hand, and we have had two breaks there, often comes from fractures, and comes no more than once or twice.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin.	And when the hand is broken or fractured, if it is suspected that the bones are fractured, the patient should sit comfortably forward; then place the hand on a wide bandage, and the physician should extend the fractured bones and align them properly; and put on plaster and bandages, if necessary; and put on a splint as needed; and be covered with a sheet of linen.</start_of_turn>
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	And if the fracture is on the outside of the limb towards the belly, make a loop of cloth, and command the patient to hold it against the fractured limb; then pull from a long bandage, and be supported by a splint as large as the limb, and strain, if necessary.</start_of_turn
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if the break is outward, if you command that you place a pin above and another below at the joint, so that the hand is overextended and straight, then hold it firmly around the hand, and staunch the bleeding between the two.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en .i. tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	And if the break does not come from above or below, if it is at the elbow, if you command it to be even; and you stretch with the thumb, and if you see that you must place a pin straight, small to lift the break, and it does not move; and if the break is elsewhere, as in the index or any other, if you command it to be even, and you bind it with the two hands which are after; or you bind them all together, holding the wrist, or you place a pin upon it, as with a pouch; and take care in the restoration and arrangement of the cautery burn, and secure what comes out, as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	and if the break is outward, if you command that you place a pin above and another below at the joint, so that the hand is overextended and straight, then hold it firmly around the hand, and staunch the bleeding between the two.
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie .i. liien desus la briseure, et .i. autre desoz.	The bones of the thigh are often fractured, and it is well seen when it turns before and behind; and the restoration is when it is bound with thread beneath the fracture and above.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	The patient lies on his face, then extends his limbs equally; and it is when the fracture is in the middle of the bone
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	If the fracture is close to the root of the thigh, if one of the tendons below the bulge and the other below the fracture.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	And if it is close to the knee, then either the tendon below the knee or the tendon below the fracture; then put the thumb of the hand over the bone, so that it is in its natural position, and then put on the dressing and bind it, for it will not come loose.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	And if there is an abscess above, if you leave it quiet and return to your work and your cure; the suture is made in haste.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	It is necessary to wrap around the fracture with a bandage twice or thrice, and to drain the excess, then bend the limb until the nails reach the root of the nail; and pass a thread long between the thigh and the limb below the knee, from below the knee to above, and pass the thread over the top; then bend the limb and the thigh, and put the dressing under the fracture, and put a splint on the bone of the limb; then put under the limb and the thigh some cloth of coarse wool to even out the tension, and begin to bind from three or four places on the fracture; and the more you bind above the fracture, the less you strain; then take out two threads that you passed between the limb and the thigh, and put in three splints that are above, then return to the level of the thread at the top, until you see below the bone; and the strain, if it does not move from its place, then leave it alone, and do not bring any dressing or swelling or anything similar.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	And if there is swelling, if it comes loose, and you address that which comes, as we have said many times; and if there are pieces of bone that prick, it is necessary to remove them; and if we are unable to do so, we must cut the limb and drain the pus; and cure as we have said, until it is healed.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	And never is the bone broken in this way that it can be put into place without causing pain to the patient, as in the arm and the shoulder; however, in restoring it that is done, it does not cause any harm to the patient.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en .l. jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And sometimes the bone is restored in a day, or less or more, according to the diversity of complexions.
de la ruelle dou genoil	of the groin area.
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	Hair that in the groin has often burst, but it falls many times.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	And if it breaks, if not a mere tear, or an opening, and there is pain at every wound, and sense of pain, and this is well known.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is set right, do this: put the rounded peg back in its place until it is well assembled; then put the stuffing in, and put a round pin in if you have need of it, and hold it as it should be held; then restore all the arrangements that we have mentioned before, as for example incisions and other similar things; if you put in every mishap that it should be put in, as long as it is healthy.
de la brisure de la jambe	And if it is set right, do this: put the rounded peg back in its place until it is well assembled; then put the stuffing in, and put a round pin in if you have need of it, and hold it as it should be held; then restore all the arrangements that we have mentioned before, as for example incisions and other similar things; if you put in every mishap that it should be put in, as long as it is healthy.
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	Hair that on the leg has two bones, of which one is called the “muscle” and the other the “fossil”; and there is breaking of the whole limb as when it comes to the arm, and for this reason the restoration is made in the same way as for the arm, and the work is all the same. And if both bones are broken together, if the limb is twisted from all sides
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if a subtle bone is broken, it will twist forward.</start_of_turn>
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz.	And if the great bone is broken, if one sees great pain, and one sees it well; and it is twisted about the knee
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	When it is necessary to restore the limb, extend it fully and make it even; and bind the joints evenly. However, if the break is severe, there are more pieces, even if the extension is less severe and lighter; and adjust according to your skill.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren .ij. faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en .ij. leus .i. bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent .i. bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have completed your work, if you take.ij. strips of coarse cloth which will embrace the limb from one side to the other, and be as long as the limb from the knee to the foot; then cover with.ij. cloth.i. bandage above and below, and bind firmly in the middle, and with this binding the limb will not slip downwards or upwards, and that is good; and let no one administer any more drugs whose length is greater than the limb, and which may cause stiffness, and put on the limb a support to prevent movement, and do this cautiously at the break or in the case of an injury; and move each part of the limb, in order to see if there is any swelling or other accident; if there is swelling as much as before.
de la brisure des os dou piet	Of the fracture of bones due to violence.
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle, fracture does not arise; but in bones of violence, fracture never comes alone, and there must be two together; and there is no other cause of death but certainty and fear.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a .ij. chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	And if there is a fracture in bones of violence, and you see these bones pushing against each other, if you put the limb so sick on the earth, as if it were falling from the sky, and then put your limb on the ground, where the bones are raised, then press the limb until it returns to its place; then put on the dressing and bandage, and put some small weights on the belly of the limb, and hold the limb firmly, and as soon as the limb has healed, wrap it in bandages, and other things that you must provide.
Et quant .iij. jors ou .iiij. seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when two or three days have passed, if the limb is loose, because you will find the bones equal, whether fractured or dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a .ij. ou .iij., ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en .i. drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	If there are two fractures, restore them as we have said; then place at the fracture a splint of the length of the fracture, and make it wider; then place a bandage over that wound that I have mentioned. If there are three or more fractures, break them; then place upon each fracture a splint according to its quantity, enveloped in one layer of linen, and strain the wound over the fracture. Make it firm over the top of the fracture and over the abdomen of the fracture.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	Remember also the other things that I have mentioned concerning other fractures, as we have said; and treat each case as it should be treated.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	of the fracture of the clavicle bone
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the limb is broken and the woman sits expanded, lean her forward at the waist and support her behind; then fill the wound of the patient with cotton, and put as much in as I have; then draw out the woman, and keep her waist pressed against her back and front; and then pull out the cotton, until it reaches the entrance of the wound, and return the limb with the cotton; and when she sees blood, if she pulls the cotton, and when she has bled, she will recover; and if the fracture is restored, take a bladder of vinegar and tie a string to the belly; and pour all the vinegar into the wound; then blow in the string until the bladder is empty: the limb will then return to its normal position; then fill with cotton and leave it for several days until it is healed.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	When the bone of the arm or of the woman is broken, if you restore it just as we have said concerning the thigh bone; these breaks are not hidden from him who has put his study and his art into it, and he understands my book.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	For the break signifies in many ways the right way of restoration: therefore take heed.</start_of_turn>
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse .iij. jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	In the arm, when it is broken, take a goose beak and bind the arm; then cover with bandages, and leave for two days or until the arm is healed.
de brisure avec plaie	Of sudden with wound.
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	In the case of sudden fracture with wound, even if it is great, as with the bone of the thigh or the shoulder or the like, that it be set right now, as the symptoms which we have mentioned bear witness.</start_of_turn>
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound is well closed, if the vitriol has been retained, if you have nothing else, then repeat the restoration of the fracture in this way, or that way, for if it does not come, after these measures.</start_of_turn
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if the swelling comes, if you must leave the restoration until the swelling has gone down, as long as the swelling is appeased, and do not touch either the third or the fourth part, for you will otherwise cause a worse accident.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if a bone breaks suddenly, it appears above like a wound discovered, so you must cautiously hold it at a slight extension with your hands.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a .vij. dois ou .viij. de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne .iii. ou iiij., selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if the limb does not naturally extend with your hands held even, if the instrument of iron, which is about thirteen or fifteen inches long, and its width is according to the extent of the wound; for this reason it is necessary at the midpoint that it grasps three or four inches, according to what is necessary in the treatment of a fracture; and let it be round and somewhat thick, so that it does not pierce the limb during treatment, or be placed before, and thick in the middle forward.
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	It is called "palainche" because it must be known that the broken bone must be placed on the head of the visible bone; and once it is put back, as soon as it returns, it must be equal on one side with the other.</start_of_turn
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And if the break is slight and the instruments cannot firmly grasp the bone, if you must cover the head of the bone, as long as the instruments have possession of it.</start_of_turn
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	If you cannot restore the bone, as we have said, if you grasp with a curable instrument, such as an incision or a hook, at your peril; then withdraw that which is remaining embedded in the bone with rough raspings and fine splinters.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	And when the bone is reset, and the patient feels great pain afterwards, it is because the marrow is not in its natural place.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	If you do so much as to put it back in its place, then immediately I wrap it in black vinegar, and it is enough; do not put any cerate or other thing on the wound or oil, for it will cause decay and corruption; then administer stars [medication] when you have restored the bone, and leave the wound open, and keep the covering well around it, according to the quantity of the wound, and take care that the wound is not strained with the fracture; for many times have I seen fools do this, and have caused the patient to die or become lame or cause decay on many occasions; or the bruise has been more mild and softer than the others.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	If the wound is small or large, and you doubt that the remedy will be sufficient, as we have said, and you feel pain in the limb, if it is not possible for me to put on supports; but wrap around firmly, in place of supports, a thick cloth, and bind them.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	When you see after one or two days that the swelling has gone down at the wound, if the one you put on previously has fallen off, put on a healing bandage, as with a bandage of four herbs and similar things.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre .ij. fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And it is necessary that you bind the limb three times a day, in the morning and in the evening, until it is healed and sound.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And it is necessary that the limb be supported in a gentle way that the limb can move slightly without causing discomfort
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	If the limb persists, and cannot be reunited at its proper place, because there are small bone fragments, it is necessary that you close the wound with great care, and remove all these fragments which cause pain
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	If a fistula arises in the limb, or other sign of corruption, if it is possible to cure it, according to what is written in this chapter above
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	If the bone is fractured, and is open on the limb, as the bones of the thigh or shoulder, and other bones of the great limbs, if I do not treat it, for many people die from this; I leave it until it heals naturally; by chance it will heal by itself within twenty days or thirty, and then I will cure the wound, if you wish; or if you do not wish, I leave it as it is
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	Hair that comes out with the scab
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	Hair that comes out with the scab comes out many times after the heat of the wound, even when it is close to the joint, and is a helpful sign that the limb is recovering naturally.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Take care then that it is fresh: if you give astringents such as aloes, incense, and myrrh, and sarcocoll, acacia, and similar things, that you do not take any of these things, or all together, and mix them with a strong wine or with eggs or with oil; and put them on the wound in bandages, and strain it well, and do not remove it from the hand for days; and then remove it, and start another one, until the nodulation is bony; or you strain it on a well-made piece of leather; for the property of leather is that it will harden all the swellings under the limb; and if the nodulation has already turned into hardness just like stone, and it is necessary to harden it, if the swelling above is complete, and remove the excess; or do not remove it at all, until it is bony, and cure it until it is healed.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	Weak limb after care
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the bone is restored and the limb is weak and limp, if there is any discomfort: sometimes because it was too tightly bound and was not loosened enough; or because there are too many bands, and it cannot move smoothly; or from too many wounds; or from excessive movements, not in its proper place; or because there is too much blood in the limb, if it is weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the cure is to make the patient walk and keep the limb firm, until it is multiplied in him; and give him baths, and make him cheerful and comfortable; then put a poultice on the limb, so that the poultice attracts to great nourishment, and the wound often bleeds profusely until the nourishment comes to the limb; and bring it back to its natural shape.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	The limb is twisted after the seizure.
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai .i. emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the limb is twisted after restoration, and the bones are broken open, and the limb is deformed, though it retains its natural movement: if one does not believe the fools who say that the limb must be broken anew, and many have suffered from this in our land; this practice is blamed, and great evils result from it; often the patient dies. Though if the spasms and the torture are fresh, if you believe they have arisen from warm water, or soft herbs are cooked, like ivy leaves, root, and melilot, and similar things; and you apply an emollient plaster, like fine powdered aquaintance well made, and take the nourishment of ivy, and confit with beef fat or oil of sesame, and apply plaster on; or you take fat figs, and grind them with horse dung, and similar medicines that appease the bowels.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	And never is the bone loosened by continuous rubbing and length of time with moist hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	Or else be moved to the limb from the armpit hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the dislocation is swollen and hardened, like stone, and requires iron wire, if you cover it up to the bone, make a slight incision; and put padding and a bandage on the wound.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	And so begins the book of dislocations.
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation comes to no more, if you can now restore the limb to its proper position.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors; toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	For if it is delayed, if it swells up in the limb, and by chance if one touches it again, there will be pain at the root; for this reason it must not be moved while it is swollen: many times it brings on swelling and other pains; however, when this has happened, if you make the patient whole again, then leave it, until the swelling is gone; then raise the limb with warmth and oil, and move it gently, and cure each member as it comes to its place
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have ordered the chapters concerning dislocations of the shoulder joint to the end.
des mandibules	Des mandibules.
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc .ij. manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	The mandibles. For the mandibles are loosened and the dislocation of both is as follows: either they are a little loose from their sockets, and softened somewhat; or they are loosened entirely, and hang towards the chin, and cause the saliva to flow from the mouth that it cannot hold it back, cannot close its mouth, and engulfs its tongue with the words.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is small, if it returns by itself in several positions.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie; et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	And if it is entire and companioned, if you must move it urgently, and do not be afraid; and in such a manner that the attendants hold the patient’s head down, and keep their eyes away from his pocket of one of his hands at the root of the dislocation of the jaw in the mouth, if the dislocation is two parts; and the other two must be freed, to make them equal; and command the patient to soften his jaw, his teeth, and move them all over
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And behold the eye that is beside the pocket, until it returns to its place.</start_of_turn>
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les .ij. mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if it is grasped, even if both mandibles are together, if they arose from hot oil, as long as they remain lightly; do not force me to restore it, as we have said.</start_of_turn>
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens; et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules; et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	When they are returned equally, and the patient’s mouth is well closed, gently tighten the lips; then place a cloth moistened in oil of roses and beeswax on the wound, and bind it lightly with linen. Let the patient rest on their back, and keep the arms still between two cushions, so that they do not move forward or backward, or strain, but take a light diet, as long as the pain persists, and keep the jawbone still. Then gently move the tongue, and do not open the mouth too wide while swallowing or drinking, until the jawbone is well healed and healthy.
Et se les .ij. mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	If the teeth do not return to their place at a single hour, and are not otherwise converted, fever and nausea will ensue, and sometimes vomiting of pure bile.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en .viiij. jors.	When you see this, know that it is a loss; and often death follows in eight days.</start_of_turn>
de la forcelle	of the forceps.</start_of_turn>
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	The forceps cannot grasp deep within without causing displacement, and is worth nothing when removing it, and it is often felt.</start_of_turn
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint; et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez; et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	When the patient lies down on their back and extends their arms, then press the limb towards the chest; it will return. Then place a bandage on the wound and bind it; the limb which is beside the ribcage cannot be moved. If this does not happen, and if it becomes loosened once, if the dislocation has returned to its place as we have said; then place the bandage and the dressing on again, and bind it, and command the patient to rest until they are healed; and in this way the dislocation of the shoulder will be returned when it has recovered from its place.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	Of the dislocation of the shoulder.
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc; et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	Hair that has grown on the shoulder is not loosened except in three ways: firstly, it is loosened at the shoulder joint; secondly, at the elbow; and sometimes at the upper arm. Do not loosen it at the back of the shoulder or at the armpits; and loosen it often from the shoulder downwards, especially in those who have much hair, for in these people it causes great pain; in those who have little hair, loosen it only at the points where it is painful and then return to the points of pain.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And sometimes there are percussion or fractures, and the shoulder is inflamed by a thick abscess, and care must be taken that it is not dislocated by this.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	It is necessary that you be certain that it is actually dislocated; and once you are sure, then you may begin treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste; et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens; et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier; et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	It is known as dislocation when it is driven towards the shoulder, and it makes a difference between the diseased shoulder and the healthy one, and you will find between their diversity their displacement; and at the head of the shoulder there is a pit, and from the armpit to the head of the shoulder, just as if there were a nail there; and the patient cannot move their hand back to its place, neither can they make any movement. And if it is displaced upwards, if it is not hidden, for you will see it immediately; and this manner of dislocation is not sufficient to bring back, when it is new, or when the limb is painful.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	And the way is to take hold of the painful limb with the hand above, then put your thumbs under the armpit, and take hold of the joint forcefully upwards; and then the hand must be held and stretched upwards, because it must be set in place.</start_of_turn>
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree; puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide; et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere: et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar; et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	If it does not come as we have said before, if you must, instruct the patient to bathe in warm water; and give them a soft and soothing nourishment, such as decoction of elderberry, fenugreek and melilot in water, or give it directly; then or so, support the patient on their back, put on a cushion under the heel of the affected limb, not too soft nor too hard, then put the thumb of the hand on the cushion, and keep the chief of the shoulder firmly in place, and treat the hand of the patient; and another attendant holds the chief of the patient's arm, so that it does not move downwards; the shoulder will return immediately, and if you see that it remains according to this manner: that you make present someone who is greater than the patient; and be two towards the cost of the limb, and support the shoulder from the heel of the patient's limb, and keep the heel up, so that the patient hangs forward; and another attendant treats the hand of the patient downwards towards the belly.
