Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	And if the patient is too weak to bear any weight, if he can manage without anything heavy, the dislocation will return immediately.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile; puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment; et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	And so we must also do in another way: if the bone is left long and tense in the earth, from which the head of the bone has become round like a ball, and is neither too thick nor too thin; then put on the patient’s hand some soft cloth, but that it cover the wound, and that the patient’s hand be firm and long; then extend the hand forward with the other hand and the joint will return to its place without harm; and if it does not return with all these things that we have said, do this remedy: take two thumbs of two hands and three fingers wide, which have the head bent inwards to enter the bottom of the wound, according to this shape:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus .i. eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	Then lay on the head of the sufferer a drape of cloth, so that it does not touch the patient, and put on his seat the patient; and extend your arms over the patient's head, and hold the sufferer's limb on the patient's arm, and the arm at the wrist, and put the arm on his elbow of a span wide, and stretch out the hands backwards, or leave the forearm hanging down: the joint is now restored.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is restored, in whatever way, if you put on his seat a ball of wool as big as an egg, put on the plaster bandage of powder of wheat, with incense and balm of egg, on the whole shoulder and around, then strain off the seat immediately, and turn the limb on the bandage, and embrace the hand at its collar, and keep the hands still.</start_of_turn>
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés .v. jors ou .vij., et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	And it is to be known that it must be massaged often, as long as the limb is comfortable, for it will heal more quickly; and then massage more after five or six days, and move it; and if it is stiff and is not softened, if it is healed.</start_of_turn>
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint is forced out of place by moisture or for some other reason, if you can, administer cautery three times over; as is done before or alongside cautery.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés .vij. jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	And if you do all this, and it does not heal within twenty-three days, and the joint does not stay in place, and cannot lift the arm up, then know that the nerves at the head of the shoulder are compressed or stretched or softened; and that the joint never heals in its place.</start_of_turn>
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The dislocation that is towards the elbow, and the bones, or behind, if it is made by impulse and extension of the arms, and if another bandage is administered; and it cures as long as it is healthy.</start_of_turn
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	If after healing the limb grieves and becomes stiff, if the patient uses the limb many times, until the grief is relieved and returns to its former state.
de la dislocation dou coute	If after healing the limb grieves and becomes stiff, if the patient uses the limb many times, until the grief is relieved and returns to its former state.
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	If after healing the limb grieves and becomes stiff, if the patient uses the limb many times, until the grief is relieved and returns to its former state.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	And when you join the painful limb with the sound limb, if you see it clearly visible.</start_of_turn>
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	For the joint is dislocated, and cannot bend the arm, touch its shoulder at all.</start_of_turn
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	And you must ensure that it is reset immediately and firmly, so that if you postpone it, if it comes back again, you will cause more harm than good; and even if it is at the rear, it is better to leave it than to risk bringing it back in its entirety, even if it is delayed. For it is more painful and dangerous than other dislocations, and often leads to death.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes .ij. mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And if it is possible to restore it, when it is in such a way that you can bring it back, extend your hand with both hands; and let your arms be spread out, and your hands down following the curve of the joint, from front to back, and hold the joint together with your thumbs and index fingers, until it returns to its place
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocation is in front, if it returns when you double your hand over your hand, and hold from the root of the bone that is loosened.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large; et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne; et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	And if it does not return to its place, administer strong extension; and if two ministers extend the arm and hold it, so that it does not move during extension; then turn the arm from the shoulder, and having enveloped a long and wide bandage; and when you have looked at the joint with its hand, if there is any oil on the joint to soften it, then join the joint firmly, until it returns; and when it is in its place, put on dry plaster with egg white, and tighten forms, and bend the arm at the shoulder of the patient, and leave it there for some days, then take it off.</start_of_turn>
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	If the joint is firmly fixed in its place, if you loosen the limb and leave it; if you see that the joint does not move smoothly, repeat the displacement and loosening of the limb, and leave it thus for some days, until it is firmly set; then loosen it.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain; et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	If he feels pain after the joint has been reset, and it moves, bathe and massage thoroughly, pressing until it is eased; or place upon the joint a poultice of mutton fat, then leave it for a day and a night, then the bone, and let it enter or bathe; and when it sweats, wipe the joint gently, then put the poultice back, and enter or bathe; do this two or three times until it is healed. If you see that it persists, put upon it a poultice of soaked horse manure warmed with butter, and strain it out; if it returns to its place.
li dislocation de la main	The dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	The dislocation of the hand. The joint of the hand is loosened, more so than any other joint, and it must be immediately repositioned in its place, even if it is swollen or there is pus.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu; adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	If you place the affected hand on a table and extend the patient, look at the hand to see if it is straight, so that he places his palm on the appearance of the joint and stretches it until it returns whole, it is necessary that you observe if it is well positioned; then place the patient’s hand behind his back on a table extending and contracting.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	And if the dislocation is at the back of the hand, let the patient place the back of his hand on the table, and I will look and put his hand on the appearance of the joint.
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	If it comes back now, it is well. If not, if the strain of calming substances has passed away, leave it in its natural position to resume its course
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte; et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	And if he cannot bear it, and you do not put it back in place after some days, it will harden the joint. And do not cause any pain to the patient except that which arises from cutting the nerves or arteries. If there is no other remedy except to drain it out, do so with the cautery. In this case, nothing else is worth it.</start_of_turn>
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse .v. jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	When the hand is at rest, if you put on the bandage which we mentioned earlier, then strain and leave it for three days, then remove it and leave it be.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it does not move well and there is no pain, if the swelling is of warm water, and you rub it until it is healed
de la dislocation des dois de la main	of the dislocation of the shoulder of the hand.
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre; adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins; et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor; et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut; et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez; et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	Never is the thumb desoiled at the wrist, never at the palm or belly; then is the thumb stretched, and the dislocation is fixed in the pockets until it returns, then sustain the head of the thumb, and turn it towards the part where it is joined; and leave it there for two days, and then put it back as it was before; and do not move it, as we have said, and pull out the hair, and make it move, and bind it up; do this often, until it is well healed, and do the same if it is desoiled at the belly of the thumb, and do as you have done before, until it is healed; and do the same if it is desoiled from another part.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	From the loosening of the shoulder joint at the back.
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the shoulder or neck joint is loosened, or there are several such loosenings, if no cure is found, for the patient’s death is imminent.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars; celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»: li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance: si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	And the sign that it will not hold is when the urine spurts backwards; do not hold it, and often become limp in no limb, or the two thighs or two arms or one. And often the spleen is moved to three parts; that which is moved behind is called "gilbosite": it is cured if it is known that the "gilbosite" has come from infancy: if there is no cure or healing for the whole thing.

And that which comes from sitting or from blows or from similar things, they say that the ancient methods of treatment were great words, but I have abridged them according to my intention, and I have formed instruments in various ways.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit; et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis; et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece; puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles; et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons; et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	I say that in the swelling which comes before the pain, there is no healing; and the same with that which comes straight from the two coasts; and one cannot cure the fire except that which comes from behind, as I have said; and that the patient be extended over his face in one equal inch, and have strain from the bones that it does not swell; then put a cushion at the head of the bed and another at the feet, and tie a bandage around the belly of the patient, and another at the waist, and two ministers know the bands, one at the head and the other at the feet, among the two cushions; and be well closed, the cushion as we have said, and the patient puts his palms on the spine until it returns.

If it does not return by this treatment, take a spoonful of three cubits in length, and chew the thumb from the heel; let the patient sit on the side, and hold the head of the thumb from the heel, then put the middle of the thumb on the spine; and put the thumbs of the other hand on the other head of the thumb, and press firmly, until it returns to its place; and if you see that it is not returning, do it at the turning point that turns at the hand.
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc; et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent; et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet; et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	If two thumbs are put at the head of the patient’s arm of great length, and two fingers on the other side, and between each thumb there are sowers and nails, a palm of spice in length; and there is in each thumb one hole, or the nail is crooked, and the thumbs are firmly fixed in the earth, so that they do not move; and between two thumbs there is one thumb turning, so that when the bone turns, the thread turns with it, and there are two small thumbs of a palm’s length in the turns; and then you must bind the thread which is between the buttocks to the turning at the head, and the other thread to the pieces at the other turning, and the minister must turn his thumbs all around the thread, and the master puts the spine even as we have said.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant; et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations; et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption: par aventure feroit venir la mort.	When it is even, put on a dry dressing with abundance of eggs, and then press, and then support with a tablet of three inches in length, so that it embraces the belly of the rib cage and the sensitive part of the spine, then bind with a thread as we have said, and use the patient of gentle nourishment until he is well; and if nothing comes to an end of the well-being, if it is necessary, administer soothing and calming medicines, as we have said before; and never give a piece of lead, and never let it appear from behind the shoulder blade, because it is dislocation; and it is the bone that breaks, for which we must have no presumption: by chance comes death.
des dislocations de la hainche	Dislocations of the shoulder
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc .iiij. parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	Dislocations of the shoulder are only caused by dislocations of the shoulder and elbow joints; they do not occur with other joints. The dislocation of the shoulder is impaired in three parts: front and back, and above and below; the greater the displacement in front and back, the greater the impairment.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu; et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	And the knowledge of its dislocation is that when the limb is joined with the flesh, if it is longer, and the patient groans more than before, and cannot bend the limb double at the fire; and it is the bone that is often broken in this inflammation of the appendix, for which reason the head of the shoulder comes loose
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of the one who comes to the rescue, if it is that this accident is contrary to those mentioned above.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	And the sign of the one who comes to the rescue, if it is that his limb is well according to completion; however, do not double the knee joint in pain, and if you see him forced to do so, if he cannot do so before, and retains his urine, and swells the ankle, and when he walks, it passes over the heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the sign of the one who comes to the rescue, if it is that he cannot extend his knee, cannot double it, and that this limb is shorter than the other, and the ankle is softened, and the shoulder is dislocated at the root of the ribs.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	The repeated displacement of this semblance of dislocation must be treated, for if it is an ancient dislocation and remains as before, it endures according to its setting; and there is no cure; and I do not know that there is any presumption.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des .iiij. manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	If the dislocation is recent and there are three ways of dislocation, if you are hasty and turn the joint, stretch it inwards and outwards, and move it to the right and left; by chance, if it returns, there is no need for any other cure.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil; et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien; et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	If it does not return in this manner, if you must, appear with a strong minister, and with two hands on the limb, or one which is to be bound upon the knee; and another minister extends his hand downwards as far as he can, while he holds his hands above his buttocks; and another grasps the wrist of the limb; and extend both upwards and downwards at once, until the patient is lifted from the earth at once, and remains suspended.
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as .iiij. semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This method of extension is often used as in three similar cases, and if the dislocation has returned, as we have said, it is well.</start_of_turn>
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele; puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	If this is not the case, if you must, give cure to its appearance. When dislocation is complete, if you can, support the patient over his costal cartilage, and place the limb on the root of the buttock, and the limb which is below the ankle, then extend the limb upwards towards the ankle and downwards towards the heel; then grasp another minister by the arms and embrace the great limb of the painful side, and extend it outwards: if it returns to its place now; and this method of dislocation is more gentle than the others.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres; puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc; puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	If you do not force it to stay in this manner as we have said, if you know that you must bind the two feet of the patient together with a strong thread above the two toes and above the two knees, and that the limb of the patient should be extended two fingers more than the others; then let it hang suspended from the head of a pole, or on the ground two arms long; and command one minister to grasp the head of the pelvis, and let another minister hold the pelvis, because the joint is now stable.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi; puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme; et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	When the dislocation has been driven out, if the patient is conscious, as we have said in the one with swelling, grasp the limb firmly at the knee and the foot; then put on two cushions, one at the head and one at the foot; and pierce one cushion between the buttocks of the patient, shaping it like this; and plant moist cloths around it, so that it does not hurt the patient, and extend the cushions of the ministers towards him, and the master puts his hand equally on the dislocation.
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	If it comes back, it is well.
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	If not, put on the table as we have said in the previous instruction, and press on it with our hands as we have said, and keep the patient lying on the edge of the table.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	When the dislocation is forward, if you must, extend the limb strongly, as I have said; and put the thumbs on the painful area of the limb, then press with the other hand, and extend backwards towards the groin.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches; et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table; et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve; et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	If the dislocation has gone out again, if it does not manage to extend the limb downwards, do not lift it up from the ground, but keep it at the same level as when it was dislocated at the outset. As we have said previously, press on the joint at the table; and when the patient extends his leg, and they are even; then join the thighs together, put on the dressing, and bind with a bandage, so that the limb does not move; leave it for three days or four, then remove the bandage and put on the dressing again. If you see that they are even, if the bandage is still in place, as before, leave it for three days; then remove the bandage and let the patient rest comfortably, until the limb is comfortable.
de la dislocation dou genoil	of dislocation of the shoulder

Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois; puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors; et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	When it comes to the boil [a wound caused by intense heat], if the dressing is placed and the strain is made, and the limb is bound to the leg, and the nerves above the ankle are kept taut, so that the ligature is not too tight; then leave it for two or three days. If the ligature relaxes during this time, retie it. Otherwise, remove the dressing after three-quarters or four-fifths of a day and inform the patient of the danger in three days.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If he persists thus, if you must restrain him, as we have mentioned elsewhere, until he is well.
des dois	then.
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When the bones are dislocated, if you can extend the limb well, it is a light thing.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne; et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez. de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	This excerpt describes various medical procedures, including cautery for hair removal, treatment of dislocations and bleeding, and setting of dislocated shoulders.
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert: si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis; et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit; et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne; et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis; et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples; et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	When a wound accompanies a dislocation, and it is seen to be restored, many times the patient dies: if you are not very presumptuous in the cure, and if you are not skilled in the art and have not used it for a long time, and if you are not compassionate and merciful and timely, do not be bold; and at first use soothing things about the wound, and leave the patient in the hand of God, if you do not see hope of health; and when you see hope, if you remember to reset the limb, even if the wound remains; and when the limb is reset, if you administer soothing things about the wound, and cure the wound, as it should be, from dried pus; and if with the dislocation there is a fracture, and bones are broken, if the bones are fractured, do as we have said in simple diseases; and beware of going into a state of fear, as I have said, for this is unprofitable according to your Creator, and for the preservation of your arm and body.
